Inferring Tawali from the Hadith of Wudu Once Each
Deriving tawali from prophetic action and statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the ruling of tawali (continuity) in wudu from the hadith of Ibn Umar and identify the Hanafi usul principle regarding inference from a prophetic action.

Core Idea
A prophetic action combined with an exclusive condition can prove obligation, but only if the inference is linguistically and contextually sound.

This passage examines the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, in which the Prophet performed wudu once each and stated that Allah only accepts prayer performed with such wudu. The author uses this to argue for the necessity of tawali (continuity) in wudu. As a Hanafi usul text, the lesson is not about the fiqh ruling per se, but about how to correctly derive a ruling from a prophetic statement and action—a key skill in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary hadith and its chain
Locate the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar. Note the discussion of its chain: Abd al-Haqq praises it, Ibn Abi Hatim criticizes a narrator, al-Bayhaqi declares it weak. In usul, chain evaluation affects the level of certainty (thubut).
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so it cannot establish a fard obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the Prophet's action and statement
The Prophet performed wudu 'once each' and said 'this is the wudu of one whose prayer Allah does not accept except with it.' The action demonstrates continuity, and the statement links acceptance of prayer to that specific manner. The Hanafi usul rule: an action alone does not convey obligation unless it is accompanied by a command or explicit indication.
The author argues that if the Prophet did not perform tawali, the hadith would not prove continuity, but since he did, it does.
3
Apply the inference for tawali
The author uses a logical necessity: if the Prophet performed the acts with continuity (tawali), and he said prayer is only accepted with this wudu, then tawali is required. The key question: is the requirement due to the action itself or the statement? In Hanafi usul, a general statement like 'except with it' includes all elements of the described act, including continuity.
This inference is subject to counterarguments: perhaps continuity was incidental, not intended as a condition.
4
Evaluate the strength of the inference
Consider alternative interpretations: the hadith might refer to the general validity of wudu, not specifically tawali. Also, the chain weakness reduces certainty. In Hanafi usul, a weak hadith can still be used for istihsan or targhib but not for fard. Therefore, tawali becomes a recommended (mandub) rather than obligatory element.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that zanni evidence cannot establish wujub (obligation) without supporting qat'i evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمسيب بن الواضح عن عبد الله بن عمر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم توضأ مرةً مرة، وقال: هذا وضوء مَن لا يَقبلُ الله منه الصلاة إلا به». الحديث. قال عبد الحق: هذا من أحسن طرق هذا الحديث، وقال ابن أبي حاتم: المسيب: صدوق، لكنه يخطئ كثيراً ، وقال البيهقي : رُوي من أوجه كلها ضعيفة. - وجه الاستدلال به أنه لا يخلو أن يكون والى في هذا، أو لا، لا جائز أنه لم يوال، وإلا لزم عدم صحته متوالياً، فثبت أنه والى، ويلزم أن لا يصح إلا متوالياً؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا به». وما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لا يقبل الله صلاة امرئ حتى يضع الطهور مواضعه فيغسل وجهه، ثم يديه الحديث، و: «ثم»: للعطف والترتيب. وهذا الحديث قال مخرجو أحاديث الرافعي: لم نجده في شيء مما رأينا من كتب الحديث، وإنما جاء في رواية لأبي داود عن رفاعة بن رافع أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لا تتم صلاةٌ لأحد حتى يُسبغ الوضوء كما أمره الله تعالى، فيغسل وجهه ويديه إلى المرفقين، ويمسح برأسه، ويغسل رجليه إلى الكعبين، ثم يكبر». الحديث. و ما روى النسائي والدارقطني أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال عند السعي: «إن الصفا والمروة من شعائر الله ، فابدؤوا بما بدأ الله به». والعبرة لعموم اللفظ وما تقدم من حكاية فعله صلى الله عليه وسلم الذي كان يواظب عليه ، وقوله : هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا به، وتقدم وجه الاستدلال. وما أخرجه ابن ماجه من طريق كثير بن زيد عن ربيح بن عبد الرحمن بن أبي سعيد عن أبيه عن أبي سعيد الخدري أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه». وأخرج عن رباح بن عبد الرحمن بن أبي سفيان أنه جدته زيد تَذكر أنها سمعت أباها سعيد بن زيد يقول : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا صلاة لمن لا وضوء له، ولا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه».
Al-Musayyib ibn al-Wadih from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed wudu once each, and said: 'This is the wudu of one whose prayer Allah does not accept except with it.' The hadith. Abd al-Haqq said: This is one of the best chains of this hadith. Ibn Abi Hatim said: Al-Musayyib is truthful but makes many mistakes. Al-Bayhaqi said: It is narrated through weak chains. The aspect of inference from it is that either he performed it with continuity or not. It is impossible that he did not perform it with continuity, otherwise its correctness as continuous would be invalid. Thus it is established that he performed it with continuity, and it follows that it is not valid except with continuity, because he (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah does not accept prayer except with it.' Also narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah does not accept the prayer of a person until he places purification in its places, washing his face, then his hands, the hadith, and 'thumma' indicates conjunction and order. The compilers of al-Rafi'i's ahadith said: We did not find it in any of the hadith books we saw, but it is narrated by Abu Dawood from Rifa'a ibn Rafi' that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The prayer is not complete for anyone until he performs wudu completely as Allah commanded, washing his face and hands to the elbows, wiping his head, and washing his feet to the ankles, then says the takbir.' And al-Nasa'i and al-Daraqutni narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said at al-Sa'i: 'Indeed, al-Safa and al-Marwa are from the symbols of Allah, so begin with what Allah began with.' The lesson is from the generality of the wording and what preceded of his action (peace be upon him) which he persisted upon, and his saying: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.' Ibn Majah narrated from the chain of Kathir ibn Zayd from Rubeh ibn Abd al-Rahman from his father from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it.' Also narrated from Rabah ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Sufyan that his grandmother Zayd mentioned that she heard her father Sa'id ibn Zayd say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no prayer for one who has no wudu, and no wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it.'
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of hadith evidence for two wudu rulings: the obligation of tawali (continuity) and the recommendation or obligation of tasmiya (mentioning Allah's name). The author presents multiple hadith. First, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet (PBUH) performed wudu once each, and said this is the wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer. The author discusses the chain's reliability, noting that some scholars consider it weak. The author then provides the inference: the Prophet must have performed the acts with continuity (tawali), otherwise the hadith would not indicate it. Therefore, tawali is necessary. Next, a hadith with 'thumma' (then) indicates order. Another hadith from Rifa'a uses the word 'thumma' before 'takbir', showing arrangement. The author notes that this hadith is not widely found. Then the hadith about beginning with what Allah began at Safa and Marwa is used as a principle for order. The passage concludes with the hadith suggesting that tasmiya is required (or recommended) for wudu. Two narrations are given: one from Ibn Majah with a chain including Kathir ibn Zayd, and another from Rabah. The author uses these to establish the ruling. The commentary follows the author's order: first the proof for tawali, then for tasmiya, both based on textual evidence.

Key Terms
التوالى (al-tawali): Continuity between wudu acts without significant pause
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): Legal inference from textual evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis in this lesson, what is the ruling for tawali (continuity) in wudu derived from the hadith of Ibn Umar?
A) Fard (obligatory) because the Prophet said 'except with it'.
B) Mustahab (recommended) because the chain is weak and the inference is not definitive.
C) Makruh (disliked) because it leads to rigidity.
D) Mubah (permissible) because no ruling is derived.

Key Takeaway
The derivation of tawali from the hadith of Ibn Umar demonstrates that in Hanafi usul, chain reliability and linguistic precision determine whether a practice is fard or mustahab.

Inferring Tasmiya from Hadith 'No Wudu for One Who Does Not Mention Allah's Name'
Deriving tasmiya from hadith with negation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the hadith on tasmiya and apply the Hanafi usul principle that a generic negative phrase (nafi) can indicate recommendation not obligation when the chain is weak.

Core Idea
A hadith that negates the validity of an act without a condition does not necessarily make that condition obligatory; it may merely indicate lack of perfection.

The second part of the passage addresses tasmiya (mentioning Bismillah) before wudu. The hadith 'La wudu li man lam yadhkur ism Allah alayh' is presented. The author includes two chains: one via Ibn Majah and another via Rabah. In Hanafi usul, such a hadith, despite its apparent commanding tone, is interpreted as a recommendation because the chain is not fully authentic and the negation can be understood as negation of completeness (nafy al-kamal) rather than negation of validity (nafy al-sihha).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations for tasmiya
The passage gives two hadith: one from Ibn Majah via Kathir ibn Zayd from Rubeh from his father from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, and another from Rabah via his grandmother from Sa'id ibn Zayd. Note that the narrators include individuals like Kathir ibn Zayd whose reliability may be discussed in hadith criticism.
These are ahad narrations, thus zanni al-thubut.
2
Analyze the linguistic structure: 'La wudu ...'
The phrase 'لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه' uses nafi (la) to negate wudu for someone who does not perform tasmiya. In Arabic nafi can indicate either absolute nullity (nafy al-sihha) or negation of perfection (nafy al-kamal). Hanafi usul prefers the latter when the chain is weak, as a strong claim like nullity requires strong evidence.
Also consider the similar phrase 'لا صلاة لمن لا وضوء له' which is interpreted as negation of perfection?
3
Apply the Hanafi principle for ambiguous negation
The principle: عند عدم القرينة - عدم صحة - لا يثبت إلا الأفضلية. Without supporting evidence, the negation is understood as a lack of complete reward, not invalidity. Coupled with weak chains, the ruling becomes istihbab (recommendation).
This is consistent with the Hanafi maxim: al-asi fi al-ashya' al-ibaha, and obligations require definitive proof.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab perspective
Imam Ahmad and some Shafi'is consider tasmiya wajib based on this hadith, interpreting 'la wudu' as negation of validity. Hanafis, however, argue that such a strong ruling cannot be established by ahad hadith with questioned narrators.
The difference illustrates how usul principles about the burden of proof affect fiqh outcomes.

Source Text

Al-Musayyib ibn al-Wadih from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed wudu once each, and said: 'This is the wudu of one whose prayer Allah does not accept except with it.' The commentary follows the author's order: first the proof for tawali, then for tasmiya, both based on textual evidence.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiya): Mentioning the name of Allah (Bismillah) before wudu
نفي الصحة (nafy al-sihha): Negation of validity—the act is void if condition missing
نفي الكمال (nafy al-kamal): Negation of perfection—the act is valid but incomplete

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis in this lesson, what is the ruling for tasmiya (mentioning Bismillah) at the start of wudu?
A) Wajib (obligatory) because the hadith says 'no wudu'.
B) Mustahab (recommended) because the chain is weak and the negation can be interpreted as lack of perfection.
C) Sunnah mu'akkada (emphasized sunnah) because the Prophet always did it.
D) Mubah (permissible) because there is no evidence for it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on tasmiya illustrates that a hadith's apparent commanding tone can be softened by chain weakness and linguistic analysis, leading to a ruling of mustahab rather than fard.

Hadith of 'Usaylah: Proof for Tahlil Marriage Condition
Compilation of hadith proofs for the ruling of tahlil marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key phrase in the hadith of 'usaylah, explain its evidentiary value for the condition of consummation, and apply it to derive the ruling of tahlil marriage.

Core Idea
One hadith, multiple chains: 'taste the 'usaylah' consummation is a non-negotiable condition.

This lesson presents a foundational textual proof (dalīl naqlī) from the Sunnah that is central to the Hanafi ruling on tahlīl marriage. Through multiple authentic narrations, the hadith of 'usaylah repeatedly conditions the return of a triply divorced woman to her first husband upon actual physical intimacy with a second husband. As a primary source for istidlāl, this hadith demonstrates how a clear prophetic statement settles a legal condition and how the Hanafi school treats such explicit texts as definitive in both transmission and meaning.

Guided Path
1
Locate the operative phrase
Scan the various narrations and identify the recurring expression that conveys the legal condition. Notice the phrase 'taste the 'usaylah' appears in every version.
The phrase is a metaphor but legally unambiguous.
2
Classify the hadith's transmission
Observe that the hadith is reported by multiple companions (ʿĀʾishah, Ibn ʿUmar, etc.) and recorded in major collections (Bukhārī, Muslim, etc.). Determine its status as mutawātir maʿnawī or āḥād.
Hanafīs consider it qaṭʿī al-thubūt due to widespread transmission.
3
Analyze the linguistic indication (wajh al-dalālah)
The Prophet (ﷺ) uses the conditional particle 'ḥattā' (until) to link the permissibility to the action of tasting. In uṣūl al-fiqh, a condition expressed in an imperative or conditional clause indicates that the ruling is dependent on its fulfillment.
The metaphor 'usaylah' is universally understood to refer to sexual intercourse.
4
Derive the ruling
From the explicit text, conclude that mere marriage contract without consummation is insufficient. The word 'taste' implies actual physical contact, not just seclusion (khalwah).
This ruling is unique to the Hanafī school in its emphasis on actual intercourse; other schools may consider seclusion sufficient under certain conditions.
5
Confirm the authority level
Recognize that this hadith belongs to Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah (the core transmitted texts) and is relied upon by the early Hanafī masters. It cannot be overridden by istiḥsān.
The ḥadīth is cited as primary evidence in the chapter of ṭalāq and nikāḥ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسلم : لا، حتى تذوقي من عُسَيْلته، ويذوق هو من عُسَيْلتك» (۱).
(۱) حديث العُسَيْلة : وله طرق وألفاظ، منها : عن عائشة رضي الله عنها: «أن رجلاً طلق امرأته ثلاثاً، فتزوجها رجل، ثم طلقها، فسئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك ، فقال : لا ، حتى يذوق الآخرُ من عُسَيلتها ما ذاق الأول». وفي رواية قالت: «طلق رجل زوجته، فتزوجت زوجاً غيره، فطلقها، وكان معه مثل الهدبة، فلم تَصِل منه إلى شيء تريده، فلم يلبث أن طلقها، فأتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: يا رسول الله ! إن زوجي طلقني، وإني تزوجت زوجاً غيره، فدخل بي، فلم يكن معه إلا مثل هذه الهدبة، فلم يقربني إلا هبةً واحدةً لم يصل منه إليَّ شيء، فأحِلَّ لزوجي الأول؟ فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا تحلّين لزوجك الأول حتى يذوق الآخرُ عُسَيلتك، وتذوقي عُسَيلته». وفي أخرى قالت: جاءت امرأةُ رفاعة القُرَظي إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت: كنتُ عند رفاعة القرظي، فأبَتْ طلاقي، فتزوجت عبد الرحمن بن الزبير، وإنما معه مثل هدبة الثوب فقال : أتريدين أن ترجعي إلى رفاعة؟ لا، حتى تذوقي عسيلته، ويذوق عسيلتك».
زاد في رواية: «وأبو بكر جالس عنده، وخالد بن سعيد بن العاص بالباب ينتظر أن يُؤذَن له فقال : يا أبا بكر ألا تسمع إلى هذه وما تجهر به عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم؟!».
وفي أخرى: «ألا تزجرُ هذه عما تجهر به عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم؟! وما يزيد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على التبسم».
وفيه: «وما معه إلا مثل هذه الهدبة، لهُدْبَةٍ أخذَتْها من جلبابها».
وفي أخرى: «أن رفاعة طلقها آخر ثلاث تطليقات»، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم. وأخرج النسائي وأبو داود الرواية الأولى، وأخرج الترمذي والنسائي الرواية الثانية إلى قوله: «ويذوق عسيلتك، وأخرج أيضاً النسائي الثالثة بتمامها، ومثله ابن ماجه وأحمد.
=
وأخرج مالك في الموطأ عن الزبير بن عبد الرحمن بن الزبير «أن رفاعة بن سَمَوالِ طلَّق امرأته تميمة بنت وهب في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاثاً، فنكحت عبد الرحمن بن الزبير فاعترض عنها، فلم يستطع أن يمسها، ففارقها، فأراد رفاعة أن ينكحها وهو زوجها الأولُ الذي كان طلقها، فذكر ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنهاه عن تزويجها وقال : لا تحل لك حتى تذوق العسيلة».
وعن ابن عمر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سئل عن الرجل يطلق امرأته ثلاثاً، فيتزوجها الرجل، فيُغلق الباب، ويُرخي الستر ، ثم يطلقها قبل أن يدخل بها؟ قال: لا تحل للأول حتى يجامعها الآخر».
وفي رواية : عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الرجل تكون له المرأة، فيطلقها، ثم يتزوجها رجل آخر، فيطلقها قبل أن يدخل بها، فترجع إلى زوجها الأول؟ قال: لا، حتى يذوق العسيلة». أخرجه النسائي.
وأخرجه الطبراني بلفظ : أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: المطلقة ثلاثاً لا تَحِلَّ لزوجها الأول حتى تنكح زوجاً غيره، ويخالطها، ويذوق عسيلتها». ورواه أبو يعلى بمثل حديث عائشة.
وعن عبيد الله والفضل بن العباس أن العُميصاء - أو : الرميصاء - جاءت تشكو زوجها إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت إنه لا يصل إليها، قال: فقال: كذبت يا رسول الله، إني لأفعل، ولكنها تريد أن ترجع إلى زوجها الأول، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا تحل له حتى يذوق عسيلتها». رواه أبو يعلى، ورجاله رجال الصحيح.
وعن عبد الرحمن بن الزبير أن رفاعة بن سَمَوالِ طلق امرأته، فأتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : يا رسول الله ! قد تزوجني عبد الرحمن وما معه إلا مثل هذه، وأومأت إلى هدبة من ثوبها فجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يُعرض عن كلامها، ثم قال: أتريدين أن ترجعي إلى رفاعة؟ لا حتى تذوقي عسيلته، ويذوق عسيلتك». رواه البزار والطبراني، ورجاله ثقات.
And he said, peace be upon him: No, until you taste from his 'usaylah and he tastes from your 'usaylah. (1) The hadith of 'usaylah: it has multiple chains and wordings, among them: from 'A'ishah, may Allah be pleased with her: that a man divorced his wife three times, then another man married her, then divorced her, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about that and said: No, until the other tastes from her 'usaylah what the first tasted. In another narration: she said: A man divorced his wife, then she married another husband, and he divorced her, and he had something like the fringe of a garment and did not achieve what she wanted... and the Prophet said: You are not lawful for your first husband until the other tastes your 'usaylah and you taste his 'usaylah. In another: the wife of Rifa'ah al-Qurazi came to the Prophet and said... and the Prophet said: Do you want to return to Rifa'ah? No, until you taste his 'usaylah and he tastes your 'usaylah. Added in a narration: And Abu Bakr was sitting with him, and Khalid ibn Sa'id ibn al-'As was at the door waiting... In another: 'Do you not forbid this woman from speaking loudly in the presence of the Messenger of Allah?'... In it: 'And he has nothing but like this fringe, a fringe she took from her cloak.' In another: 'that Rifa'ah divorced her the final three divorces', narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. And al-Nasa'i and Abu Dawud narrated the first narration, al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i narrated the second up to his words 'and he tastes your 'usaylah', and al-Nasa'i also narrated the third in full, and similarly Ibn Majah and Ahmad. And Malik narrated in al-Muwatta' from al-Zubayr ibn 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr that Rifa'ah ibn Samwal divorced his wife Tamimah bint Wahb three times in the time of the Prophet, so she married 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr, but he turned away from her and could not touch her, so he separated from her, then Rifa'ah wanted to marry her again, and he mentioned that to the Prophet, who forbade him from marrying her and said: She is not lawful for you until you taste the 'usaylah. And from Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet was asked about a man who divorces his wife three times, then another man marries her, closes the door, lowers the curtain, then divorces her before entering? He said: She is not lawful for the first until the other has intercourse with her. In another narration: from the Prophet concerning a man who has a wife, divorces her, then another man marries her and divorces her before entering, so she returns to her first husband? He said: No, until he tastes the 'usaylah. Narrated by al-Nasa'i. And al-Tabarani narrated it with the wording: The Messenger of Allah said: The woman divorced three times is not lawful for her first husband until she marries another husband, and he mixes with her, and he tastes her 'usaylah. And Abu Ya'la narrated it similar to the hadith of 'A'ishah. And from 'Ubayd Allah and al-Fadl ibn al-'Abbas that al-'Umayṣā' - or al-Rumayṣā' - came complaining of her husband to the Prophet and said that he does not reach her, and he (the husband) said: She lies, O Messenger of Allah, I do, but she wants to return to her first husband, so the Prophet said: She is not lawful for him until he tastes her 'usaylah. Narrated by Abu Ya'la, and its narrators are those of the Sahih. And from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr that Rifa'ah ibn Samwal divorced his wife, and she came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, 'Abd al-Rahman married me and he has nothing like this, and she pointed to a fringe of her garment, so the Prophet turned away from her speech, then said: Do you want to return to Rifa'ah? No, until you taste his 'usaylah and he tastes your 'usaylah. Narrated by al-Bazzar and al-Tabarani, and its narrators are trustworthy.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of multiple narrations of the famous hadith of 'usaylah (عسيلة), which serves as a primary textual proof (dalil naqli) for the Hanafi ruling on the condition of tahlil marriage. The hadith establishes that a woman who has been divorced three times (al-mubtâtah) is not lawful for her first husband until she marries another man and he actually consummates the marriage—symbolized by the term 'usaylah (a metaphor for the sweetness of intimacy). The various chains and wordings reinforce the requirement of actual sexual intercourse (dukhul haqiqi), not merely a marriage contract. Hanafi usul scholars use this hadith to derive the ruling that the tahlil marriage must involve full physical consummation; mere seclusion or incomplete contact is insufficient. The multiple narrations from different companions (A'ishah, Ibn Umar, etc.) and the authentication by major hadith scholars give this proof high authority (mutawatir ma'nawi in some views). In Istidlal, this hadith is cited to support the necessity of 'ibahah (permissibility) contingent upon actual intimacy, a rule that is further elaborated in the chapter on talaq and nikah. The passage also highlights the proper method of adab in the presence of the Prophet (avoiding explicit speech), but the core legal principle remains the condition of consummation.

Key Terms
العسيلة (al-'usaylah): A diminutive form of عسل (honey), used in the hadith as a metaphor for the sweetness of sexual intercourse.
المطلقة ثلاثاً (al-mutallaqah thalathan): A woman divorced three times (al-ba'in baynunah kubra), who is not lawful to her husband until she marries another and he consummates the marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of 'usaylah, what must occur for a woman divorced three times to be lawful for her first husband?
A) She must marry another man and have a valid marriage contract.
B) She must marry another man and consummate the marriage with him.
C) She must marry another man and then divorce him before consummation.
D) She must wait for a waiting period after the third divorce.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of 'usaylah is a definitive proof that actual consummation is a necessary condition for a triply divorced woman to return to her first husband.

Analyzing the Shafi'i Proof for Condition of Dukhul in Tahleel
Presentation of Shafi'i hadith-based proof for dukhul condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key hadiths cited as Shafi'i proof for the condition of dukhul in tahleel and apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding ziyada in a mashhur report to evaluate the opposing argument.

Core Idea
The Shafi'i school proves the condition of intercourse in tahleel through multiple hadiths and consensus; the Hanafi response reinterprets the curse hadith without invalidating the marriage.

In this passage from al-Bazdawi's usul, the author presents the Shafi'i argument that actual intercourse (dukhul) is a necessary condition for a woman divorced three times to become lawful for her first husband. The Shafi'is cite several hadith narrations, all emphasizing that she is not halal until the second husband 'tastes the honey.' The text then engages with the Hanafi position, arguing that the condition is established by an addition (ziyada) in a well-known report and by consensus. Your task is to trace the proof chain, identify the Hadith sources, and understand how the Shafi'i school derives this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Hadith
Find the hadith that forms the main proof: 'She is not lawful until she tastes the honey.' This hadith is narrated in multiple versions. Identify the central message and its legal implication.
The term 'ʿasīla' is a metaphor for intercourse.
2
Examine the Supporting Narrations
The text cites additional hadiths from Ibn Umar, Ubaydullah, and others. Note how each narration reinforces the condition of actual intercourse, rejecting mere formalities like closing the door.
Pay attention to variations in wording; they all converge on the same ruling.
3
Analyze the Ziyada Argument
The Shafi'i author argues that the condition of dukhul is an addition (ziyada) in a well-known (mashhur) report, and such an addition is acceptable in Hanafi usul. Understand the principle: a trusted narrator's addition is accepted unless it contradicts a stronger source.
This is a key usul principle: ziyadat al-thiqa maqbula.
4
Consider the Consensus Claim
The text claims that the condition of dukhul is established by consensus (ijma'). Identify the basis for this claim and evaluate its strength.
Consensus among the Companions or early scholars is a strong proof.
5
Contrast with the Hanafi Position
The passage addresses the Hanafi school ('antum'), which is said to invalidate the description of tahleel while accepting the original condition of dukhul. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: the dispute is over the validity of a marriage with the intention of tahleel.
The Hanafis require dukhul but do not invalidate a marriage contracted with the intention of tahleel.

Source Text

وأخرج مالك في الموطأ عن الزبير بن عبد الرحمن بن الزبير «أن رفاعة بن سَمَوالِ طلَّق امرأته تميمة بنت وهب في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلاثاً، فنكحت عبد الرحمن بن الزبير فاعترض عنها، فلم يستطع أن يمسها، ففارقها، فأراد رفاعة أن ينكحها وهو زوجها الأولُ الذي كان طلقها، فذكر ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنهاه عن تزويجها وقال : لا تحل لك حتى تذوق العسيلة». وعن ابن عمر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سئل عن الرجل يطلق امرأته ثلاثاً، فيتزوجها الرجل، فيُغلق الباب، ويُرخي الستر ، ثم يطلقها قبل أن يدخل بها؟ قال: لا تحل للأول حتى يجامعها الآخر». وفي رواية : عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الرجل تكون له المرأة، فيطلقها، ثم يتزوجها رجل آخر، فيطلقها قبل أن يدخل بها، فترجع إلى زوجها الأول؟ قال: لا، حتى يذوق العسيلة». أخرجه النسائي. وأخرجه الطبراني بلفظ : أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: المطلقة ثلاثاً لا تَحِلَّ لزوجها الأول حتى تنكح زوجاً غيره، ويخالطها، ويذوق عسيلتها». ورواه أبو يعلى بمثل حديث عائشة. وعن عبيد الله والفضل بن العباس أن العُميصاء - أو : الرميصاء - جاءت تشكو زوجها إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت إنه لا يصل إليها، قال: فقال: كذبت يا رسول الله، إني لأفعل، ولكنها تريد أن ترجع إلى زوجها الأول، فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا تحل له حتى يذوق عسيلتها». رواه أبو يعلى، ورجاله رجال الصحيح. وعن عبد الرحمن بن الزبير أن رفاعة بن سَمَوالِ طلق امرأته، فأتت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : يا رسول الله ! قد تزوجني عبد الرحمن وما معه إلا مثل هذه، وأومأت إلى هدبة من ثوبها فجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يُعرض عن كلامها، ثم قال: أتريدين أن ترجعي إلى رفاعة؟ لا حتى تذوقي عسيلته، ويذوق عسيلتك». رواه البزار والطبراني، ورجاله ثقات. وفي ذكر العود، دون الانتهاء : إشارة إلى التحليل. وفي حديث آخر: لعن الله المُحلَّلَ والمُحَلَّلَ له»(۱): فثبت الدخول زيادة بخبر مشهور يحتمل الزيادة بمثله، وما ثبت الدخول بدليله إلا بصفة التحليل. وقد ثبت شرط الدخول به ،بالإجماع، ومن صفته التحليل، وأنتم أبطلتم هذا الوصف عن دليله عملاً بما هو هذا الحكم، أعني الدخول بأصله ووصفه جميعاً. ومن ذلك قوله تعالى : الطَّلَقُ مَرَّتَانِ ... الآية، البقرة /٢٢٩
And Malik narrated in al-Muwatta from al-Zubayr ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr that Rifa'a ibn Samwal divorced his wife Tamima bint Wahb three times during the time of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, so she married Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr, but he refrained from her, and could not touch her, so he separated from her, and Rifa'a wanted to marry her, and he was her first husband who had divorced her, so that was mentioned to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and he forbade him from marrying her and said: 'She is not lawful for you until she tastes the honey.' And from Ibn Umar that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about a man who divorces his wife three times, then a man marries her, closes the door, and draws the curtain, then divorces her before entering upon her? He said: 'She is not lawful for the first until the other has intercourse with her.' And in a narration: from the Prophet, peace be upon him, regarding a man who has a wife, divorces her, then another man marries her, then divorces her before entering upon her, and she returns to her first husband? He said: 'No, until he tastes the honey.' Al-Nasa'i recorded it. And al-Tabarani recorded it with the wording: 'The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: The woman divorced three times is not lawful for her first husband until she marries another husband, and he mixes with her, and tastes her honey.' And Abu Ya'la narrated it like the hadith of Aisha. And from Ubaydullah and al-Fadl ibn al-Abbas that al-Umayṣa' - or al-Rumayṣa' - came complaining about her husband to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, and said that he does not have intercourse with her. He said: 'He lied, O Messenger of God, I do, but she wants to return to her first husband.' So the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'She is not lawful for him until he tastes her honey.' Abu Ya'la narrated it, and its narrators are the narrators of Sahih. And from Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Zubayr that Rifa'a ibn Samwal divorced his wife, so she came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said: 'O Messenger of God! Abd al-Rahman married me and he has nothing like this,' and she gestured to a fringe of her garment, so the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, turned away from her speech, then said: 'Do you want to return to Rifa'a? No, until you taste his honey and he tastes your honey.' Al-Bazzar and al-Tabarani narrated it, and its narrators are trustworthy. And the mention of return, without cessation, indicates tahleel. And in another hadith: 'May God curse the muhallil and the muhallal lahu.' So the condition of intercourse is established by an addition in a well-known report that permits addition similar to it, and intercourse is not established by its evidence except with the description of tahleel. And the condition of intercourse has been established by consensus, and from its description is tahleel, and you have invalidated this description from its evidence, acting on what is this ruling, that is, intercourse in its origin and description all together. And from that is His saying, Most High: 'Divorce is twice...' the verse, al-Baqarah 2:229.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents the Shafi'i proof for the condition of actual intercourse (dukhul) in the second marriage for a woman divorced three times to become lawful for her first husband (tahleel). The author cites multiple hadith narrations all reinforcing the same ruling: the woman does not become halal until 'tastes the honey' (i.e., experiences intercourse with the second husband). The hadiths consistently repeat the condition, emphasizing rejection of mere formalities like closing the door or drawing the curtain. The passage then highlights that the mention of 'return' (al-awd) without termination indicates the concept of tahleel. It also cites the hadith cursing the muhallil and muhallal lahu, which condemns marriages explicitly intended for making the woman lawful, thus distinguishing between genuine marriage and mere formality. The text then argues that the condition of intercourse is established by an addition (ziyada) in a well-known report that permits such an addition, and that the condition is also established by consensus (ijma'). The opponent (addressed as 'antum') is accused of invalidating the description of tahleel from its evidence, while accepting the original ruling of intercourse. The passage ends by referring to the Quranic verse on divorce twice, indicating that the three-time divorce requires a proper intervening marriage.

Key Terms
مُحلِّل (muhallil): A man who marries a woman divorced three times with the intention of making her lawful for her first husband by consummating and then divorcing her.
عسيلة (ʿasīla): A metaphor for intercourse; literally 'honey,' used in hadith to denote the pleasure of marital relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the hadiths cited, what must occur for a woman divorced three times to become lawful for her first husband?
A) She must marry another man and simply have a marriage contract.
B) She must marry another man and have actual intercourse with him.
C) She must marry another man, close the door, and draw the curtain.
D) She must marry another man and both must taste honey symbolically.

Key Takeaway
The Shafi'i school derives the condition of intercourse in tahleel from multiple hadiths and consensus, while the Hanafi school accepts the condition but disagrees on the effect of explicit intention.

Deriving the Ruling on Tahlil from Hadith: Consummation Required
Derives ruling on tahlil from hadith and refutes opponents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling that consummation is required in tahlil by applying the usul principle that explicit descriptions in hadith indicate conditions.

Core Idea
The hadith's condition of 'tasting sweetness' makes consummation a wajib component of valid tahlil.

This passage shows how Hanafi usul al-fiqh derives rulings from hadith. The author cites multiple narrations on tahlil, each emphasizing the necessity of actual intercourse. You will learn how the explicit description in the hadith is treated as a conditional requirement, and how the Hanafi school refutes opposing views that consider the contract alone sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hadith Text and Its Key Phrase
Locate the operative words: 'hatta yadhuqa' (until he tastes) and the curse on the muhallil. These are the focus of the derivation.
The hadith of Anas and the curse hadith are both cited.
2
Classify the Textual Category
The phrase 'la, hatta yadhuqa' is an explicit condition (shart) in the form of a negative response followed by a condition. In Hanafi usul, such explicit descriptions indicate a binding requirement.
This is mantuq (explicit) and is treated as a condition (shart).
3
Apply the Hanafi Usul Principle
The principle that a description indicating a condition (wasf al-shart) makes that condition necessary. Additionally, the curse on the muhallil indicates that the act without consummation is forbidden.
The curse strengthens the binding nature.
4
Derive the Ruling
Therefore, tahlil is invalid without intercourse; the woman does not become halal for the first husband. This ruling is derived directly from the hadith.
This is the Hanafi position.
5
Refute the Opposing Argument
Opponents who argue that the marriage contract alone suffices are refuted by the explicit hadith. The Hanafi response is that the hadith's wording is clear and cannot be overridden by analogy or general principles.
The author calls out the opponents as having annulled the description from its proof.

Source Text

وفي ذكر العود، دون الانتهاء : إشارة إلى التحليل. وفي حديث آخر: لعن الله المُحلَّلَ والمُحَلَّلَ له»(۱): فثبت الدخول زيادة بخبر مشهور يحتمل الزيادة بمثله، وما ثبت الدخول بدليله إلا بصفة التحليل. وقد ثبت شرط الدخول به ،بالإجماع، ومن صفته التحليل، وأنتم أبطلتم هذا الوصف عن دليله عملاً بما هو هذا الحكم، أعني الدخول بأصله ووصفه جميعاً. [ساکت؟]، وهو نص الكتاب عن وعن أنس أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سئل عن رجل كانت تحته امرأة، فطلقها ثلاثاً، فتزوجها بعده ،رجل، فطلقها قبل أن يدخل بها، أتحل لزوجها الأول؟ فقال: لا، حتى يذوق الآخرُ ما ذاق من عسيلتها وذاقت من عسيلته». رواه أحمد والبزار وأبو يعلى، وقد تتبعتُ ألفاظ هذا الحديث جُهدي فلم أقف على قوله: «تعودي»، والله أعلم. (۱) حديث: «لعن الله المحلل»: عن عُقبة بن عامر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ألا أخبركم بالتّيس المستعار؟ قالوا: بلى يا رسول الله قال: هو المُحِلِّ ، لعن الله المُحِلَّ والمحلل له ، رواه ابن ماجه، ورجاله ثقات. وعن عبد الله بن مسعود قال: لعن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المُحِلَّ والمحلل له. رواه أحمد والنسائي والترمذي وصححه وللخمسة إلا النسائي من حديث علي مثله.
And in mentioning the return, without the completion: an indication of analysis (tahlil). And in another hadith: 'May Allah curse the one who makes permissible and the one for whom it is made permissible.' Thus entry (dakhul) is established as an addition by a well-known report that is capable of being added to. Entry is not established by its proof except with the description of tahlil. The condition of entry has been established by consensus, and its description is tahlil. And you have annulled this description from its proof, acting upon what is this ruling, meaning entry in its essence and description together. [...] And from Anas that the Messenger of Allah was asked about a man who had a wife, divorced her three times, then another man married her and divorced her before entering upon her - is she permissible for her first husband? He said: 'No, until the other tastes what she tastes from his sweetness and she tastes from his sweetness.' Narrated by Ahmad, al-Bazzar, and Abu Ya'la. I have traced the wordings of this hadith with my effort and did not find his saying 'ta'udi', and Allah knows best. (1) Hadith: 'Allah curse the muhallil': from Uqba ibn Amir said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Shall I inform you of the borrowed he-goat?' They said: Yes, O Messenger of Allah. He said: 'He is the muhill; may Allah curse the muhill and the one for whom tahlil is done.' Narrated by Ibn Majah, and his narrators are trustworthy. And from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'The Messenger of Allah cursed the muhill and the one for whom tahlil is done.' Narrated by Ahmad, al-Nasa'i, and al-Tirmidhi and authenticated it. And the five except al-Nasa'i have a similar hadith from Ali.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and proof from hadith on the topic of tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman permissible for her first husband by marrying and then divorcing her). The author first notes that mentioning return without completion indicates tahlil. Then he presents the hadith: 'May Allah curse the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done.' This establishes that actual entry (intercourse) is required; the description of tahlil is the act itself. The condition of entry is established by consensus. The author refutes opponents who nullify this description. The hadith of Anas is cited: the Prophet said the second husband must taste her sweetness, confirming consummation is necessary. Additional hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Uqba ibn Amir reinforce the ruling. The author notes he could not find the word 'ta'udi' in the hadith. These narrations firmly establish that tahlil requires actual intercourse, not just a marriage contract.

Key Terms
المُحَلَّل (al-muhallal): A man who marries a thrice-divorced woman intending to make her permissible for her first husband, and then divorces her.
التحليل (al-tahlil): The act of making permissible, specifically through marriage and consummation followed by divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must marry with the intention of tahlil
B) He must consummate the marriage
C) He must divorce immediately
D) He must be a relative

Key Takeaway
The explicit condition in the hadith of Anas makes consummation a necessary condition for valid tahlil; without it, the woman does not become halal for her first husband.

Command After Prohibition: Hanafi Rule of Obligation
Establishing that command after prohibition indicates obligation, not recommendation or permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a command after prohibition indicates obligation and apply it to distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A command after prohibition indicates obligation unless evidence shows otherwise.

This lesson introduces a key usul principle: when a command follows a prior prohibition on the same act, the Hanafi school holds that the command is for obligation (wujub) by default. This is based on the original meaning of the command form and its usage. Other scholars argue that such commands indicate permission (ibaha) or recommendation (nadb), citing the Quranic verse about hunting after ihram. We will examine the evidence and see how the Hanafi school defends its position by distinguishing the source of permission from the form of the command.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
Read the first sentence: 'the command after prohibition does not relate to recommendation and permission inevitably, but rather it is for obligation according to us, unless there is evidence.' This is the core Hanafi rule.
The rule applies to any command that comes after a prohibition on the same act.
2
Identify the Quranic example
The opponents cite the verse: 'And when you have completed [the rituals], then hunt' (al-Ma'idah 5:2), which is a command after the prohibition of hunting during ihram. They claim this shows permission.
The Hanafi response does not deny the permissibility of hunting after ihram, but argues that the permission comes from a different verse.
3
Understand the opponent's claim
Some scholars (like al-Shafi'i) hold that a command after prohibition indicates ibaha (permission) or nadb (recommendation), not obligation. They use the hunting verse as evidence.
The text says 'some of them said it is for recommendation and permission'.
4
See the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the permissibility of hunting after ihram is established by another verse: 'Permitted for you are good things...' (al-Ma'idah 5:4), not by the form of the command 'then hunt'.
Thus, the example does not contradict the principle that the command form itself indicates obligation.
5
Note the extension to al-mujib
The last sentence mentions a difference regarding 'the obligator' (al-mujib). This refers to debates about whether obligation can only come from Allah or also from other authorities, but the text does not elaborate further.
This is a separate discussion often linked to the attributes of Allah (sifat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتصل بهذا الأصل: أن الأمر بعد الحظر لا يتعلق بالندب ،والإباحة لا محالة بل هو للإيجاب عندنا، إلا بدليل؛ استدلالاً بأصله وصيغته.
ومنهم من قال بالندب والإباحة ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا حَلَلْتُمْ فَأَصْطَادُوا ﴾ المائدة / ٢ .
ولكن ذلك عندنا بقوله تعالى: ﴿أُحِلَّ لَكُمُ الطَّيِّبَتُ وَمَا عَلَّمْتُم مِّنَ الْجَوَارِحِ مُكَلِّبِينَ﴾ المائدة/ ٤ ، لا بصيغته.
ومن هذا الأصل: الاختلاف في الموجب :
And connected to this principle: that the command after prohibition does not relate to recommendation and permission inevitably, but rather it is for obligation according to us, unless there is evidence; deriving from its origin and form. And some of them said it is for recommendation and permission, due to His saying: 'And when you have completed [the rituals], then hunt' [al-Ma'idah 2]. But that according to us is [permitted] by His saying: 'Permitted for you are good things and what you have taught of hunting animals' [al-Ma'idah 4], not by its form. And from this principle is the difference regarding the obligator (al-mūjib).
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage introduces an important usul principle: when a command appears after a prior prohibition (e.g., 'Do not hunt while in ihram,' then 'When you are halal, hunt'), the command is for obligation (wujub) according to the Hanafi school, unless there is a specific evidence indicating otherwise. The reasoning is based on the original meaning of command (as established in the previous lesson) and its form (sighah). Some opponents argue that such a command indicates recommendation or permission, citing the verse 'When you have completed the rituals, then hunt' (al-Ma'idah 2). The Hanafi response is that the permissibility of hunting after ihram is actually derived from another verse (al-Ma'idah 4) which explicitly permits hunting in general, not from the form of the command itself. Thus, the example does not disprove the principle. The last sentence alludes to further differences regarding the 'obligator' (the one who issues the command), possibly a reference to debates about the attributes of Allah (sifāt) or about whether obligation can come from other than Allah.

Key Terms
الأمر بعد الحظر (al-amr ba'd al-hazr): A command given after a prior prohibition on the same act, e.g., 'When you are halal, hunt' after the prohibition of hunting in ihram.
الموجب (al-mūjib): The obligator; in usul, it refers to the one whose command creates obligation (e.g., Allah, or a qualified authority).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, what does a command given after a prohibition (amr ba'd al-hazr) indicate by default?
A) Recommendation (nadb).
B) Permissibility (ibaha).
C) Obligation (wujub).
D) It is ambiguous (waqf).

Key Takeaway
A command after prohibition indicates obligation (wujub) by default in Hanafi usul, with the burden of proof on those who claim otherwise.

The Foundations of Iman in the Hanafi School
Defining Iman and quoting hadith on its pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the three foundations of Iman as per the hadith of Anas ibn Malik, and explain the Hanafi view that actions are not part of the essence of Iman but are its necessary effects.

Core Idea
Iman rests on three eternal pillars: tawhid, non-excommunication, perpetual jihad, and belief in qadar.

This lesson unpacks a key hadith used by Hanafi scholars to define the foundations of Iman. Understanding these principles helps distinguish the Hanafi position that Iman is primarily inner belief, while actions are its fruits — a view that shapes rulings on takfir and the status of sinful Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its sources
Locate the hadith in the passage. It is attributed to Anas ibn Malik and narrated by Abu Dawud and others. Note the author's remark on the chain (Yazid ibn Abi Nushbah being unknown). This affects the hadith's authority in Usul.
The hadith is a hadith ahad, not mutawatir, but considered sound enough for foundational principles.
2
Extract the three foundations
The hadith lists three 'asl' (foundations): 1) Tawhid (la ilaha illa Allah), 2) Not excommunicating a believer for a sin and not expelling from Islam for an action, 3) Jihad continues until the end, and 4) Belief in predestination. Note that the third foundation combines jihad and qadar.
The numbering is ambiguous; some scholars count them as three broad principles with sub-elements.
3
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation of each foundation
For each principle, explain the Hanafi view: Tawhid is the core of Iman; non-excommunication means that a Muslim who commits a sin is still a believer (see Murji'a influence); jihad is fard kifaya and not invalidated by unjust rulers; belief in qadar affirms divine decree without negating human responsibility.
This hadith is used to support the Hanafi stance that Iman does not increase or decrease with deeds.
4
Connect to Usul al-Fiqh: How this hadith is used as a proof
In Usul, this hadith provides a textual basis (dalil) for defining Iman. Its wujh al-dalalah (indication) is that it explicitly lists the components. Scholars debate whether actions are part of Iman or not. The Hanafi school uses this hadith to argue that actions are not part of the essence (asl) but are required.
The hadith says 'do not expel him from Islam for an action' — implying action alone does not negate Iman.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school holds that Iman includes both belief and action. They interpret this hadith as warning against excommunication for a sin, but still consider major sins as potentially weakening Iman. The Hanafi response: actions are fruits, not constituents.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences in rulings on apostasy, intercession, and the status of grave sinners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان: الكف عمن قائماً، وعن جابر بن سمرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا يزال هذا الدين تقاتل عليه عصابة من المسلمين حتى تقوم الساعة». أخرجه البخاري. قلت: وفي الباب عن أنس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «ثلاث من أصل قال : لا إله إلا الله، ولا تُكفّره بذنب، ولا تُخرجه من الإسلام بعمل والجهاد ماض منذ بعثني الله إلى أن يقاتل آخرُ أمتي الدجال، لا يُبطله جَوْر جائر، ولا عدل عادل والإيمان بالأقدار. رواه أبو داود ، وحكاه أحمد في رواية ابنه عبد الله ، وفي سنده يزيد بن أبي نُشبة، قال المنذري في معنى المجهول، وقال عبد الحق هو رجل من بني سليم لم يرو عنه إلا جعفر بن برقان.
The meaning of Iman: refraining from those who stand? And from Jabir ibn Samurah from the Prophet (SAW): 'A group of Muslims will not cease to fight for this religion until the Hour is established.' Narrated by Bukhari. I said: In this chapter from Anas that the Prophet said: 'Three from the foundation: he said: There is no god but Allah, and do not declare him a disbeliever for a sin, and do not expel him from Islam for an action, and jihad is ongoing from when Allah sent me until the last of my ummah fights the Dajjal; it is not invalidated by the injustice of an unjust ruler nor the justice of a just ruler, and faith in predestination.' Narrated by Abu Dawud, and Ahmad related it in the narration of his son Abdullah, and in its chain is Yazid ibn Abi Nushbah; al-Mundhiri said he is unknown, and Abd al-Haqq said he is a man from Banu Sulaym from whom only Ja'far ibn Burqan narrated.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage appears to be from a section defining Iman (faith). The text begins with a definition 'al-Iman: al-kaf...' which is garbled in OCR. It then presents two hadith: one from Jabir ibn Samurah about a group fighting for religion until the Hour, and one from Anas ibn Malik listing three foundations: tawhid, not excommunicating for sin, not expelling from Islam for action, the perpetuity of jihad (not invalidated by any ruler), and faith in predestination. The author comments on the chain of the second hadith, noting Yazid ibn Abi Nushbah is unknown. This passage is likely meant to be memorized as a concise definition of Iman and its core principles.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-imān): Faith in Islam, which includes verbal confession, deeds (including jihad), and belief in predestination, as per this hadith.
الجهاد (al-jihād): Struggling in the path of Allah, which continues until the last group fights the Dajjal; not invalidated by rulers' justice or injustice.
أصل (aṣl): Foundation or fundamental principle; here the three things from which other aspects of faith derive.
الكف (al-kaf): Refraining; here possibly 'الكف عن' meaning 'refraining from' [something] – the OCR is unclear but likely part of a definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Iman is founded on tawhid, non-excommunication for sin, perpetual jihad, and belief in qadar; actions do not remove it.

The Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute on Specifying Intention (Ta'yin al-Niyyah) in Fasting
Dispute on necessity of specifying intention in fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on ta'yin al-niyyah in fasting, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the analogy to prayer and the concept of time determining the act.

Core Idea
A general intention suffices when the act is uniquely determined by time—specification is not independently required.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i on whether the intention (niyyah) for fasting must specify the type (ta'yin) or a general intention will do. The debate hinges on the nature of the act—its indivisibility, the role of resolve (azimah), and the analogy to prayer. Understanding this dispute illuminates how usul principles generate concrete fiqh differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Is specification (ta'yin) of the type of fast required in the intention, and can intention be made before dawn or later?
The dispute centers on whether the time automatically specifies the act.
2
Trace the Shafi'i proof
Specification is a condition by consensus; the fast is indivisible; resolve is needed at the start.
Shafi'i argues that the first part of the fast requires specification, else the whole is corrupt.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The act is unified by time, so general intention suffices; resolve is dropped due to incapacity; analogy to prayer.
Hanafi: constancy of resolve is dropped by consensus, just as in prayer.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Valid vs invalid fasting in specific scenarios: general intention at night for qada', intention after midday for nafl.
Hanafis permit general intention; Shafi'is require explicit specification.
5
Assess the tarjih
Al-Bazdawi favors the Hanafi position based on the qiyas to prayer and the specifying power of time.
The text concludes with the Hanafi view as the preferred one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوقتي ؛ لعدم كونه مشروعاً، لا باستحقاق منافعه، كما ينعدم في الليل أصلاً، ولا استحقاق ثمةَ ، فإذا بقيت المنافع له : لم يكن بد من التعيين ولم يوجد ؛ لأن عدم العزيمة ليس بشيءٍ، بخلاف هبة النصاب؛ لأنه عبادة تصلح مجازاً الصدقة ؛ استحسانا . عن وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لما كانت منافعه بقيت على ملكه وجب التعيين حتى يصير مختاراً، لا مجبوراً ، ولو وضعنا عنه تعيين الجهة : لصار مجبوراً في صفة العبادة، ولخلا معنى العبادة عن الإقبال والعزيمة. وقلنا الأمر على ما قلت إلا أنه لما اتحد المشروع في هذا الوقت: تعين في زمانه، فأصيب بمطلق الاسم ، ولم يُفقد بالخطأ في الوصف، كالمتعين في مكانه فصار جوازه بهذه النية على أنه تعيين، لا على أن التعيين عنه موضوع، فكان هذا منا قولاً بموجب العلة. و وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لما وجب التعيين شرطاً بالإجماع: وجب من أوله ؛ لأن أول أجزائه فعل مفتقر إلى العزيمة، فإذا تراخى بطل، فإذا اعترضت العزيمة من بعد: لم تُؤثر في الماضي بوجه؛ لأن إخلاص العبد فيما قد عمله لا يتحقق، وإنما هو لما لم يعمله بعد، فإذا فسد ذلك الجزء: فسد الباقي ؛ لأنه لا يتجزأ، ووجب ترجيح جانب الفساد ؛ احتياطاً. وهذا بخلاف التقديم ؛ لأن التقديم واقع على جملة الإمساك، ولم يعترض عليه ما يُبطله فبقي وأما المعترض فلا يحتمل التقديم. ألا يُرى أن النية بعد نصف النهار : لا تصح. وألا يُرى أن في الصوم الدين وجب الفصل بين هذين الوجهين. وقلنا نحن إن الحاجة إلى النية؛ لأن الإمساك قُربةً، وهذا يصير الإمساك واحدٌ غير متجزئ صحةً وفساداً، والثبات على العزيمة حالَ الأداء ساقط بالإجماع؛ للعجز، وحالَ الشروع في الأداء ابتداء ساقط بالإجماع أيضاً؛ للعجز ، وصار حال الابتداء ها هنا: نظير حال البقاء في الصلاة، وحالُ البقاء : نظير حال الابتداء في الصلاة. = ثم هذا العجز أطلق التقديم مع الفصل عن ركن العبادة، وجعل موجوداً تقديراً، فصار له فضل الاستيعاب، ونقصان حقيقة الوجود عند الأداء على حد الإخلاص، والعجز الداعي إلى التأخير موجود في الجملة في جنس) من يقيم بعد الصبح، أو يفيق عن إغمائه. وفي يوم الفرض حرامٌ ، ونيةُ النفل عندك لغو، فقد جاءت الضرورة، فلأن يثبت بها التأخير مع الوصل بالركن أولى ، ولهذا رجحان في الوجود عند الفعل وهو حد حقيقة الأصل، ونقصان القصور عن الجملة بقليل: يحتمل الشك ضرورة لازمة؛ لأن تقديم النية من الليل عن صوم كا العفو، فاستويا في طريق الرخصة، بل هذا أرجح. وهذا الوجه يوجب الكفارة بالفطر فيه، وروي ذلك عنهما، ولما صح الاقتصار على البعض للضرورة وجب المصير إلى ما له حكم الكل من الكل من كل وجه، وهو أن يُشترط الوجود في الأكثر ؛ لأن خَلَفاً وجه الأقل في مقابلة الأكثر : في حكم العدم، ولا ضرورة في ترك هذا الكل الثابت تقديراً، فلم نجوزه بعد الزوال، ورجحنا الكثير على القليل؛ لأنه (۱) وفي نسخ: حق»، والمعنى واحد سائد
... [the temporary fast] because it is not legislated, not by entitlement to its benefits, just as it is nonexistent at night originally, and there is no entitlement there. So if the benefits remain for him, then specification is necessary and it did not exist, because the absence of resolve is nothing, unlike the gift of the nisab, because it is an act of worship that is metaphorically valid for charity by istihsan. Al-Shafi'i said: Since its benefits remained in his ownership, specification became obligatory so that he becomes a chooser, not compelled. If we remove specification of the direction from him, he would become compelled in the quality of worship, and the meaning of worship would become devoid of devotion and resolve. We said: The matter is as you said, except that since the legislated act is one at this time, it is specified in its time, so it is hit by the absolute name, and is not lost by error in description, like that which is specified in its place. So its permissibility with this intention is as specification, not that specification is removed; so this from us is a statement according to the implication of the cause. Al-Shafi'i said: Since specification was obligatory as a condition by consensus, it is obligatory from its beginning, because the first part of it is an act needing resolve; if it is delayed, it becomes invalid. If resolve intervenes later, it does not affect the past in any way, because the sincerity of the servant in what he has already done is not actualized; rather it is for what he has not done yet. If that part becomes corrupt, the rest becomes corrupt because it is indivisible, and it is obligatory to give weight to the side of invalidity out of precaution. This is unlike the [intention made] before [dawn] because it occurs on the whole of the fast and nothing that invalidates it intervenes, so it remains. As for what intervenes, it does not bear being made before. Do you not see that intention after midday is not valid? Do you not see that in the make-up fast, it is obligatory to distinguish between these two aspects? We said: The need for intention is because the fast is a devotional act, and this makes the fast one indivisible in validity and invalidity. Constancy upon resolve at the time of performance is dropped by consensus due to incapacity, and at the time of beginning performance initially it is also dropped by consensus due to incapacity. The initial state here became analogous to the state of continuance in prayer, and the state of continuance is analogous to the initial state in prayer. = Then this incapacity permitted making [intention] before [dawn] with separation from the pillar of worship, and it is considered existing by estimation, so it has the virtue of comprehensiveness, and the deficiency of actual existence at performance on the level of sincerity, and the incapacity leading to delay exists in sum in the kind of one who stays after dawn or recovers from his coma. And on the day of an obligatory fast it is prohibited, and the intention for supererogatory [fast] according to you is invalid; necessity has arisen, so it is more appropriate that delay with connection to the pillar is established, and for this it has precedence in existence at the act, which is the limit of the reality of the origin, and deficiency of falling short of the sum by a little is tolerated due to a necessary necessity because making intention at night for a fast is like pardon, so both are equal in the way of concession; rather this is more preponderant. This aspect necessitates expiation for breaking it, and that was narrated from both of them. Since limiting to some [parts] for necessity is valid, it is necessary to resort to what has the ruling of the whole in every respect, which is that existence is required in the majority, because the substitute is the face of the minority in comparison to the majority: it is considered nonexistent, and there is no necessity in leaving this whole that is established by estimation. So we did not permit it after midday, and we gave weight to the many over the few, because [according to another manuscript: 'right' and the meaning is the same]...
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i regarding the necessity of specifying the intention (ta'yin al-niyyah) in fasting. The discussion begins with a scenario where the benefits of the fast remain with the owner, requiring specification, unlike a gift of nisab which is valid without specification by istihsan. Al-Shafi'i argues that since the benefits of the fast remain with the person, specification is necessary to ensure the act is chosen rather than compelled; without specifying the direction (like qada' or nafl), the worshipper would lose the quality of devotion and resolve. The Hanafi response maintains that although the act is unified, because the legislated fast at a particular time is homogeneous (e.g., only qada' or only nafl at that moment), it is automatically specified by the time, analogous to an act specified by place. Thus, the intention with the absolute name suffices as a form of specification, not that specification is dropped. Al-Shafi'i then counters that specification is a condition from the beginning, as the fast is indivisible; if the initial part lacks resolve, the whole fast is corrupt, and later resolve cannot rectify the past. The Hanafi rebuttal affirms the need for intention but argues that constancy of resolve is removed by consensus due to incapacity at both the start and during performance, drawing an analogy to prayer: the initial intention in fasting is like the continuance in prayer (where intention remains without renewal), and continuance is like the initial intention in prayer. The passage further discusses the permissibility of making intention before dawn (taqdim) and the effect of necessity. It concludes that for obligatory fasts, intention must be made before midday, and for supererogatory fasts, intention is valid even after midday under necessity. The Hanafi position gives weight to the majority of the fast, and does not permit intention after midday for obligatory fasts.

Key Terms
النِّيَّة (al-niyyah): The intention to perform an act of worship, distinguishing it from habit.
التَّعْيِين (al-ta'yin): Specifying the particular act of worship (e.g., qada' vs nafl) in the intention.
العَزِيمَة (al-'azimah): Firm resolve to perform the act of worship from start to end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is a general intention at night valid for a qada' fast?
A) Because the time period uniquely determines the fast as qada'.
B) Because intention is always valid without specification.
C) Because the Prophet said so.
D) Because qada' is not required.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers a general intention sufficient when the act is specified by its time, drawing on the analogy to prayer and the dropped requirement for constant resolve.

General Rule: When Prohibition Invalidates and When It Does Not
Rule statement with example and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a prohibition does not invalidate an act unless it attacks the essence (wajh al-illah) of the act.

Core Idea
A prohibition on an external factor leaves the act valid; a prohibition on the essence invalidates it.

This lesson unpacks a critical distinction in Hanafi usul: not every divine prohibition renders the prohibited act invalid. Using the examples of prayer in usurped land and sale at the time of the Friday call, we explore how to determine when a prohibition merely makes the act sinful versus when it nullifies the act entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the prohibition
Find the act being examined (e.g., prayer) and the prohibition that applies to it (e.g., prohibition of usurpation).
2
Determine the target of the prohibition
Ask: does the prohibition directly address the essence of the act, or does it target an external factor? For prayer in usurped land, the prohibition is on usurpation, not on the prayer itself.
External factors include time, place, or associated sin.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
If the prohibition is on an external factor, the act remains valid; if on the essence, the act becomes invalid. This is the rule: 'An-nahy 'ala shay'in la yufsiduhu illa idha ta'allaqa bi-dhatihi.'
4
Derive the ruling
For prayer in usurped land: the prayer itself is valid (sahih) but the person sins by performing it in a forbidden place. For sale at the Friday call: the sale is valid but participation in the Friday prayer is wajib.
The ruling is 'valid but sinful' (sahih ma'a al-ithm).
5
Compare with void cases
This rule explains why the sale of a free person, or sales of uncertain future assets (madamin, malaqih), are void: the prohibition attaches to the very subject matter, making the contract impossible.
In those cases, the prohibition is a metaphor for negation (nafi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعرف به فازداد الأثر ، فصار فاسداً، فلم يُضمن بالشروع. والنهي عن الصلاة في أرض مغصوبة): متعلق بما ليس بوصف، فلم تفسد، فكذلك البيع وقت النداء. وهذا يخالف بيع الحر، والمضامين، والملاقيح؛ لأنه أضيف إلى غير محله، فلم ينعقد، فصار النهي مجازاً عن النفي، وهذه الاستعارة صحيحة لما بينهما من المشابهة، ولا خلاف فيه، إنما الخلاف في حكم حقيقته.
(١) قوله : والنهي عن الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة : لم أقف على نص فيه نهي عن نفس الصلاة وإنما جاء النهي عن الغصب فمنه ما تقدم ص ۱۸۱]، من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يحل مال امرىء مسلم إلا بطيب نفسه. ومنه في الأرض ما رواه البخاري ومسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن ظلم شبراً من الأرض طوقه طوقه من سبع أرضين». وما رواه أحمد والطبراني عن عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه قال: «قلت يا رسول الله ! أي الظلم أظلم ؟ فقال : ذراع من أرض ينتفع المرء المسلم من حق أخيه، فليس حصاة من الأرض يأخذها إلا طوقها يوم القيامة إلى قعر الأرض، ولا يعلم قعرها إلا الله الذي خلقها، وإسناد أحمد حسن.
(۲) قوله : فصار النهي عن عبد الله بن عمر: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن المضامين والملاقيح وحَبَل الحبلة قال والمضامين: ما في أصلاب الإبل، والملاقيح ما في بطونها وحبل الحبلة ولد ولد هذه الناقة». أخرجه عبد الرزاق. وعنه : كان أهل الجاهلية يتبايعون لحم الجزور إلى حبل الحبلة، وحبل الحبلة: ثم تحمل التي نتجت فنهاهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك». متفق عليه.
وكذلك صوم الليالي ؛ لأن الوصال غير مشروع، ولا ممكن، والنهار المتعين لشهوة البطن ،غالباً، فتعيَّن للصوم؛ تحقيقاً للابتلاء، فصار النهي مستعاراً عن النفي. ولا يلزم النكاح بغير شهود ؛ لأنه منفي بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: لا نكاح إلا بشهود، فكان نسخاً وإبطالاً. وإنما سقط الحد، وثبت النسبُ والعِدَّة؛ لشبهة العقد، ولأن النكاح شرع لملك ضروري لا ينفصل عن الحِل، حتى لم يُشرع مع الحرمة. ومن قضية النهي : التحريم، فبطل العقد؛ لمضادة ثبتت بمقتضى النهي، بخلاف البيع ؛ لأنه وضع لملك العين، والتحريم لا يضاده؛ لأن الحل فيه تابع. ألا يُرى أنه شرع في موضع الحُرمة، وفيما لا يحتمل الحل أصلاً، كالأمة المجوسية والعبيد والبهائم، وكملك الخمر. وكذلك نكاح المحارم منفي ؛ لعدم محله، فلفظ النهي في قوله
(١) قوله : فصار النهي هو في حديث الوِصال، وقد تقدم في باب بيان معرفة أحكام الخصوص [ص۱۲۱]. (۲) حديث: لا نكاح إلا بشهود قال مخرجو أحاديث «الهداية»: لم نجده، وإنما أخرج الترمذي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «البغايا : اللاتي يُنكحن أنفسهن بغير بينة، ورجح الترمذي وقفه على ابن عباس، وقيل: لا يقدح الوقف فإن الذي رفعه عبد الأعلى، وهو ثقة، ورفعه زيادة، فتقبل، قلت: أخرجه محمد في «الأصل» بلاغاً مرفوعاً بلفظ الكتاب، وأخرجه الدارقطني عن أبي سعيد الخدري موقوفاً، والله أعلم.
And it is known by it, so the effect increased, so it became corrupt, so it was not guaranteed by beginning. And the prohibition of prayer in usurped land: it pertains to that which is not a description, so it does not become corrupt, and likewise the sale at the time of the call. And this differs from the sale of a free person, and al-madamin, and al-malaqih; because it was added to something not its place, so it did not contract, so the prohibition became a metaphor for negation, and this metaphor is valid due to the similarity between them, and there is no dispute about it, only the dispute is about the ruling of its reality. (1) His saying: The prohibition of prayer in usurped land: I did not find a text containing a prohibition of the prayer itself, rather the prohibition came for usurpation, from it is what preceded on page 181, from his saying peace be upon him: 'It is not lawful for a Muslim's property except with his good pleasure.' And from it regarding land is what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Aisha may Allah be pleased with her that the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'Whoever wrongs a span of land, it will be made into a necklace for him from seven earths.' And what Ahmad and al-Tabarani narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud may Allah be pleased with him: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, which injustice is the greatest? He said: A forearm of land from which a Muslim benefits from the right of his brother, for there is not a pebble of the land he takes except that it will be made a necklace for him on the Day of Resurrection to the depth of the earth, and no one knows its depth except Allah who created it, and the chain of Ahmad is good.' (2) His saying: So the prohibition became... from Abdullah ibn Umar: that the Prophet peace be upon him forbade al-madamin, al-malaqih, and habal al-habala, and he said: al-madamin are what are in the loins of camels, and al-malaqih are what are in their wombs, and habal al-habala is the offspring of the offspring of this she-camel. Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. And from him: The people of Jahiliyyah used to trade the meat of a camel to habal al-habala, and habal al-habala: then the one that gave birth becomes pregnant, so the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him forbade them from that. Agreed upon. And likewise fasting the nights; because al-wisal is not legislated, nor possible, and the day is specified for the desire of the stomach mostly, so it is specified for fasting to realize the trial, so the prohibition became a metaphor for negation. And marriage without witnesses is not binding; because it is negated by his saying peace be upon him: 'No marriage except with witnesses', so it was abrogation and nullification. And the punishment (hadd) is dropped, while lineage and waiting period are established due to the semblance of the contract, and because marriage was legislated for necessary ownership that is inseparable from permissibility, so it was not legislated with prohibition. And from the requirement of the prohibition is prohibition (tahrim), so the contract becomes invalid due to opposition established by the implication of the prohibition, unlike sale; because it was established for ownership of the substance, and prohibition does not oppose it because permissibility in it is subsidiary. Do you not see that it is legislated in a place of prohibition, and in what does not admit permissibility at all, such as a Magian slave-girl, and male slaves, and animals, and ownership of wine. And likewise marriage with mahrams is negated due to lack of its place, so the wording of prohibition in his saying (1) His saying: So the prohibition became it is in the hadith of al-wisal, and it preceded in the chapter on the exposition of the rulings of specificity [p. 121]. (2) Hadith: 'No marriage except with witnesses' said the expositors of the ahadith of al-Hidayah: we did not find it. Rather al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Abbas may Allah be pleased with them that the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'al-baghaya (prostitutes) are those who marry themselves without evidence.' And al-Tirmidhi considered its waqf on Ibn Abbas to be preponderant, and it was said: the waqf does not harm because the one who raised it is Abd al-A'la, and he is trustworthy, and raising it is an addition, so it is accepted. I said: Muhammad narrated it in al-Asl as a balagh marfu' with the wording of the book, and al-Daraqutni narrated it from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri as mauquf, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Bazdawi's Usul explains the usul rule that a prohibition (nahy) does not necessarily invalidate an act; it depends on whether the prohibition pertains to the essence (wajh al-illah) or to an external factor. The author begins by discussing prayer in usurped land: the prohibition is against usurpation, not the prayer itself, so the prayer is valid but sinful. This is analogous to selling at the time of the Friday call—the prohibition is about abandoning the prayer, not the sale itself, so the sale is valid but sinful. This differs from the sale of a free person, or the prohibited sales of madamin and malaqih (uncertain future assets), because the prohibition there attaches to the very subject matter, making the contract void. The author then applies the same principle to fasting on nights (wisal): the prohibition is on continuous fasting (wisal), which is impossible and not legislated, so the prohibition is metaphorical negation—fasting only applies to days. For marriage without witnesses, the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses' is seen as an explicit negation (nafi) that renders the marriage void, not just prohibited. Yet, due to the semblance of a contract, the hadd punishment for fornication is dropped, and lineage and iddah are established. The author contrasts this with sale: sale is valid even if prohibited (e.g., selling at the time of call) because prohibition does not oppose the essence of sale (ownership of substance), whereas marriage is legislated for necessity and cannot coexist with absolute prohibition. The passage concludes with a note on marriage with mahrams, which is void for lack of a valid subject (mahall). Footnotes provide hadith evidence for the prohibitions on usurpation, uncertain sales, and marriage without witnesses, discussing the authenticity of the latter.

Key Terms
النهي (al-nahy): A divine or prophetic prohibition that indicates a demand to abstain. A prohibition may be literal (haqiqi) or metaphorical (majazi) for negation.
بيت (al-bay'): A contract of sale; its validity depends on the subject matter being owned and permissible for transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle explained in this passage, what is the ruling on prayer performed in a usurped land?
A) The prayer is invalid and sinful.
B) The prayer is valid but sinful.
C) The prayer is valid and not sinful because the land is not owned.
D) The prayer is invalid but not sinful.

Key Takeaway
A prohibition invalidates an act only when it directly attacks the essence (wajh al-illah) of the act; otherwise, the act remains valid but sinful.
