Void Sales: When Prohibition Negates the Contract
Differentiation of void contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify sales that are void because the prohibition attacks the essence of the subject matter.

Core Idea
When prohibition targets the very existence of the subject, it negates the contract entirely.

The passage contrasts permissible but prohibited acts with acts that are completely void. The sale of a free person, madamin, and malaqih are examples where the prohibition is not on an external factor but on the inherent impossibility or illegality of the subject matter. This lesson examines why such contracts are null from the outset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the void sales mentioned
The text lists: selling a free person (بيع الحر), al-madamin (what is in loins), and al-malaqih (what is in wombs). These are contracts with uncertain or non-existent subject matter.
2
Determine why the prohibition invalidates
The phrase 'أضيف إلى غير محله' (added to other than its place) indicates the prohibition is on the subject itself. A free person cannot be owned; a future unborn animal is uncertain. The prohibition here acts as a negation (nafi) of the contract.
Technical term: 'صار النهي مجازاً عن النفي' (the prohibition becomes a metaphor for negation).
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
If the prohibition attacks the very possibility of ownership, the contract is void (batil), not just corrupt (fasid). The subject matter is non-existent or inherently unlawful.
Contrast with sale at Friday call: the subject (e.g., goods) exists and is lawful, only the time is problematic.
4
Derive the ruling
Sale of a free person is void because a free person is not eligible for ownership. Madamin and malaqih are void due to gharar (uncertainty) and the explicit prohibition in hadith.
These are not just prohibited; they are legally non-existent contracts.
5
Distinguish from valid but prohibited sales
In valid-but-sinful cases, the prohibition is on an external factor (time, place). In void sales, the prohibition goes to the root of the contract, making it impossible.
This distinction is crucial for determining whether the contract can be enforced or must be annulled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعرف به فازداد الأثر ، فصار فاسداً، فلم يُضمن بالشروع. والنهي عن الصلاة في أرض مغصوبة): متعلق بما ليس بوصف، فلم تفسد، فكذلك البيع وقت النداء. وهذا يخالف بيع الحر، والمضامين، والملاقيح؛ لأنه أضيف إلى غير محله، فلم ينعقد، فصار النهي مجازاً عن النفي، وهذه الاستعارة صحيحة لما بينهما من المشابهة، ولا خلاف فيه، إنما الخلاف في حكم حقيقته.
(١) قوله : والنهي عن الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة : لم أقف على نص فيه نهي عن نفس الصلاة وإنما جاء النهي عن الغصب فمنه ما تقدم ص ۱۸۱]، من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يحل مال امرىء مسلم إلا بطيب نفسه. ومنه في الأرض ما رواه البخاري ومسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن ظلم شبراً من الأرض طوقه طوقه من سبع أرضين». وما رواه أحمد والطبراني عن عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه قال: «قلت يا رسول الله ! أي الظلم أظلم ؟ فقال : ذراع من أرض ينتفع المرء المسلم من حق أخيه، فليس حصاة من الأرض يأخذها إلا طوقها يوم القيامة إلى قعر الأرض، ولا يعلم قعرها إلا الله الذي خلقها، وإسناد أحمد حسن.
(۲) قوله : فصار النهي عن عبد الله بن عمر: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن المضامين والملاقيح وحَبَل الحبلة قال والمضامين: ما في أصلاب الإبل، والملاقيح ما في بطونها وحبل الحبلة ولد ولد هذه الناقة». أخرجه عبد الرزاق. وعنه : كان أهل الجاهلية يتبايعون لحم الجزور إلى حبل الحبلة، وحبل الحبلة: ثم تحمل التي نتجت فنهاهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك». متفق عليه.
وكذلك صوم الليالي ؛ لأن الوصال غير مشروع، ولا ممكن، والنهار المتعين لشهوة البطن ،غالباً، فتعيَّن للصوم؛ تحقيقاً للابتلاء، فصار النهي مستعاراً عن النفي. ولا يلزم النكاح بغير شهود ؛ لأنه منفي بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: لا نكاح إلا بشهود، فكان نسخاً وإبطالاً. وإنما سقط الحد، وثبت النسبُ والعِدَّة؛ لشبهة العقد، ولأن النكاح شرع لملك ضروري لا ينفصل عن الحِل، حتى لم يُشرع مع الحرمة. ومن قضية النهي : التحريم، فبطل العقد؛ لمضادة ثبتت بمقتضى النهي، بخلاف البيع ؛ لأنه وضع لملك العين، والتحريم لا يضاده؛ لأن الحل فيه تابع. ألا يُرى أنه شرع في موضع الحُرمة، وفيما لا يحتمل الحل أصلاً، كالأمة المجوسية والعبيد والبهائم، وكملك الخمر. وكذلك نكاح المحارم منفي ؛ لعدم محله، فلفظ النهي في قوله
(١) قوله : فصار النهي هو في حديث الوِصال، وقد تقدم في باب بيان معرفة أحكام الخصوص [ص۱۲۱]. (۲) حديث: لا نكاح إلا بشهود قال مخرجو أحاديث «الهداية»: لم نجده، وإنما أخرج الترمذي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «البغايا : اللاتي يُنكحن أنفسهن بغير بينة، ورجح الترمذي وقفه على ابن عباس، وقيل: لا يقدح الوقف فإن الذي رفعه عبد الأعلى، وهو ثقة، ورفعه زيادة، فتقبل، قلت: أخرجه محمد في «الأصل» بلاغاً مرفوعاً بلفظ الكتاب، وأخرجه الدارقطني عن أبي سعيد الخدري موقوفاً، والله أعلم.
And it is known by it, so the effect increased, so it became corrupt, so it was not guaranteed by beginning. And the prohibition of prayer in usurped land: it pertains to that which is not a description, so it does not become corrupt, and likewise the sale at the time of the call. And this differs from the sale of a free person, and al-madamin, and al-malaqih; because it was added to something not its place, so it did not contract, so the prohibition became a metaphor for negation, and this metaphor is valid due to the similarity between them, and there is no dispute about it, only the dispute is about the ruling of its reality. (1) His saying: The prohibition of prayer in usurped land: I did not find a text containing a prohibition of the prayer itself, rather the prohibition came for usurpation, from it is what preceded on page 181, from his saying peace be upon him: 'It is not lawful for a Muslim's property except with his good pleasure.' And from it regarding land is what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Aisha may Allah be pleased with her that the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'Whoever wrongs a span of land, it will be made into a necklace for him from seven earths.' And what Ahmad and al-Tabarani narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud may Allah be pleased with him: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, which injustice is the greatest? He said: A forearm of land from which a Muslim benefits from the right of his brother, for there is not a pebble of the land he takes except that it will be made a necklace for him on the Day of Resurrection to the depth of the earth, and no one knows its depth except Allah who created it, and the chain of Ahmad is good.' (2) His saying: So the prohibition became... from Abdullah ibn Umar: that the Prophet peace be upon him forbade al-madamin, al-malaqih, and habal al-habala, and he said: al-madamin are what are in the loins of camels, and al-malaqih are what are in their wombs, and habal al-habala is the offspring of the offspring of this she-camel. Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. And from him: The people of Jahiliyyah used to trade the meat of a camel to habal al-habala, and habal al-habala: then the one that gave birth becomes pregnant, so the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him forbade them from that. Agreed upon. And likewise fasting the nights; because al-wisal is not legislated, nor possible, and the day is specified for the desire of the stomach mostly, so it is specified for fasting to realize the trial, so the prohibition became a metaphor for negation. And marriage without witnesses is not binding; because it is negated by his saying peace be upon him: 'No marriage except with witnesses', so it was abrogation and nullification. And the punishment (hadd) is dropped, while lineage and waiting period are established due to the semblance of the contract, and because marriage was legislated for necessary ownership that is inseparable from permissibility, so it was not legislated with prohibition. And from the requirement of the prohibition is prohibition (tahrim), so the contract becomes invalid due to opposition established by the implication of the prohibition, unlike sale; because it was established for ownership of the substance, and prohibition does not oppose it because permissibility in it is subsidiary. Do you not see that it is legislated in a place of prohibition, and in what does not admit permissibility at all, such as a Magian slave-girl, and male slaves, and animals, and ownership of wine. And likewise marriage with mahrams is negated due to lack of its place, so the wording of prohibition in his saying (1) His saying: So the prohibition became it is in the hadith of al-wisal, and it preceded in the chapter on the exposition of the rulings of specificity [p. 121]. (2) Hadith: 'No marriage except with witnesses' said the expositors of the ahadith of al-Hidayah: we did not find it. Rather al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Abbas may Allah be pleased with them that the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'al-baghaya (prostitutes) are those who marry themselves without evidence.' And al-Tirmidhi considered its waqf on Ibn Abbas to be preponderant, and it was said: the waqf does not harm because the one who raised it is Abd al-A'la, and he is trustworthy, and raising it is an addition, so it is accepted. I said: Muhammad narrated it in al-Asl as a balagh marfu' with the wording of the book, and al-Daraqutni narrated it from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri as mauquf, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Bazdawi's Usul explains the usul rule that a prohibition (nahy) does not necessarily invalidate an act; it depends on whether the prohibition pertains to the essence (wajh al-illah) or to an external factor. The author begins by discussing prayer in usurped land: the prohibition is against usurpation, not the prayer itself, so the prayer is valid but sinful. This is analogous to selling at the time of the Friday call—the prohibition is about abandoning the prayer, not the sale itself, so the sale is valid but sinful. This differs from the sale of a free person, or the prohibited sales of madamin and malaqih (uncertain future assets), because the prohibition there attaches to the very subject matter, making the contract void. The author then applies the same principle to fasting on nights (wisal): the prohibition is on continuous fasting (wisal), which is impossible and not legislated, so the prohibition is metaphorical negation—fasting only applies to days. For marriage without witnesses, the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses' is seen as an explicit negation (nafi) that renders the marriage void, not just prohibited. Yet, due to the semblance of a contract, the hadd punishment for fornication is dropped, and lineage and iddah are established. The author contrasts this with sale: sale is valid even if prohibited (e.g., selling at the time of call) because prohibition does not oppose the essence of sale (ownership of substance), whereas marriage is legislated for necessity and cannot coexist with absolute prohibition. The passage concludes with a note on marriage with mahrams, which is void for lack of a valid subject (mahall). Footnotes provide hadith evidence for the prohibitions on usurpation, uncertain sales, and marriage without witnesses, discussing the authenticity of the latter.

Key Terms
المضامين (al-madamin): What is in the loins of male camels; an uncertain future asset.
الملاقيح (al-malaqih): What is in the wombs of female camels; also uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'فصار النهي مجازاً عن النفي' indicate?
A) The prohibition is metaphorical for making the act sinful.
B) The prohibition acts as a negation, making the contract void.
C) The prohibition is weak and can be ignored.
D) The act is valid but disliked.

Key Takeaway
When a prohibition attaches to the subject matter itself, it negates the contract's existence, rendering it void.

Fasting on Nights: Prohibition as Metaphorical Negation
Rule application to fasting on nights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the prohibition of fasting on nights (wisal) is interpreted as a metaphorical negation rather than a prohibition of a valid act.

Core Idea
Some prohibitions simply indicate that the act is impossible or not legislated, thus the prohibition is a negation.

The passage uses the example of fasting on nights (wisal) to show a different kind of prohibition: one that indicates the act is not legislated at all. The Prophet forbade continuous fasting (wisal), but the prohibition is interpreted as informing that it is not possible or not required, rather than making it a sinful act. This lesson explores how to distinguish such prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and prohibition
The act is fasting on nights (wisal) — continuous fasting without breaking at sunset. The Prophet forbade it.
2
Analyze the nature of the act
Fasting at night is not possible because night is for eating and drinking. It is not legislated (غير مشروع). The prohibition here reflects the impossibility.
The day is specified for fasting, night is not.
3
Apply the principle of metaphorical negation
In such cases, the prohibition is metaphorical: it means 'this act does not exist in the Shari'ah' rather than 'do not do it'. The act is not merely sinful; it is invalid because it cannot be validly performed.
The phrase 'صار النهي مستعاراً عن النفي' (the prohibition becomes a metaphor for negation).
4
Derive the ruling
Fasting on nights (if one attempts it) is invalid and not recognized. It is not a valid act of worship because the time is not designated for fasting.
Contrast with prayer in usurped land: prayer is valid, but here the act itself is not valid.
5
Compare with other cases
This is similar to the sale of madamin/malaqih: the prohibition negates the existence of the contract. For fasting on nights, the prohibition negates the possibility of the act being a valid fast.
The difference: in prayer example, prohibition is on external (place); here prohibition is on the very time, making the act impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعرف به فازداد الأثر ، فصار فاسداً، فلم يُضمن بالشروع. والنهي عن الصلاة في أرض مغصوبة): متعلق بما ليس بوصف، فلم تفسد، فكذلك البيع وقت النداء. وهذا يخالف بيع الحر، والمضامين، والملاقيح؛ لأنه أضيف إلى غير محله، فلم ينعقد، فصار النهي مجازاً عن النفي، وهذه الاستعارة صحيحة لما بينهما من المشابهة، ولا خلاف فيه، إنما الخلاف في حكم حقيقته.
(١) قوله : والنهي عن الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة : لم أقف على نص فيه نهي عن نفس الصلاة وإنما جاء النهي عن الغصب فمنه ما تقدم ص ۱۸۱]، من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يحل مال امرىء مسلم إلا بطيب نفسه. ومنه في الأرض ما رواه البخاري ومسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن ظلم شبراً من الأرض طوقه طوقه من سبع أرضين». وما رواه أحمد والطبراني عن عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه قال: «قلت يا رسول الله ! أي الظلم أظلم ؟ فقال : ذراع من أرض ينتفع المرء المسلم من حق أخيه، فليس حصاة من الأرض يأخذها إلا طوقها يوم القيامة إلى قعر الأرض، ولا يعلم قعرها إلا الله الذي خلقها، وإسناد أحمد حسن.
(۲) قوله : فصار النهي عن عبد الله بن عمر: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن المضامين والملاقيح وحَبَل الحبلة قال والمضامين: ما في أصلاب الإبل، والملاقيح ما في بطونها وحبل الحبلة ولد ولد هذه الناقة». أخرجه عبد الرزاق. وعنه : كان أهل الجاهلية يتبايعون لحم الجزور إلى حبل الحبلة، وحبل الحبلة: ثم تحمل التي نتجت فنهاهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك». متفق عليه.

Why is the prohibition of night fasting considered a metaphor for negation (isti'arat 'an al-nafi)?

Marriage Without Witnesses: Prohibition as Nullification
Application of negation principle to marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the ruling that marriage without witnesses is void due to the explicit negation in the hadith, and explain why the punishment is dropped but lineage established.

Core Idea
The hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بشهود' explicitly negates the existence of marriage, making it void, but saves lineage and iddah due to semblance.

This lesson examines the case of marriage without witnesses. The hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses' is taken as an explicit negation, rendering the contract void. Yet, because there is a semblance of a valid contract, certain consequences (like lineage and iddah) still apply, though the criminal punishment is dropped. This illustrates how a prohibition can be an outright nullification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the proof
The act is marriage without witnesses. The proof is the hadith: 'لا نكاح إلا بشهود' (No marriage except with witnesses).
2
Classify the hadith linguistically
The word 'لا' with 'إلا' indicates total negation (nafi). This is not merely a prohibition but a denial of the contract's existence.
In usul, 'لا نكاح إلا' is a form of negation (nafi al-jins).
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
When the prohibition is in the form of negation, the act is void (batil). The contract does not take effect.
The author says 'فكان نسخاً وإبطالاً' (so it was abrogation and nullification).
4
Examine the consequences
Even though the marriage is void, the hadd punishment for zina is dropped because there is a semblance of a contract. Similarly, lineage and iddah are established due to the semblance.
This is because marriage is legislated for necessary ownership that is inseparable from permissibility.
5
Distinguish from sale
Sale is valid even if prohibited (e.g., time) because permissibility in sale is subsidiary to ownership. In marriage, permissibility is inherent; if the contract is void, no permissibility exists.
The passage explicitly contrasts marriage with sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعرف به فازداد الأثر ، فصار فاسداً، فلم يُضمن بالشروع. والنهي عن الصلاة في أرض مغصوبة): متعلق بما ليس بوصف، فلم تفسد، فكذلك البيع وقت النداء. وهذا يخالف بيع الحر، والمضامين، والملاقيح؛ لأنه أضيف إلى غير محله، فلم ينعقد، فصار النهي مجازاً عن النفي، وهذه الاستعارة صحيحة لما بينهما من المشابهة، ولا خلاف فيه، إنما الخلاف في حكم حقيقته.
(١) قوله : والنهي عن الصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة : لم أقف على نص فيه نهي عن نفس الصلاة وإنما جاء النهي عن الغصب فمنه ما تقدم ص ۱۸۱]، من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : لا يحل مال امرىء مسلم إلا بطيب نفسه. ومنه في الأرض ما رواه البخاري ومسلم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن ظلم شبراً من الأرض طوقه طوقه من سبع أرضين». وما رواه أحمد والطبراني عن عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه قال: «قلت يا رسول الله ! أي الظلم أظلم ؟ فقال : ذراع من أرض ينتفع المرء المسلم من حق أخيه، فليس حصاة من الأرض يأخذها إلا طوقها يوم القيامة إلى قعر الأرض، ولا يعلم قعرها إلا الله الذي خلقها، وإسناد أحمد حسن.
(۲) قوله : فصار النهي عن عبد الله بن عمر: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن المضامين والملاقيح وحَبَل الحبلة قال والمضامين: ما في أصلاب الإبل، والملاقيح ما في بطونها وحبل الحبلة ولد ولد هذه الناقة». أخرجه عبد الرزاق. وعنه : كان أهل الجاهلية يتبايعون لحم الجزور إلى حبل الحبلة، وحبل الحبلة: ثم تحمل التي نتجت فنهاهم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك». متفق عليه.
وكذلك صوم الليالي ؛ لأن الوصال غير مشروع، ولا ممكن، والنهار المتعين لشهوة البطن ،غالباً، فتعيَّن للصوم؛ تحقيقاً للابتلاء، فصار النهي مستعاراً عن النفي. ولا يلزم النكاح بغير شهود ؛ لأنه منفي بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: لا نكاح إلا بشهود، فكان نسخاً وإبطالاً. وإنما سقط الحد، وثبت النسبُ والعِدَّة؛ لشبهة العقد، ولأن النكاح شرع لملك ضروري لا ينفصل عن الحِل، حتى لم يُشرع مع الحرمة. ومن قضية النهي : التحريم، فبطل العقد؛ لمضادة ثبتت بمقتضى النهي، بخلاف البيع ؛ لأنه وضع لملك العين، والتحريم لا يضاده؛ لأن الحل فيه تابع. ألا يُرى أنه شرع في موضع الحُرمة، وفيما لا يحتمل الحل أصلاً، كالأمة المجوسية والعبيد والبهائم، وكملك الخمر. وكذلك نكاح المحارم منفي ؛ لعدم محله، فلفظ النهي في قوله
(١) قوله : فصار النهي هو في حديث الوِصال، وقد تقدم في باب بيان معرفة أحكام الخصوص [ص۱۲۱]. (۲) حديث: لا نكاح إلا بشهود قال مخرجو أحاديث «الهداية»: لم نجده، وإنما أخرج الترمذي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «البغايا : اللاتي يُنكحن أنفسهن بغير بينة، ورجح الترمذي وقفه على ابن عباس، وقيل: لا يقدح الوقف فإن الذي رفعه عبد الأعلى، وهو ثقة، ورفعه زيادة، فتقبل، قلت: أخرجه محمد في «الأصل» بلاغاً مرفوعاً بلفظ الكتاب، وأخرجه الدارقطني عن أبي سعيد الخدري موقوفاً، والله أعلم.
And it is known by it, so the effect increased, so it became corrupt, so it was not guaranteed by beginning. And the prohibition of prayer in usurped land: it pertains to that which is not a description, so it does not become corrupt, and likewise the sale at the time of the call. And this differs from the sale of a free person, and al-madamin, and al-malaqih; because it was added to something not its place, so it did not contract, so the prohibition became a metaphor for negation, and this metaphor is valid due to the similarity between them, and there is no dispute about it, only the dispute is about the ruling of its reality. (1) His saying: The prohibition of prayer in usurped land: I did not find a text containing a prohibition of the prayer itself, rather the prohibition came for usurpation, from it is what preceded on page 181, from his saying peace be upon him: 'It is not lawful for a Muslim's property except with his good pleasure.' And from it regarding land is what al-Bukhari and Muslim narrated from Aisha may Allah be pleased with her that the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'Whoever wrongs a span of land, it will be made into a necklace for him from seven earths.' And what Ahmad and al-Tabarani narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud may Allah be pleased with him: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, which injustice is the greatest? He said: A forearm of land from which a Muslim benefits from the right of his brother, for there is not a pebble of the land he takes except that it will be made a necklace for him on the Day of Resurrection to the depth of the earth, and no one knows its depth except Allah who created it, and the chain of Ahmad is good.' (2) His saying: So the prohibition became... from Abdullah ibn Umar: that the Prophet peace be upon him forbade al-madamin, al-malaqih, and habal al-habala, and he said: al-madamin are what are in the loins of camels, and al-malaqih are what are in their wombs, and habal al-habala is the offspring of the offspring of this she-camel. Narrated by Abd al-Razzaq. And from him: The people of Jahiliyyah used to trade the meat of a camel to habal al-habala, and habal al-habala: then the one that gave birth becomes pregnant, so the Messenger of Allah peace be upon him forbade them from that. Agreed upon. And likewise fasting the nights; because al-wisal is not legislated, nor possible, and the day is specified for the desire of the stomach mostly, so it is specified for fasting to realize the trial, so the prohibition became a metaphor for negation. And marriage without witnesses is not binding; because it is negated by his saying peace be upon him: 'No marriage except with witnesses', so it was abrogation and nullification. And the punishment (hadd) is dropped, while lineage and waiting period are established due to the semblance of the contract, and because marriage was legislated for necessary ownership that is inseparable from permissibility, so it was not legislated with prohibition. And from the requirement of the prohibition is prohibition (tahrim), so the contract becomes invalid due to opposition established by the implication of the prohibition, unlike sale; because it was established for ownership of the substance, and prohibition does not oppose it because permissibility in it is subsidiary. Do you not see that it is legislated in a place of prohibition, and in what does not admit permissibility at all, such as a Magian slave-girl, and male slaves, and animals, and ownership of wine. And likewise marriage with mahrams is negated due to lack of its place, so the wording of prohibition in his saying (1) His saying: So the prohibition became it is in the hadith of al-wisal, and it preceded in the chapter on the exposition of the rulings of specificity [p. 121]. (2) Hadith: 'No marriage except with witnesses' said the expositors of the ahadith of al-Hidayah: we did not find it. Rather al-Tirmidhi narrated from Ibn Abbas may Allah be pleased with them that the Prophet peace be upon him said: 'al-baghaya (prostitutes) are those who marry themselves without evidence.' And al-Tirmidhi considered its waqf on Ibn Abbas to be preponderant, and it was said: the waqf does not harm because the one who raised it is Abd al-A'la, and he is trustworthy, and raising it is an addition, so it is accepted. I said: Muhammad narrated it in al-Asl as a balagh marfu' with the wording of the book, and al-Daraqutni narrated it from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri as mauquf, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Bazdawi's Usul explains the usul rule that a prohibition (nahy) does not necessarily invalidate an act; it depends on whether the prohibition pertains to the essence (wajh al-illah) or to an external factor. The author begins by discussing prayer in usurped land: the prohibition is against usurpation, not the prayer itself, so the prayer is valid but sinful. This is analogous to selling at the time of the Friday call—the prohibition is about abandoning the prayer, not the sale itself, so the sale is valid but sinful. This differs from the sale of a free person, or the prohibited sales of madamin and malaqih (uncertain future assets), because the prohibition there attaches to the very subject matter, making the contract void. The author then applies the same principle to fasting on nights (wisal): the prohibition is on continuous fasting (wisal), which is impossible and not legislated, so the prohibition is metaphorical negation—fasting only applies to days. For marriage without witnesses, the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses' is seen as an explicit negation (nafi) that renders the marriage void, not just prohibited. Yet, due to the semblance of a contract, the hadd punishment for fornication is dropped, and lineage and iddah are established. The author contrasts this with sale: sale is valid even if prohibited (e.g., selling at the time of call) because prohibition does not oppose the essence of sale (ownership of substance), whereas marriage is legislated for necessity and cannot coexist with absolute prohibition. The passage concludes with a note on marriage with mahrams, which is void for lack of a valid subject (mahall). Footnotes provide hadith evidence for the prohibitions on usurpation, uncertain sales, and marriage without witnesses, discussing the authenticity of the latter.

Key Terms
النكاح (al-nikah): Marriage contract; it is invalid without witnesses, as the hadith 'No marriage except with witnesses' negates its existence.
الحد (al-hadd): Prescribed punishment for zina (adultery/fornication).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadd punishment dropped in a marriage without witnesses?
A) Because the contract is valid.
B) Because of the semblance of a contract (shubhah).
C) Because witnesses are not required.
D) Because the Prophet forgave it.

Key Takeaway
Marriage without witnesses is void due to explicit negation in the hadith, but the Islamic legal system protects lineage and avoids punishment due to semblance.

Marriage with Mahrams: Negation Due to Missing Place (Mahall)
Final application: negation due to missing mahall

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why marriage with mahram relatives is void because the subject (mahall) is non-existent.

Core Idea
Some prohibitions void a contract because the very subject (mahall) is missing; the act is impossible by nature.

This final case in the passage deals with marriage between mahrams (prohibited degrees of kinship). Such a marriage is not merely prohibited; it is considered non-existent because the legal place (mahall) for such a contract does not exist. The prohibition functions as a negation, similar to the sale of a free person. This lesson wraps up the discussion by showing how the type of prohibition determines the validity of the act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the prohibition
The act is marriage between mahrams (e.g., brother and sister, parent and child). The prohibition is explicit in the Quran (e.g., Quran 4:23).
2
Determine if the mahall exists
For a contract to be valid, there must be a valid subject (mahall). In the case of mahrams, the relationship itself prevents the existence of a valid marriage; the prohibition is not on an external factor but on the very possibility.
The text says 'لعدم محله' (due to the absence of its place).
3
Apply the principle of negation
The prohibition here is a metaphor for negation because the marriage cannot be contracted at all. The act is not just sinful; it is legally impossible.
Similar to sale of a free person: the subject matter does not exist.
4
Derive the ruling
Marriage with mahrams is void (batil). There is no contract at all, and it is not even considered a semblance of a contract.
Unlike marriage without witnesses, here there is no shubhah because the prohibition is absolute.
5
Contrast with marriage without witnesses
In marriage without witnesses, there is a semblance because the contract was intended and only lacking a condition. In marriage with mahrams, the relationship itself prevents any possibility of a valid contract.
Thus, hadd punishment would apply? Actually, it would be considered zina because there is no semblance.

Key Terms
المحارم (al-maharm): Relatives within prohibited degrees for marriage (e.g., mother, sister, daughter).
المحل (al-mahall): The subject of a contract; if absent, the contract is void.

What is meant by 'لعدم محله' (due to absence of its place) in the context of marriage with mahrams?

The Negation-Exception Construction as Legal Proof
Ruling on marriage without witnesses, proven by hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a negation-exception construction (النفي والاستثناء) indicates the absence of validity when the excepted condition is missing.

Core Idea
‘No marriage except with witnesses’ means no valid marriage at all without witnesses.

The passage presents a ruling that a marriage without witnesses is not legally binding. The proof is a short but powerful hadith: 'لا نكاح إلا بشهود.' In Hanafi usul, the negation of a genus (here 'marriage') followed by an exception (except with witnesses) is a definitive indicator that the condition (witnesses) is essential for the existence of the contract. This lesson will walk through the analytical steps to extract the ruling from this textual construction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Operative Phrase
Locate the key phrase in the source text that conveys the legal rule. Here it is the hadith: 'لا نكاح إلا بشهود.'
The source uses the same wording as the proof.
2
Classify the Textual Category
Analyze the linguistic structure. The phrase 'لا نكاح' is a negation of the genus (نفي الجنس), which in Arabic grammar makes 'marriage' non-existent or invalid. The exception 'إلا بشهود' restricts this negation, so the negation applies only when witnesses are absent. In usul, this is a form of عام مخصوص (general made specific) or a mafhum mukhālif? Actually, it is a direct textual indication (mantiq) that negates the hukm when the condition is missing.
Hanafi usul treats negation-exception as قاطع في الدلالة (definitive in meaning) when the negation is of the genus.
3
Apply the Hanafi Principle
The Hanafi principle: 'النفي والاستثناء يفيد الحصر' - negation followed by exception indicates exclusivity. Thus, the validity of marriage is exclusively tied to the presence of witnesses. Without witnesses, the marriage is not simply invalid in a minor sense; it is legally non-existent (منفي).
This principle is derived from Arabic usage and is accepted by the majority of usulis.
4
Derive the Ruling
From the hadith, the ruling is that a marriage contract without witnesses is void (باطل) and does not take legal effect (لا يلزم). The passage says it is 'نسخاً وإبطالاً' (abrogation and nullification), meaning any prior allowance is overridden.
The term 'نسخ' here may refer to abrogation of a previous ruling that might have allowed it; but the key is the absolute nullity.
5
Note the Epistemological Weight
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), yet its meaning (dalala) is qati because the linguistic structure is unambiguous. Thus, the ruling is considered definitive in practice for the Hanafi school.
This distinction between thubut and dalala is crucial in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يلزم النكاح بغير شهود؛ لأنه منفي بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: لا نكاح إلا بشهود، فكان نسخاً وإبطالاً.
And marriage without witnesses does not become binding; because it is negated by his saying, peace be upon him: 'There is no marriage except with witnesses', so it is an abrogation and nullification.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents a fiqh ruling: a marriage contract without witnesses is not valid (la yalzam). The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (SAW): 'There is no marriage except with witnesses.' The phrase 'la nikaaha' (no marriage) indicates negation of validity. Thus, the hadith effectively abrogates any previous allowance or presumption, making such marriages void. The term 'naskh' here means abrogation of any conflicting ruling, and 'ibtaal' means nullification of the contract.

Key Terms
يلزم (yalzam): becomes binding, takes legal effect
منفي (munfiy): negated, declared non-existent
نسخاً وإبطالاً (naskhan wa ibtaalan): abrogation and nullification
لا نكاح إلا بشهود (laa nikaaha illaa bi-shuhood): There is no (valid) marriage except with witnesses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What linguistic feature in the hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بشهود' makes the Hanafi ruling definitive?
A) The word 'نكاح' is defined.
B) The negation of the genus followed by an exception.
C) The hadith is mutawatir.
D) The exception 'إلا بشهود' is a general statement.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بشهود' linguistically and legally establishes that witnesses are a necessary condition for a valid marriage; without them, the marriage is void.

Particle Analysis in Oath Expiation Hadith
Analyzing particles to derive ruling on order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of preferring haqiqah over majaz to determine the correct interpretation of particles in a hadith, and identify the resulting legal flexibility in oath expiation order.

Core Idea
When literal meaning leads to impossibility, figurative interpretation becomes necessary.

This passage examines how Hanafi usul applies the principle of acting upon haqiqah when possible, and resorting to majaz when the literal meaning is impossible. Through the analysis of the particles 'wa', 'thumma', and 'fa' in the oath expiation hadith, we see how the Hanafi school derives flexibility in the order of expiation and the better action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its literal meaning
The hadith uses 'thumma' (then) implying sequence. Note its literal function in Arabic.
In the version: 'فليكفر يمينه، ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير'
2
Assess possibility of acting literally
Can expiation be performed before breaking the oath? No, because expiation is only obligatory after the oath is broken (hanth). Literal interpretation would require expiation before hanth, which is impossible.
Expiation without hanth is not legally valid.
3
Apply the rule: haqiqah over majaz when possible
Since literal is impossible, we must move to figurative interpretation. This is a core Hanafi usul principle.
Hanafi: al-haqiqah tulaq bi imkan, fa idha ta'addara al-haqiqah yuntaqal ila al-majaz.
4
Determine the figurative meaning
Interpret 'thumma' as 'wa' (simple conjunction) to remove the impossibility. This aligns with other narrations using 'wa' or 'fa'.
The author argues that borrowing 'thumma' for 'wa' is valid; 'fa' is even more appropriate.
5
Derive the legal ruling
Both orders (expiation before action, or action before expiation) are permissible. The thamarah al-khilaf is the practical flexibility.
Hanafi position: no required order; expiation can precede or follow the better action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنه يُحمل على حقيقته؛ لأن العمل به ممكن؛ لأنا نعمل بحقيقة موجب الأمر، فنجعل الكفارة واجبةً بعد الحنث. وروي: «فليكفر يمينه، ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير»: فحَمَلْنا هذا على واو العطف؛ لأن العمل بحقيقته غير ممكن، وهو موجَبُ الأمر؛ لأن التكفير قبل الحنث غيرُ واجب، فكان المجاز متعيّناً؛ تحقيقاً لما المقصود. وإذا صح أن يُستعار ثم للواو فالفاء به أولى؛ لأن جوازه بالفاء أقرب، ولهذا قال بعضُ مشايخنا رحمهم الله : فيمن قال لامرأته : إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق فطالقٌ فطالقٌ، ولم يدخل بها: إن هذا على الاختلاف، مثل ما اختلفوا في الواو ، إلا أن الحقيقة أولى، فلذلك اخترنا الاتفاق في هذا. لفظ من حلف على يمين فرأى غيرها خيراً منها، فليأت الذي هو خير، وليكفر عن يمينه. رواه أحمد ومسلم والنسائي وابن ماجه وهذا مثل لفظ الكتاب، إلا أنه بالواو. وعن أبي هريرة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال مَن حلف على يمين، فرأى غيرها خيراً منها فليكفر عن يمينه وليفعل الذي هو خير». رواه أحمد ومسلم والترمذي وصححه وفي لفظ: فليأت الذي هو خير وليكفر عن يمينه». رواه مسلم. وعن أبي موسى الأشعري عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لا أحلف على يمين فأرى غيرها خيراً منها : إلا أتيتُ الذي هو خير وتحلَّلتُها»، وفي لفظ : «إلا أتيتُ الذي هو خير، وكفّرتُ عن يميني»، وفي لفظ : «إلا كفرتُ عن يميني، وأتيت الذي هو خير متفق عليهن. وإذا قدم الجزاء بحرف الفاء: فعلى هذا أيضاً.
It is interpreted according to its literal meaning because acting upon it is possible; for we act according to the literal implication of the command, thus we make expiation obligatory after the violation. And it is narrated: 'Let him expiate his oath, then let him do what is better' — we interpreted this as the conjunction 'wa' because acting upon its literal meaning is not possible, and it is the implication of the command, because expiation before violation is not obligatory, so the figurative meaning is necessary to achieve the intended purpose. And if it is correct that 'thumma' can be borrowed for 'wa', then 'fa' is more appropriate because its permissibility with 'fa' is closer. That is why some of our teachers (may Allah have mercy on them) said concerning one who said to his wife, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced, divorced, divorced' and he did not consummate the marriage: this is subject to disagreement, just as they disagreed about 'wa', but the literal meaning is preferable, so we choose agreement in this. The wording: 'Whoever swears an oath and then sees something better, let him do what is better and expiate his oath' — narrated by Ahmad, Muslim, Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah, and this is like the wording of the book except that it uses 'wa'. And from Abu Huraira that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever swears an oath and then sees something better, let him expiate his oath and do what is better' — narrated by Ahmad, Muslim, Tirmidhi who authenticated it, and in one wording: 'Let him do what is better and expiate his oath' — narrated by Muslim. And from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I do not swear an oath and then see something better except that I do what is better and break it' and in one wording: 'except that I do what is better and expiate my oath' and in one wording: 'except that I expiate my oath and do what is better' — agreed upon. And if the result is introduced with the particle 'fa', then it is also upon this.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the hadith on oath expiation focusing on the particles 'wa' and 'fa' to determine the proper order of actions. The author begins by stating that when a word can be interpreted literally, that is preferred if possible. The hadith wording 'فليكفر يمينه، ثم ليأت بالذي هو خير' (let him expiate his oath, then do what is better) uses 'thumma', which implies sequence. But the author interprets this 'thumma' metaphorically as 'wa' (and) because acting literally is impossible: expiation before breaking the oath is not obligatory. Thus the figurative meaning is necessary. The author then argues that if 'thumma' can be borrowed for 'wa', then 'fa' (which also implies sequence but is weaker) is even more appropriate. He cites the opinion of some Hanafi scholars regarding a conditional divorce with multiple 'fa's: the matter is disputed like the case of 'wa', but the literal meaning (sequence) is preferred, so they chose agreement. The author then cites various hadith narrations using 'wa' or 'fa' to support the permissibility of either order. The key principle is that the literal implication of particles is to be upheld when possible, but when impossible, figurative interpretation is permissible. The passage concludes that if the result is introduced with 'fa', the same ruling applies.

Key Terms
الحقيقة (al-haqiqah): Literal or real meaning of a word as opposed to metaphorical.
المجاز (al-majaz): Figurative or metaphorical meaning used when literal meaning is not intended or not possible.
واو العطف (waw al-'atf): The conjunctive particle 'wa' meaning 'and', indicating mere conjunction without sequence.
ثم (thumma): Particle indicating sequence and delay, but here interpreted metaphorically as 'wa'.
الفاء (al-fa'): Particle indicating immediate sequence or causation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis, why is the word 'thumma' in the oath expiation hadith interpreted figuratively as 'wa'?
A) Because 'thumma' always means 'and' in legal contexts.
B) Because acting on the literal meaning (expiate before breaking the oath) is impossible.
C) Because the majority of hadith narrations use 'wa'.
D) Because Imam Abu Hanifa preferred figurative interpretation in all cases.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul requires applying literal meaning when possible, but when impossible, figurative interpretation is necessary to achieve the Shari'ah's objective.

The Particle 'على' and Its Variants in Amān: Linguistic Precision in Hanafi Usul
Textual analysis of particles in amān from al-Siyar al-Kabir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the legal ruling for the scope of amān based on the different Arabic prepositions as used in al-Siyar al-Kabir, applying Hanafi usul principles of literal interpretation of particles.

Core Idea
Each Arabic particle in amān yields a distinct legal scope; linguistic analysis determines fiqh rulings.

In the Hanafi school, legal rulings often hinge on the precise meaning of Arabic particles. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, in al-Siyar al-Kabir, demonstrates how the choice of preposition in granting amān (safe conduct) changes the number of protected individuals. This lesson walks through the key phrases and the usul principle that governs their interpretation: the literal meaning of a particle is binding unless context indicates otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle in each phrase
Read each statement from the source text and isolate the Arabic preposition (harf jarr) or conjunction used. The particles are: 'على', 'و', 'ب', 'في', and the phrase with 'لي'.
Particles are function words that modify meaning; in usul, they are considered zahir (clear) in their primary sense.
2
Recall the primary meaning of the particle
For each particle, recall its core meaning in Arabic: 'على' means 'upon/over' (implying inclusion of the speaker?), 'و' means 'and', 'ب' means 'with/at', 'في' means 'in', and the lām in 'لي' indicates 'for/belonging to'.
These meanings are established by language and are the basis for analogy.
3
Apply the meaning to the amān context
Consider how the particle shapes the scope of protection. For example, 'على' in 'آمنوني على عشرة' is interpreted as the protection covering the speaker and ten others, as if the speaker is 'over' them. In contrast, 'في' in 'آمنوني في عشرة' implies the speaker is 'in' a group of ten, so protection covers him plus nine others.
The usul principle: the literal meaning (haqiqah) of the particle is taken unless a shifting context (qarina) exists.
4
Determine the ruling and who has the choice
From the application, derive the number of protected individuals and identify whether the head of the fortress or the Muslim Imam has the choice of who those individuals are. The text explicitly states the outcomes.
The choice is an additional legal effect; it follows from the nature of the phrase and the authority of the one granting amān.
5
Connect to the original usul principle
Recognize that all these rulings are derived from a single methodological principle: the meaning of particles is literal unless there is evidence to shift it. This is a key feature of Hanafi usul.
This principle is part of the broader Hanafi approach to linguistic interpretation (usul al-fiqh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذَكَر في السير الكبير باباً بناه على معرفة الحروف التي ذكرنا: آمِنُوني على عشرة من أهل الحصن قال ذلك رأس الحصن، ففعلنا : وقع عليه، وعلى عشرة غيره، والخيار إليه. ولو قال آمنوني وعشرة : فكذلك إلا أن الخيار إلى إمام المسلمين. - ولو قال بعشرة فمثل قوله : وعشرة. ولو قال : في عشرة : وقع على تسعة سواه، والخيار إلى الإمام. ولو قال: آمنوا لي عشرة وقع على عشرة، لا غير، ولرأس الحصن أن يُدخل نفسه فيهم، والخيار فيهم إليه، وذلك يُخرَّج على هذا الأصل.
And he mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir a chapter built on the knowledge of the letters (particles) we have mentioned: 'Grant me protection over ten people from the fortress' – if the head of the fortress said that, and we did it: it applies to him and ten others, and the choice is his. And if he said 'Grant me protection and ten', it is similar except that the choice is to the Imam of the Muslims. And if he said 'with ten', it is like his saying 'and ten'. And if he said 'in ten', it applies to nine besides him, and the choice is to the Imam. And if he said 'Grant protection to me for ten', it applies to ten, no more, and the head of the fortress may include himself among them, and the choice among them is his, and that is derived from this principle.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Siyar al-Kabir discusses the legal implications of different Arabic prepositions when used in the context of granting amān (protection). If the head of a fortress says 'أمّنوني على عشرة' (grant me protection for/over ten people), the protection covers him and ten others, and he has the choice of who those ten are. If he says 'وعشرة' (and ten), it is similar but the choice goes to the Muslim Imam. If he says 'بعشرة' (with ten), it is like 'وعشرة'. If he says 'في عشرة' (in ten), the protection covers nine others besides him, with the Imam choosing. If he says 'آمنوا لي عشرة' (grant protection to me for ten), it covers exactly ten individuals, and he may include himself among them, with the choice among them being his. These rulings are all derived from the original principle (الأصل) which is the understanding of the particles.

Key Terms
على (ala): A preposition meaning 'over' or 'upon'; in this context, it indicates the protected party includes the speaker and the speaker has the choice.
أمان (aman): Protection or safe conduct granted to enemy combatants.
باء (ba): Preposition 'bi' meaning 'with/at'; treated like 'و' (and) in this context.
في (fi): Preposition 'in'; indicates the speaker is part of the number specified.
لام (lam): Preposition 'li' meaning 'for/belonging to'; used in 'لي' (for me) to specify exact individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ten people including the head, head's choice.
B) Ten people excluding the head, Imam's choice.
C) Exactly ten people (head may include himself), head's choice.
D) Exactly ten people (head is automatically included), Imam's choice.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the literal meaning of each Arabic particle uniquely determines the legal scope of amān, demonstrating the school's emphasis on precise linguistic analysis.

The Hanafi Principle on Khabar al-Wahid: Authority and Boundaries
Articulating the Hanafi principle on khabar al-wahid with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle regarding khabar al-wahid to identify when its ruling is upheld and when it yields to qat'i texts.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid is authoritative for action but yields to definitive texts when conflict arises.

Imam al-Bazdawi presents the Hanafi middle path on khabar al-wahid: it is a valid source for obligations, but it is not on par with the Qur'an and mutawatir sunnah. Through several examples, he illustrates how khabar al-wahid establishes rulings like the delay of Maghrib at Muzdalifah and the order of missed prayers, yet these rulings are dropped when they conflict with broader Quranic principles. This lesson unpacks the epistemological weight of khabar al-wahid and the conditions for its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi principle
State that khabar al-wahid is a hujjah for action but not for certainty. Note the two errors: rejection and equating with qat'i texts.
2
Examine the examples of obligation
For each example (justice, tawaf, sa'i, delay of Maghrib, tartib, al-Hatim), note what obligation is established and its proof.
Focus on the link between the hadith and the ruling.
3
Analyze the boundaries of application
Identify when the obligation from khabar al-wahid is dropped: e.g., delay of Maghrib after dawn, tartib when time is tight or prayers are numerous.
The text gives specific conditions for suspension.
4
Identify the underlying usul rule
Recognize that conflict with a qat'i text (e.g., timeliness of prayer) causes the khabar al-wahid ruling to yield.
This is the key difference from schools that treat khabar al-wahid as equal to mutawatir.
5
Synthesize the complete Hanafi rule
Formulate: Khabar al-wahid establishes wujub in practice, but it is zanni and cannot override definitive proofs; it is applied when no conflict exists, else suspended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك الكتاب : أوجب الركوع، وخبر الواحد أوجب التعديل). وكذلك الطواف مع الطهارة (٢). فمَن ردَّ خبر الواحد : فقد ضل عن سواء السبيل. ومَن سواه بالكتاب والسنة المتواترة فقد أخطأ في رفعه عن منزلته، ووَضَعَ الأعلى عن منزلته ، وإنما الطريق المستقيم: ما قلنا. وكذلك السعي في الحج والعمرة) ، وما أشبه ذلك. وكذلك تأخير المغرب إلى العشاء بالمزدلفة واجب، ثبت بخبر الواحد)، فإذا صلى في الطريق: أُمر بالإعادة عند بالإعادة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله ؛ عملاً بخبر الواحد. (۱) قوله : وخبر الواحد أوجب التعديل : هو حديث أبي هريرة المتقدم في باب بيان معرفة أحكام الخصوص [ص۱۰۸]. (۲) قوله : وكذلك الطواف مع الطهارة : تقدم في أحكام الخصوص [ص١٠٩]. (۳) قوله : وكذلك السعي عن صفية قالت : أخبرني نسوة من بني عبد الدار اللاتي أدركن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قلن : دخلنا دار ابن أبي حسين، رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يطوف بين الصفا والمروة والناس بين يديه، وهو وراءهم، وهو يسعى حتى أرى ركبته من شدة ما يسعى وهو يقول: اسعوا فإن الله تعالى كتب عليكم السعي . رواه الدارقطني . قال ابن عبد الهادي : له إسناد صحيح. (٤) قوله : ثبت بخبر الواحد : هو ما أسامة بن زيد قال : رَدِفتُ رسولَ الله عن صلى الله عليه وسلم من عرفات، فلما بلغ الشُّعب الأيسر الذي دون المزدلفة: أناخ ، فبال، ثم جاء فصببت عليه الوضوء، فتوضأ وضوء خفيفاً، ثم قلت الصلاة؟ قال: الصلاة أمامك». متفق عليه. فإن لم يفعل حتى طلع الفجر : سقطت الإعادة؛ لأن تأخير المغرب إنما وجب إلى وقت العشاء وقد انتهى وقت العشاء، فانتهى العمل، فلا يبقى الفساد من بعد إلا بالعلم، وخبر الواحد لا يوجبه، ولا يعارض حكم الكتاب، فلا يفسد العشاء. وكذلك الترتيب في الصلوات واجب، ثبت بخبر الواحد)، فإذا ضاق الوقت، أو كثرت الفوائتُ، فصار معارضاً لحكم الكتاب بتغيير الوقتية : سقط العمل به. (۱) قوله : وكذلك الترتيب واجب بخبر الواحد هو ما أخرج الدارقطني عن ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : مَن نسي صلاة فلم يذكرها إلا وهو مع الإمام : فليتم صلاته، فإذا فرغ من صلاته فليعد الصلاة التي نسي، ثم ليُعد الصلاة التي صلاها مع الإمام». (۲) قوله : وثبت كون الحطيم من البيت بخبر الواحد: عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: «سألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الحجر أمن البيت هو؟ قال: نعم. الحديث متفق عليه. وفي رواية عنها: كنتُ أحب أن أدخل البيت أصلي فيه، فأخذ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بيدي فأدخلني الحجر، فقال صلي في الحجر إذا أردتِ دخول البيت، فإنما هو قطعة من البيت. رواه الخمسة إلا ابن ماجه، وصححه الترمذي.
And likewise the Book: it made bowing obligatory, and the single-narrator hadith made justice ('adl) obligatory. And likewise circumambulation with purity. So whoever rejects the single-narrator hadith has gone astray from the straight path. And whoever equates it with the Book and the mutawatir sunnah has erred in raising it above its station and lowering the higher from its station. The straight path is only what we have said. And likewise the sa'i in Hajj and 'Umrah, and what resembles that. And likewise delaying Maghrib to 'Isha' at Muzdalifah is obligatory, established by a single-narrator hadith. So if he prays on the way, he is commanded to repeat according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, acting upon the single-narrator hadith. Footnote 1: His saying: 'the single-narrator hadith made justice obligatory' is the hadith of Abu Hurayra previously mentioned in the chapter on explaining the rulings of particularity. Footnote 2: His saying: 'and likewise circumambulation with purity' already mentioned in rulings of particularity. Footnote 3: His saying: 'and likewise the sa'i' from Safiyya who said: some women from Banu 'Abd al-Dar who had met the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, informed me, they said: we entered the house of Ibn Abi Husayn, and the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was performing sa'i between Safa and Marwa with people in front of him and he behind them, and he was jogging so intensely that I saw his knee due to the intensity of his jogging while he said: 'Perform sa'i, for Allah has written sa'i upon you.' Reported by al-Daraqutni. Ibn 'Abd al-Hadi said: it has a sound chain. Footnote 4: His saying: 'established by a single-narrator hadith' is what Usama ibn Zayd said: I rode behind the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, from 'Arafat. When he reached the left mountain pass that is before Muzdalifah, he made the camel kneel, urinated, then came and I poured water for his ablution, so he performed a light ablution, then I said: the prayer? He said: 'The prayer is ahead of you.' Agreed upon. If he does not do it until dawn breaks, the repetition is dropped because the delay of Maghrib was only obligatory until the time of 'Isha', and the time of 'Isha' has ended, so the obligation is finished, and corruption remains thereafter only through knowledge, and the single-narrator hadith does not impose it, nor does it oppose the ruling of the Book, so it does not invalidate the 'Isha' prayer. And likewise the order in prayers is obligatory, established by a single-narrator hadith. So if time becomes tight or the missed prayers become numerous, it becomes opposing the ruling of the Book by changing the timeliness, so acting upon it is dropped. Footnote 1: His saying: 'and likewise order is obligatory by a single-narrator hadith' is what al-Daraqutni reported from Ibn 'Umar: the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer and does not remember it except while he is with the imam, let him complete his prayer, and when he finishes his prayer, let him repeat the prayer he forgot, then let him repeat the prayer he prayed with the imam.' Footnote 2: His saying: 'and it is established that al-Hatim is part of the House by a single-narrator hadith' from 'Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: 'I asked the Prophet, peace be upon him, about al-Hijr: is it part of the House? He said: Yes.' The hadith is agreed upon. In another narration: 'I wished to enter the House and pray in it, so the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, took my hand and made me enter al-Hijr and said: Pray in al-Hijr if you wish to enter the House, for it is a piece of the House.' Reported by the five except Ibn Majah, and al-Tirmidhi authenticated it.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage from Imam al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh (Kanz al-Wusul) expounds the Hanafi position on the authority of khabar al-wahid (single-narrator hadith). The author states that khabar al-wahid is a valid source for establishing obligations (wujub), but it must be recognized as subordinate to the Qur'an and mutawatir sunnah—the qat'i (definitive) texts. Rejecting khabar al-wahid altogether is misguidance, while equating it with qat'i texts is an error of elevating it beyond its proper station. The straight path is to accept khabar al-wahid as a hujjah (proof) for action, but not as definitive in belief or as overriding clear proofs. The passage provides several illustrative examples: (1) The obligation of justice ('adl) in witnesses is proven by a khabar al-wahid (hadith of Abu Hurayra). (2) The obligation of tawaf with purity (wudu) is also based on a single narration. (3) Sa'i between Safa and Marwa is wajib by a khabar al-wahid. (4) Delaying Maghrib prayer until 'Isha' at Muzdalifah is wajib by a single narration (hadith of Usama). If one prays Maghrib on the way, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require repetition (i'ada) because the obligation to delay is established by khabar al-wahid. However, if dawn breaks before making up the delay, the i'ada is dropped—because the obligation was limited to the time of 'Isha', which has expired. After the time ends, the ruling of corruption (fasad) would require definitive knowledge ('ilm), which khabar al-wahid does not provide, and it cannot oppose the Qur'anic principle that prayers are fixed times. (5) The order (tartib) of missed prayers is wajib by khabar al-wahid, but if time is tight or many prayers are missed, the obligation to maintain order is dropped because it would conflict with the Qur'an's command to pray on time. (6) The Hatim (al-Hijr) is established as part of the Ka'ba by a khabar al-wahid (hadith of 'Aisha), so tawaf around it is obligatory, but this does not contradict the original (asl) because the original obligation is tawaf of the House; the detail of including the Hatim is a specific addition from khabar al-wahid. The Hanafi principle is consistent: khabar al-wahid is relied upon for establishing obligations in practice, but it yields to qat'i texts when conflict arises, and it does not create definitive knowledge for matters beyond the temporal realm.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators at each level, which does not reach the level of tawatur and thus yields zann (probable knowledge) rather than qat' (certainty).
متواتر (mutawatir): A transmission by such a large number at each level that collusion on falsehood is impossible, yielding qat' (certain knowledge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of delaying Maghrib at Muzdalifah, why does i'ada (repetition) drop if dawn breaks before the person makes up the delay?
A) Because the hadith is weak and not reliable in such cases.
B) Because the time for Maghrib has ended and the obligation of delay was only for the 'Isha' period, and khabar al-wahid cannot impose a missed obligation after the fact.
C) Because the person is excused due to forgetfulness.
D) Because the Qur'an allows flexibility in travel.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts khabar al-wahid as a legitimate source for establishing obligations, but it is subordinate to the Qur'an and mutawatir sunnah; when conflict arises, the qat'i text prevails.

Khabar al-Wahid and Quranic Conflict: Tartib and Hatim
Analyzing two examples of Khabar al-Wahid conflicting with Quranic principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a Khabar al-Wahid is overridden by a Quranic principle and apply the Hanafi rule that Khabar al-Wahid can establish wujub but not contradict qat'i texts.

Core Idea
Khabar al-Wahid establishes obligation, but yields when it contradicts the Quran's certainty.

Khabar al-Wahid (single-narrator hadith) is a zanni source that can establish wujub in the Hanafi school. However, when it directly conflicts with a qat'i principle from the Quran, it must yield. This lesson examines two illustrative cases: the order of missed prayers (tartib) and the status of the Hatim (the semicircular wall near the Kaaba). By working through these examples, you will learn to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of evidence and avoid the common error of treating Khabar al-Wahid as absolute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi premise
Recall that Hanafi usul classifies Khabar al-Wahid as zanni in both thubut (transmission) and dalalah (meaning). It can establish wujub (obligation) but cannot override a qat'i text such as a clear Quranic verse.
The Quranic principle that each prayer has a fixed time (Quran 4:103) is qat'i.
2
Analyze the tartib example
The hadith from Ibn 'Umar (narrated by al-Daraqutni) commands repeating a forgotten prayer after the current one. This establishes tartib as wajib. But when time is tight or many prayers are missed, enforcing tartib would conflict with the Quranic rule that prayers must be performed in their time. Therefore, the obligation of tartib is dropped.
Conflict arises because the hadith would require delaying prayers beyond their prescribed times.
3
Analyze the Hatim example
The hadith from 'A'isha (agreed upon) states that the Hatim is part of the Kaaba. This does not contradict any Quranic principle, so it is accepted. Consequently, tawaf must encompass the Hatim, making it wajib to include it in tawaf.
The original (asl) is that tawaf is around the Kaaba; the hadith clarifies its boundary.
4
Distinguish Sunnah from Wajib
The passage clarifies that Sunnah (the recommended path) is demanded without making it fard or wajib. Abandoning Sunnah deserves blame but does not require qada or dam. This contrasts with wujub from Khabar al-Wahid, which does require compensation if missed.
The Hanafi definition: Sunnah is a way we are commanded to revive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يفعل حتى طلع الفجر : سقطت الإعادة؛ لأن تأخير المغرب إنما وجب إلى وقت العشاء وقد انتهى وقت العشاء، فانتهى العمل، فلا يبقى الفساد من بعد إلا بالعلم، وخبر الواحد لا يوجبه، ولا يعارض حكم الكتاب، فلا يفسد العشاء. وكذلك الترتيب في الصلوات واجب، ثبت بخبر الواحد، فإذا ضاق الوقت، أو كثرت الفوائتُ، فصار معارضاً لحكم الكتاب بتغيير الوقتية : سقط العمل به. وثبت كونُ الحطيم من البيت بخبر الواحد، فجعلنا الطواف به واجباً، لا يعارض الأصل. وحكم السُّنَّة : أن يطالب المرء بإقامتها من غير افتراض، ولا وجوب ؛ لأنها طريقةً أمرنا بإحيائها، فنَستَحقُّ المَلامة بتركها.

(1) قوله : وكذلك الترتيب واجب بخبر الواحد هو ما أخرج الدارقطني عن ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : مَن نسي صلاة فلم يذكرها إلا وهو مع الإمام : فليتم صلاته، فإذا فرغ من صلاته فليعد الصلاة التي نسي، ثم ليُعد الصلاة التي صلاها مع الإمام.

(2) قوله : وثبت كون الحطيم من البيت بخبر الواحد: عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: «سألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الحجر أمن البيت هو؟ قال: نعم. الحديث متفق عليه. وفي رواية عنها: كنتُ أحب أن أدخل البيت أصلي فيه، فأخذ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بيدي فأدخلني الحجر، فقال صلي في الحجر إذا أردتِ دخول البيت، فإنما هو قطعة من البيت. رواه الخمسة إلا ابن ماجه، وصححه الترمذي.
If he does not do so until dawn breaks, the repeat is dropped; because delaying Maghrib is only obligatory until the time of Isha, and the time of Isha has ended, so the action ends, so corruption does not remain afterwards except by knowledge, and Khabar al-Wahid does not make it obligatory, and it does not contradict the ruling of the Book, so it does not invalidate Isha. Similarly, order in prayers is obligatory, established by Khabar al-Wahid. So when time becomes tight, or missed prayers become numerous, it becomes contradictory to the ruling of the Book by changing the temporality: so acting upon it is dropped. And it is established that the Hatim is from the House by Khabar al-Wahid, so we make tawaf around it obligatory, without contradicting the original. And the ruling of the Sunnah: that a person is to be demanded to perform it without obligation or necessity; because it is a way we are commanded to revive, so we deserve blame for abandoning it.

(1) His saying: 'Similarly order is obligatory by Khabar al-Wahid' is what al-Daraqutni narrated from Ibn 'Umar: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer and does not remember it except while he is with the Imam, let him complete his prayer, and when he finishes his prayer, let him repeat the prayer he forgot, then let him repeat the prayer he prayed with the Imam.'

(2) His saying: 'And it is established that the Hatim is from the House by Khabar al-Wahid' is from 'A'isha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about the Hijr: Is it part of the House? He said: Yes.' The hadith is agreed upon. And in another narration: 'I loved to enter the House and pray therein, so the Messenger of Allah took my hand and entered me into the Hijr, and said: Pray in the Hijr if you want to enter the House, for it is a piece of the House.' Narrated by the five except Ibn Majah, and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the use of Khabar al-Wahid (single-narrator hadith) in establishing rulings, and how it interacts with the Quran. The author, likely from the Hanafi school, presents two examples. First, the obligation of ordering (tartib) missed prayers is established by a Khabar al-Wahid. However, when time is tight or many prayers are missed, this order conflicts with the general Quranic principle that prayer is tied to its specific time (time-based obligation). In such conflict, the Khabar al-Wahid is dropped, because it cannot override the certainty of the Quran. Second, the Hatim (the semicircular wall next to the Kaaba) is established to be part of the Kaaba by Khabar al-Wahid. This does not conflict with any Quranic principle, so it is accepted and tawaf around it is made obligatory. The passage then defines the ruling of the Sunnah: it is demanded without making it fard or wajib, but its abandoner is blameworthy. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that Khabar al-Wahid can establish obligation (wujub) but yields to Quranic text when there is direct contradiction.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (Khabar al-Wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few narrators, providing zanni (probable) knowledge.
ترتيب (Tartīb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in order; established by Khabar al-Wahid.
الحطيم (al-Ḥaṭīm): The semicircular area adjacent to the Kaaba; established to be part of the Kaaba by Khabar al-Wahid.

Key Takeaway
Khabar al-Wahid is a valid source for wujub, but it must yield when it directly contradicts a qat'i text like the Quran.

Causes for Acts of Worship
Enumeration of causes for worship obligations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi cause for each act of worship (hajj, 'ushr, kharaj, taharah) and explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
Each worship obligation has a unique cause that determines its timing and validity.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul lays out the Hanafi theory of causes (asbab) for key acts of worship. Understanding these causes helps us know when obligations become due and why conditions are not the same as causes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause for hajj
Look for the sentence that mentions hijrah and visitation; the cause is the Kaaba itself.
2
Analyze the cause for 'ushr
The cause is the productive land, not the produce. Note the reasoning about advance payment.
3
Distinguish 'ushr from kharaj
Kharaj's cause is the land's potential productivity, not actual growth. Note the punishment element.
4
Understand the cause for taharah
The cause is the intention to pray, not impurity. Impurity is a condition, not a cause.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هجرة وزيارة، فكان البيت سبباً لها. وسبب وجوب العشر : الأرض النامية بحقيقة الخارج؛ لأن العشر يُنسب إلى الأرض، وفي العشر معنى مؤنة الأرض؛ لأنها أصل، وفيه معنى العبادة؛ لأن الخارج للسبب وصف، وصار السبب بتجدد وصفه متجدداً في التقدير، فلم يجز التعجيل قبل الخارج؛ لأن الخارج بمعنى السبب لوصف العبادة، فلو صح التعجيل لخلص معنى المؤنة، فلما صارت به الأرض ناميةً : أشبه تعجيل زكاة السائمة، والإبل العلوفة، ثم أسامها. وكذلك سبب الخراج، إلا أن النماء معتبر في الخراج تقديراً، لا تحقيقاً بالتمكن به من الزراعة فصار مؤنةً باعتبار الأصل، وعقوبة باعتبار الوصف؛ لأن الزراعة عمارة للدنيا، وإعراض عن الجهاد، فكان سبباً لضرب من المذلة، ولذلك لم يجتمعا عندنا. وسبب وجوب الطهارة الصلاة؛ لأنها تُنسب إليها، وتقوم بها، وهي شرطها، فتعلقت بها، حتى لم تجب قصداً، لكن عند إرادة الصلاة، والحدث شرطه بمنزلة سائر شروط الصلاة، ومن المحال أن يُجعل الحدث سبباً ، ألا يُرى أنه إزالة له وتبديل له، فلا يصلح سبباً له. وأما سبب الحدود والعقوبات فما تُنسب إليه من قتل، وزناً، وسرقة. وسبب الكفارات : ما نُسبت إليه من أمر دائر بين حظر وإباحة، مثل الفطر، وقتل الخاطئ، وقتل الصيد، واليمين، ونحوها. وقتل العمد واليمين الغموس وما أشبه ذلك: لا يصلح سبباً للكفارة، وتفسير ذلك يُذكر في موضعه إن شاء الله تعالى. وسبب المعاملات: تعلُّق البقاء المقدور بتعاطيها، والبقاء معلق بالنسل والكفاية، وطريقهما أسباب شرعية موضوعة للملك والاختصاص، والله أعلم.
Hijrah and visitation, thus the House (Kaaba) is the cause for it. And the cause for the obligation of tithe ('ushr): the productive land by actual produce; because the tithe is attributed to the land, and in the tithe there is the meaning of maintenance of the land because it is the origin, and in it there is the meaning of worship because the produce is for the cause as a description, and the cause becomes renewed in estimation due to the renewal of its description, so it is not permissible to pay in advance before the produce because the produce is in the sense of the cause due to the description of worship; if advance payment were valid, the meaning of maintenance would be isolated. When the land becomes productive through it, it resembles advance payment of the zakah of grazing livestock and fed camels, then their similar. And similarly the cause of land tax (kharaj), except that growth is considered in kharaj by estimation, not actual, by the ability to engage in agriculture, so it becomes maintenance in consideration of the origin and punishment in consideration of the description; because agriculture is cultivation of the world and turning away from jihad, so it became a cause for a kind of humiliation, and therefore they do not combine according to us. And the cause for the obligation of purification (taharah): prayer; because it is attributed to it, and it is established by it, and it is its condition, so it is attached to it, such that it is not obligatory in itself, but only when intending prayer. And the state of impurity (hadath) is its condition like other conditions of prayer, and it is impossible to make impurity a cause; do you not see that it is removal and alteration of it, so it cannot be a cause for it? As for the cause of prescribed punishments (hudud) and penalties: what they are attributed to of murder, adultery, and theft. And the cause of expiations (kaffarat): what they are attributed to from matters oscillating between prohibition and permission, such as breaking the fast, accidental killing, killing game, oaths, and the like. Intentional killing and the false oath (yamin ghamus) and similar: they cannot be causes for expiation, and its explanation will be mentioned in its place if Allah wills. And the cause of transactions (mu'amalat): the attachment of lasting subsistence that is within capability through their practice, and subsistence is linked to progeny and sufficiency, and their methods are Shariah-prescribed causes placed for ownership and exclusive right. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh discusses the concept of sabab (cause) in determining various obligations in Hanafi law. The author enumerates causes for different categories: hajj, 'ushr, kharaj, taharah, hudud, kaffarat, and mu'amalat. For each, he explains why that specific thing is the cause, often using reasoning (ta'lil). For 'ushr: the cause is productive land with actual growth because the 'ushr is technically attached to the land, and the produce is like the description. Advance payment is invalid because the cause must be realized. For kharaj: similarly, but growth is considered by estimation (potential productivity) rather than actual output, making it a punishment for engaging in worldly agriculture instead of jihad. For taharah: the cause is the intention to pray, not the state of impurity, because impurity is a condition that is removed. For hudud: the acts themselves (murder, adultery, theft) are the causes. For kaffarat: matters between prohibition and permission, such as breaking a fast or accidental killing; intentional aggression does not cause kaffarah. For mu'amalat: the cause is the attachment of subsistence through permissible transactions. The text emphasizes that each cause has a specific nature and cannot be conflated. This is a foundational Hanafi usul analysis.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The cause that triggers a legal obligation or ruling; e.g., the Kaaba for Hajj, the land for 'ushr.
العشر (al-'ushr): Tithe (10%) on agricultural produce, obligatory on Muslim-owned productive land.
الخراج (al-kharaj): Land tax on non-Muslim owned or conquered land, based on estimated productivity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the cause (land) is not yet productive
B) Because the owner might not harvest
C) Because the niṣāb is not reached
D) Because it resembles zakah on livestock

Key Takeaway
The cause (sabab) for each act of worship is distinct and must be correctly identified for the obligation to be valid.
