Causes for Hudud and Kaffarat
Enumeration of causes for hudud and kaffarat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the causes for hudud and kaffarat and identify which acts qualify as causes for expiation.

Core Idea
Hudud are caused by the prohibited acts themselves; kaffarat require acts oscillating between permission and prohibition.

This part of al-Bazdawi's text explains the causes for penal and expiatory obligations. Understanding these causes helps clarify when punishments apply and when expiation is required, especially in cases like accidental killing or breaking a fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause for hudud
The passage says the cause is what the punishment is attributed to: murder, adultery, theft.
These are the acts themselves.
2
Identify the cause for kaffarat
The cause is matters oscillating between prohibition and permission, like breaking a fast or accidental killing.
The nature must be intermediate, not purely aggressive.
3
Understand what is NOT a cause for kaffarah
Intentional killing (qatl al-'amd) and false oaths (yamin ghamus) are not causes because they are purely aggressive.
These are matters of punishment, not expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هجرة وزيارة، فكان البيت سبباً لها. وسبب وجوب العشر : الأرض النامية بحقيقة الخارج؛ لأن العشر يُنسب إلى الأرض، وفي العشر معنى مؤنة الأرض؛ لأنها أصل، وفيه معنى العبادة؛ لأن الخارج للسبب وصف، وصار السبب بتجدد وصفه متجدداً في التقدير، فلم يجز التعجيل قبل الخارج؛ لأن الخارج بمعنى السبب لوصف العبادة، فلو صح التعجيل لخلص معنى المؤنة، فلما صارت به الأرض ناميةً : أشبه تعجيل زكاة السائمة، والإبل العلوفة، ثم أسامها. وكذلك سبب الخراج، إلا أن النماء معتبر في الخراج تقديراً، لا تحقيقاً بالتمكن به من الزراعة فصار مؤنةً باعتبار الأصل، وعقوبة باعتبار الوصف؛ لأن الزراعة عمارة للدنيا، وإعراض عن الجهاد، فكان سبباً لضرب من المذلة، ولذلك لم يجتمعا عندنا. وسبب وجوب الطهارة الصلاة؛ لأنها تُنسب إليها، وتقوم بها، وهي شرطها، فتعلقت بها، حتى لم تجب قصداً، لكن عند إرادة الصلاة، والحدث شرطه بمنزلة سائر شروط الصلاة، ومن المحال أن يُجعل الحدث سبباً ، ألا يُرى أنه إزالة له وتبديل له، فلا يصلح سبباً له. وأما سبب الحدود والعقوبات فما تُنسب إليه من قتل، وزناً، وسرقة. وسبب الكفارات : ما نُسبت إليه من أمر دائر بين حظر وإباحة، مثل الفطر، وقتل الخاطئ، وقتل الصيد، واليمين، ونحوها. وقتل العمد واليمين الغموس وما أشبه ذلك: لا يصلح سبباً للكفارة، وتفسير ذلك يُذكر في موضعه إن شاء الله تعالى. وسبب المعاملات: تعلُّق البقاء المقدور بتعاطيها، والبقاء معلق بالنسل والكفاية، وطريقهما أسباب شرعية موضوعة للملك والاختصاص، والله أعلم.
Hijrah and visitation, thus the House (Kaaba) is the cause for it. And the cause for the obligation of tithe ('ushr): the productive land by actual produce; because the tithe is attributed to the land, and in the tithe there is the meaning of maintenance of the land because it is the origin, and in it there is the meaning of worship because the produce is for the cause as a description, and the cause becomes renewed in estimation due to the renewal of its description, so it is not permissible to pay in advance before the produce because the produce is in the sense of the cause due to the description of worship; if advance payment were valid, the meaning of maintenance would be isolated. When the land becomes productive through it, it resembles advance payment of the zakah of grazing livestock and fed camels, then their similar. And similarly the cause of land tax (kharaj), except that growth is considered in kharaj by estimation, not actual, by the ability to engage in agriculture, so it becomes maintenance in consideration of the origin and punishment in consideration of the description; because agriculture is cultivation of the world and turning away from jihad, so it became a cause for a kind of humiliation, and therefore they do not combine according to us. And the cause for the obligation of purification (taharah): prayer; because it is attributed to it, and it is established by it, and it is its condition, so it is attached to it, such that it is not obligatory in itself, but only when intending prayer. And the state of impurity (hadath) is its condition like other conditions of prayer, and it is impossible to make impurity a cause; do you not see that it is removal and alteration of it, so it cannot be a cause for it? As for the cause of prescribed punishments (hudud) and penalties: what they are attributed to of murder, adultery, and theft. And the cause of expiations (kaffarat): what they are attributed to from matters oscillating between prohibition and permission, such as breaking the fast, accidental killing, killing game, oaths, and the like. Intentional killing and the false oath (yamin ghamus) and similar: they cannot be causes for expiation, and its explanation will be mentioned in its place if Allah wills. And the cause of transactions (mu'amalat): the attachment of lasting subsistence that is within capability through their practice, and subsistence is linked to progeny and sufficiency, and their methods are Shariah-prescribed causes placed for ownership and exclusive right. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh discusses the concept of sabab (cause) in determining various obligations in Hanafi law. The author enumerates causes for different categories: hajj, 'ushr, kharaj, taharah, hudud, kaffarat, and mu'amalat. For each, he explains why that specific thing is the cause, often using reasoning (ta'lil). For 'ushr: the cause is productive land with actual growth because the 'ushr is technically attached to the land, and the produce is like the description. Advance payment is invalid because the cause must be realized. For kharaj: similarly, but growth is considered by estimation (potential productivity) rather than actual output, making it a punishment for engaging in worldly agriculture instead of jihad. For taharah: the cause is the intention to pray, not the state of impurity, because impurity is a condition that is removed. For hudud: the acts themselves (murder, adultery, theft) are the causes. For kaffarat: matters between prohibition and permission, such as breaking a fast or accidental killing; intentional aggression does not cause kaffarah. For mu'amalat: the cause is the attachment of subsistence through permissible transactions. The text emphasizes that each cause has a specific nature and cannot be conflated. This is a foundational Hanafi usul analysis.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments ordained by Allah for specific crimes.
الكفارات (al-kaffarat): Expiations for wrongdoings that are not considered major sins requiring fixed punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid cause for kaffarah according to the passage?
A) Breaking a fast due to travel
B) Accidental killing of a person
C) Theft (sariqah)
D) Breaking an oath (yamin)

Key Takeaway
Hudud are caused by pure prohibitions; kaffarat require acts with both prohibition and permission aspects.

Cause for Transactions
Statement of the cause for transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause for the permissibility of transactions (mu'amalat) and explain how it relates to human subsistence.

Core Idea
Transactions are permitted because they secure human subsistence, which is essential for survival.

Al-Bazdawi concludes his enumeration of causes with transactions (mu'amalat). He explains that the cause for their permissibility is the need for lasting subsistence. This connects economic activities to the higher maqasid of preserving life and progeny.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause for mu'amalat
The cause is the attachment of lasting subsistence (al-baqa') that is within human capability through engaging in transactions.
2
Understand the link to subsistence
Subsistence depends on progeny (nasl) and sufficiency (kifayah).
3
Recognize that the means are shariah-prescribed
The methods of transactions are laid down by the Shari'ah for ownership (milk) and exclusive right (ikhtisas).
This includes contracts like sale, lease, etc.

The Four Divisions of the Sunnah According to al-Bazdawi
Introduces the chapter on divisions of the Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four divisions of the Sunnah as outlined by al-Bazdawi and explain why the Sunnah is considered a branch of the Quran in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The Sunnah is the Quran's branch; its study divides into connection, disconnection, proof-context, and report-nature.

This lesson opens al-Bazdawi's chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah. The author reminds us that the Sunnah encompasses all categories of legal speech (command, prohibition, etc.) and serves as a branch of the Quran. He then introduces four distinct dimensions: how the Sunnah reaches us, how it may be disconnected, where it serves as proof, and the classification of the report itself. Understanding these divisions is foundational to Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching principle
Al-Bazdawi states that the Sunnah is a branch (far') of the Quran. It comprehensively covers all categories of legal discourse (amr, nahy, 'amm, khass) already discussed for the Quran.
This principle establishes the Quran as the primary source and the Sunnah as its explanatory branch.
2
List the four divisions
The author enumerates four distinct divisions: (1) how the Sunnah is connected to us from the Prophet, (2) disconnection in that connection, (3) the context in which a report is considered a proof, and (4) the classification of the report itself.
Memorize these four as the structural framework for the entire chapter.
3
Examine the first division's sublevels
Under connection, al-Bazdawi identifies three levels: complete connection without doubt (mutawatir), connection with doubt in form (e.g., ahad with strong chains), and connection with doubt in both form and meaning (e.g., weak reports).
The first level, mutawatir, is the subject of the next section and yields certain knowledge.
4
Note the role of mutawatir
Mutawatir is the highest level of connection, transmitting with certainty. It is free from any doubt and forms the foundation of definitive legal proofs from the Sunnah.
This sets the stage for comparing mutawatir with other categories like mashhur and ahad.
5
Connect to later lessons
This passage is a roadmap. Subsequent lessons will elaborate each division, especially the detailed conditions of mutawatir and other transmission categories.
Keep this overview in mind as we dive deeper into each division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب بيان أقسام السنة اعلم أن سُنّة النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام جامعة للأمر والنهي، والخاص والعام، وسائر الأقسام التي قد سبق ذكرها. وكانت السُّنَّةُ فرعاً للكتاب في بيان تلك الأقسام بأحكامها، فلا نعيدها، وإنما هذا الباب لبيان وجوه الاتصال وما يتصل بها فيما يفارق الكتاب، وتختص السنن به. وذلك أربعة أقسام : ١ - قسم في كيفية الاتصال بنا من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. ٢- وقسم في الانقطاع. ۳- وقسم في بيان محل الخبر الذي جعل حجةٌ فيه. ٤ - وقسم في بيان نفس الخبر. فأما الاتصال برسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام فعلى مراتب اتصال كامل، بلا شبهة فيه. - واتصال فيه ضرب شبهة صورةً. واتصال فيه شبهةً صورة ومعنى. * وأما المرتبة الأولى ، فهو المتواتر، وهذا باب المتواتر :
Chapter on the explanation of the divisions of the Sunnah. Know that the Sunnah of the Prophet, peace be upon him, encompasses command and prohibition, the specific and the general, and the rest of the divisions that have been previously mentioned. And the Sunnah was a branch of the Book in explaining those divisions with their rulings, so we do not repeat them. Rather, this chapter is to explain the aspects of connection and what relates to it regarding what differs from the Book and what is specific to the Sunnah. That is four divisions: (1) A division concerning the manner of connection to us from the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. (2) A division concerning disconnection. (3) A division concerning the explanation of the place of the report that is made a proof. (4) A division concerning the explanation of the report itself. As for the connection to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, it has levels: Complete connection with no doubt in it. - Connection with a type of doubt in form. Connection with doubt in form and meaning. And as for the first level, it is the mutawatir, and this is the chapter of mutawatir.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah. The author, Imam al-Bazdawi, first reminds us that the Sunnah encompasses all categories of speech (command, prohibition, general, specific) already discussed for the Quran. The Sunnah is a branch of the Quran in explaining these categories, so he won't repeat them. Instead, this chapter focuses on aspects unique to the Sunnah: how it reaches us (connection vs. disconnection), its authority (where it serves as proof), and its nature (the report itself). He then lists four divisions: (1) how the Sunnah is connected to us from the Prophet, (2) disconnection (e.g., mursal, munqati), (3) the context in which a report is considered proof, and (4) the report's own classification (e.g., mutawatir, ahad). For connection, he identifies three levels: complete connection without doubt (mutawatir), connection with doubt in form (e.g., ahad with strong chain but not mass transmitted), and connection with doubt in both form and meaning (e.g., weak reports). The first level is mutawatir, which he will elaborate in the coming section.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): The prophetic tradition including sayings, actions, and approvals, which is a source of law and a branch of the Quran.
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report transmitted by so many narrators at every level that collusion on falsehood is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.
الخبر (al-khabar): A report transmitted from the Prophet, which can be mutawatir or ahad, and is the subject of the fourth division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, how many divisions does the Sunnah have in this chapter?
A) Two divisions: mutawatir and ahad
B) Three divisions: mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad
C) Four divisions: connection, disconnection, place of proof, and nature of the report
D) Five divisions: command, prohibition, general, specific, and mutawatir

Key Takeaway
Al-Bazdawi divides the study of the Sunnah into four aspects: how it reaches us, its continuity, its authority context, and its intrinsic classification; with the highest level of connection being mutawatir.

Mutawatir: Definition, Conditions, and Epistemological Value
Definition and conditions of mutawatir with epistemological argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of mutawatir, identify its conditions, and distinguish between 'ilm al-yaqin and 'ilm tumaninah in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mutawatir reports produce certain, necessary knowledge like direct sight, not mere tranquility.

This lesson presents the Hanafi definition of mutawatir — reports transmitted by an uncountable multitude that precludes the possibility of collusion on a lie. These reports, such as the Quran and the daily prayers, yield certain knowledge (yaqin) that is necessary (daruri). The text also critiques those who deny knowledge from reports entirely and rejects the view that mutawatir only produces tranquility (tumaninah), arguing that such a view allows for doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The concept under definition is khabar mutawatir. Recognize that it is a type of report from the Prophet that conveys certainty.
2
List the conditions
From the text, extract the conditions: uncountable number of narrators, impossibility of collusion due to numbers, justice, geographical diversity, and continuity of these conditions throughout the chain.
Note that the text does not specify a fixed number; it says 'a group whose number cannot be counted'.
3
Examine the examples
The author gives examples: the Quran, the five daily prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, and the amounts of zakat. Understand that these are matters transmitted tawatur.
4
Understand the epistemological claim
The text states that mutawatir produces 'ilm al-yaqin (certain knowledge) that is daruri (necessary), comparing it to direct vision. This is the Hanafi position.
5
Contrast with opposing views
The author refutes two views: (1) those who deny all knowledge from reports (called foolish), and (2) those who say mutawatir yields only 'ilm tumaninah (tranquility) which allows for doubt. The latter argument is that mutawatir is an aggregate of ahad reports, each probable, so the aggregate remains probable.
The author implies this reasoning is flawed because the conditions of tawatur eliminate the possibility of collusion and error, transforming the epistemological status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المتواتر
الخبر المتواتر : الذي اتصل بك من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتصالاً بلا شُبهة، حتى صار كالمعاين المسموع منه.
وذلك بأن يرويه قومٌ لا يُحصى عددهم، ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب ؛ لكثرتهم، وعدالتهم وتباين أماكنهم، ويدوم هذا الحد، فيكون أوَّلُه كآخره، وآخره كأوله ، وأوسطه كطرفَيه.
وذلك مثلُ نقل القرآن والصلوات الخمس، وأعداد الركعات ومقادير الزكوات، وما أشبه ذلك.
وهذا القسم يوجب علم اليقين، بمنزلة العيان علماً ضرورياً.
ومن الناس من أنكر العلم بطريق الخبر أصلاً .
وهذا رجلٌ سفيه، لم يعرف نفسه، ولا دينه ولا دنياه، ولا أُمَّه ولا أباه مثل من أنكر العيان.
وقال قوم: إن المتواتر يوجب علمَ طُمأنينة، لا يقين، ومعنى الطمأنينة عندهم : ما يحتمل أن يتخالجه شك، أو يَعتريَه وَهُمْ.
وقالوا : لأن المتواتر صار جمعاً ،بالآحاد، وخبر كل واحد منهم محتمل، والاجتماعُ يحتمل التواطؤ، وذلك كإخبار المجوس قصة
Chapter on Mutawatir. The mutawatir report is that which reaches you from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, with connection without any doubt, until it becomes like something seen and heard directly from him. That is because it is narrated by a group whose number cannot be counted, and it is not imagined that they could collude on a lie due to their large number, their justice, and the diversity of their places; and this condition persists so that the first is like the last, and the last like the first, and the middle like the sides. That is like the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'ahs, the amounts of zakat, and similar things. This type produces knowledge of certainty, in the position of direct vision, as necessary knowledge. Among people are those who denied knowledge through reports entirely. This is a foolish man, who does not know himself, nor his religion, nor his worldly life, nor his mother, nor his father, like one who denies direct sight. And some people said that mutawatir produces knowledge of tranquility, not certainty, and the meaning of tranquility according to them is that which a doubt can enter or a suspicion can affect. They said: because mutawatir is a collection of ahad reports, and the report of each one of them is probable, and the collection can possibly be collusion, like the report of the Magians of a story...
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage defines mutawatir and its conditions. The author states that mutawatir is a report transmitted continuously from the Prophet without any doubt, to the point that it feels like direct observation. The conditions include: narrators whose number is uncountable, it is impossible to imagine they would collude on a lie due to their large number, justice, and geographical dispersion; and this condition must hold throughout the entire chain. Examples include the Quran, the five daily prayers, the number of rak'ahs, and zakat amounts. Such reports produce certain knowledge ('ilm al-yaqin) that is necessary (daruri), like direct sight. The author harshly refutes those who deny knowledge from reports entirely, calling them foolish. He also addresses a milder opposing view that mutawatir yields 'ilm tumaninah (tranquility) rather than certainty, which allows for potential doubt. Their argument is that mutawatir is composed of ahad reports, each subject to uncertainty, and the combination could involve collusion. This view is implied to be incorrect according to the author.

Key Terms
خبر متواتر (khabar mutawatir): A report that reaches the listener from the Prophet with complete connection without doubt, as if witnessed directly
علم اليقين (ilm al-yaqin): Certain knowledge that excludes all possibility of doubt
علم ضروري (ilm daruri): Necessary knowledge that is self-evident, not acquired through reasoning
علم طمأنينة (ilm tumaninah): Knowledge of tranquility that may admit doubt or suspicion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what kind of knowledge does a mutawatir report produce?
A) Knowledge of tranquility ('ilm tumaninah)
B) Certain knowledge ('ilm al-yaqin) that is necessary (daruri)
C) Probable knowledge (zann)
D) Knowledge of direct vision (ayn al-yaqin)

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir reports produce certain necessary knowledge and are a foundational source in Hanafi usul.

Definition and Epistemic Status of Khabar Mutawatir
Defines mutawatir and argues it yields certain knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar mutawatir, enumerate its conditions, and explain why the Hanafi school holds it yields necessary certain knowledge ('ilm al-yaqin al-daruri) like direct observation.

Core Idea
Mutawatir report yields certain knowledge because its conditions make fabrication impossible.

This passage defines khabar mutawatir, the highest category of transmitted reports in Hanafi usul. The author lays out precise conditions—uncountable narrators, impossibility of collusion, persistence—and argues it produces 'ilm al-yaqin al-daruri, equivalent to seeing with your own eyes. He then refutes those who claim it only gives tuma'nina (reassurance), using both commonsense examples and rational analysis.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition and conditions
Identify the precise wording: 'that which reaches you from the Messenger without any doubt, until it becomes like direct observation.' List the conditions: uncountable number, impossibility of collusion due to numbers, uprightness, diverse locations, and persistence throughout the chain.
The definition includes both the effect (like direct observation) and the conditions.
2
Identify the epistemological effect
Note the claim: 'This category necessitates the knowledge of certainty, like direct observation, as necessary knowledge.' Understand that this is the Hanafi position—mutawatir gives yaqin not merely zann.
This is the core of the Hanafi usul position on mutawatir.
3
Understand the opposing view and its evidence
The opponents (some mutakallimun) say mutawatir gives only tuma'nina (reassurance), not certainty. Their evidence: each individual report is probable (zanni), and a collection of probabilites can still be fabricated (like Zoroaster or Jesus crucifixion stories).
Note how they use counterexamples to challenge the certainty claim.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response via wad' and tahqiq
The author uses two methods: (1) wad' (commonsense analogy): e.g., we know our fathers through reports just as we know our children by sight; (2) tahqiq (rational analysis): agreement among diverse upright people can only be from hearing, not fabrication. The counterexamples are not true mutawatir because they fail the conditions.
This is the Hanafi proof that mutawatir yields yaqin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المتواتر
الخبر المتواتر : الذي اتصل بك من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتصالاً بلا شُبهة، حتى صار كالمعاين المسموع منه.
وذلك بأن يرويه قومٌ لا يُحصى عددهم، ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب ؛ لكثرتهم، وعدالتهم وتباين أماكنهم، ويدوم هذا الحد، فيكون أوَّلُه كآخره، وآخره كأوله ، وأوسطه كطرفَيه.
وذلك مثلُ نقل القرآن والصلوات الخمس، وأعداد الركعات ومقادير الزكوات، وما أشبه ذلك.
وهذا القسم يوجب علم اليقين، بمنزلة العيان علماً ضرورياً.
ومن الناس من أنكر العلم بطريق الخبر أصلاً .
وهذا رجلٌ سفيه، لم يعرف نفسه، ولا دينه ولا دنياه، ولا أُمَّه ولا أباه مثل من أنكر العيان.
وقال قوم: إن المتواتر يوجب علمَ طُمأنينة، لا يقين، ومعنى الطمأنينة عندهم : ما يحتمل أن يتخالجه شك، أو يَعتريَه وَهُمْ.
وقالوا : لأن المتواتر صار جمعاً ،بالآحاد، وخبر كل واحد منهم محتمل، والاجتماعُ يحتمل التواطؤ، وذلك كإخبار المجوس قصة زرادشت(۱) اللعين، وإخبار اليهود صَلبَ عيسى عليه السلام).
وهذا قول باطل، نعوذ بالله من الزيغ بعد الهدى، بل المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين ضرورةً بمنزلة العيان ،بالبصر والسمع بالأذن، وضعاً وتحقيقاً.
أما الوضع فإنا نجد المعرفة بآبائنا بالخبر : مثل المعرفة بأولادنا عياناً، ونجد المعرفة بأنا مولودون نشأنا عن صغر: مثل معرفتنا به في أولادنا، ونجد المعرفة بجهة الكعبة خبراً : مثل معرفتنا بجهة منازلنا سواء. وأما التحقيق: فلأن الخَلق خُلقوا على هِمَم متفاوتة، وطبائع متباينة، لا تكاد تقع أمورهم إلا مختلفةً، فلما وقع الاتفاق : كان ذلك لداع إليه، وهو سماع، أو اختراع وبطل الاختراع؛ لأن تباين الأماكن، وخروجهم عن الإحصاء مع العدالة : يقطع الاختراع، فتعين الوجه الآخر.
والطمأنينة على ما فسره المخالف إنما تقع بغفلة من المتأمل، لو تأمل حقّ تأمله : لوضح له فساد باطنه، فلما اطمأن بظاهره : كان أمراً.

(۱) باب المتواتر قوله : وأما أخبار زَرَادُشت... إلى آخره: نقل الحافظ أبو محمد ابن حزم في كتاب الملل والنَّحَل له اختلاف أهل الإسلام في نبوة زَرادشت، وحينئذ لا يَضُرُّ ما نُقل عنه وإن تواتر، والله أعلم.
(۲) قوله : وإخبار اليهود قلت: روى ابن إسحاق أنهم جعلوا للدال جعلاً ثلاثين ،درهماً، وكذا أخرجه ابن جرير، ومثل هذا لا يصدر عن جمع لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب، وقد روى القصة ابن أبي حاتم عن ابن عباس بسند صحيح، ورواها النسائي وابن جرير، ولم يتعرض أحد منهم لعدة اليهود، والله أعلم.
Chapter on Mutawatir. The khabar mutawatir: that which reaches you from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ with a connection without any doubt, until it becomes like direct observation and hearing from him. And that is that a group of people narrate it, whose number cannot be counted, and it is inconceivable that they would collude upon falsehood, due to their large number, their uprightness, and the diversity of their locations; and this condition persists, so that its beginning is like its end, and its end is like its beginning, and its middle like its extremities. And that is like the transmission of the Quran, the five prayers, the numbers of rak'at, the amounts of zakat, and similar matters. This category necessitates the knowledge of certainty, like direct observation, as necessary knowledge. Some people deny knowledge through khabar entirely. And this person is a fool, who does not know himself, nor his religion, nor his world, nor his mother nor his father, like one who denies direct observation. And some people said: that mutawatir necessitates the knowledge of reassurance (tuma'nina), not certainty; and the meaning of tuma'nina with them is: that which is susceptible to doubt creeping into it, or illusion affecting it. And they said: because mutawatir is a collection of individuals (ahad), and the report of each one of them is probable (muhtamil), and the collection is susceptible to collusion, such as the report of the Magians of the story of the accursed Zoroaster, and the report of the Jews of the crucifixion of Jesus (peace be upon him). And this is a false statement. We seek refuge in Allah from deviation after guidance. Rather, mutawatir necessitates the knowledge of certainty by necessity, like direct observation with sight and hearing with the ear, both by placement and by verification. As for placement (wad'), we find that knowledge of our fathers through report is like knowledge of our children through direct observation; and we find that knowledge of our being born and having grown up from childhood is like our knowledge of it in our children; and we find that knowledge of the direction of the Ka'ba through report is like our knowledge of the direction of our houses. As for verification (tahqiq): because people are created with varying ambitions and diverse natures; their affairs rarely happen except differently. So when agreement occurs, it is due to a cause that calls to it, which is either listening (samā') or fabrication (ikhtirā'). And fabrication is invalidated because the diversity of places and their being beyond count combined with uprightness cuts off fabrication. So the other aspect is established. And tuma'nina as explained by the opponent only occurs due to negligence of the contemplator; if he had contemplated properly, the corruption of its interior would have become clear to him. So when he felt reassured by its exterior, it became a matter... (1) Chapter on Mutawatir: his statement: "And as for the reports of Zoroaster..." etc.: Al-Hafiz Abu Muhammad Ibn Hazm in his book Al-Milal wa al-Nihal transmitted that the people of Islam differ on the prophethood of Zoroaster. And then what is transmitted about him, even if mutawatir, does not harm. And Allah knows best. (2) His statement: "And the report of the Jews": I say: Ibn Ishaq narrated that they gave a reward of thirty dirhams for the [fabrication]. And similarly Ibn Jarir transmitted it. And such a thing would not be committed by a group about whom collusion on lying is inconceivable. And Ibn Abi Hatim narrated the story from Ibn Abbas with a sound chain, and al-Nasa'i and Ibn Jarir also narrated it, and none of them mentioned the number of Jews. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage defines khabar mutawatir and discusses its epistemological status. The author first defines mutawatir as a report transmitted from the Prophet through a chain free from doubt, such that it is like seeing and hearing directly. The conditions include: a large number of narrators (uncountable), impossibility of collusion due to their numbers, uprightness, diverse locations, and persistence of these conditions throughout the chain. Examples include the Quran, five daily prayers, etc. The ruling is that mutawatir gives necessary knowledge of certainty ('ilm al-yaqin daruri), equivalent to direct observation. The author then refutes two opposing views: (1) those who deny knowledge from reports entirely (called safih/fool), and (2) those who claim mutawatir gives only 'ilm tuma'nina (reassurance), which is susceptible to doubt. This latter group argues by analogy: mutawatir is a collection of ahad reports, each probable, and collection can involve collusion, referencing reports of Zoroaster and Jewish crucifixion narratives. The author rejects this as false, arguing by two methods: by wad' (commonsense analogy) and by tahqiq (rational analysis). For wad': we know our fathers through reports just as we know our children by sight; we know our birth through reports; we know Ka'ba direction through reports like our homes. For tahqiq: human beings naturally differ; if many diverse upright people agree on a report, fabrication is impossible, so the only explanation is true hearing. The author concludes that tuma'nina is due to negligence. The footnotes clarify that (1) the prophethood of Zoroaster is disputed, so that report does not harm the claim; (2) the Jewish report was incentivized, thus not from a trustworthy group.

Key Terms
الخبر المتواتر (al-khabar al-mutawatir): الخبر الذي اتصل بك من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتصالاً بلا شبهة حتى صار كالمعاين المسموع منه، بشرط رواية قوم لا يحصى عددهم ولا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب
علم اليقين ('ilm al-yaqin): العلم الجازم الذي لا يحتمل النقيض، وهو حاصل من المتواتر ضرورة
علم الضرورة ('ilm al-darura): العلم الذي يضطر إليه الإنسان ولا يمكنه دفعه، كالعيان
طمأنينة (tuma'nina): ما يحتمل أن يتخالجه شك أو يعتريه وهم، وهو دون اليقين
وضعاً وتحقيقاً (waḍ'an wa taḥqīqan): الوضع: الاستدلال بالعادات المشهودة. والتحقيق: الاستدلال العقلي بتحليل السبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Khabar mutawatir, when meeting all conditions, yields necessary certain knowledge, establishing the Quran and Sunnah as definitive sources.

Mutawatir Reports Produce Certain Knowledge Through Evidence
Arguing that mutawatir gives certain knowledge based on evidence, not heedlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi proof that mutawatir reports yield certain knowledge (yaqin) based on evidence (dalil), and distinguish it from knowledge arising from heedlessness (ghafla).

Core Idea
Mutawatir gives certainty because fabrication is impossible; evidence, not heedlessness, grounds this certainty.

This passage from Kanz al-Wusul tackles a foundational epistemological question in Hanafi usul: what is the basis of certainty from mass-transmitted reports? The opponent claims our acceptance is due to heedlessness, similar to instantly recognizing a funeral gathering. The author refutes this, demonstrating that mutawatir knowledge is compelled by rational evidence—the impossibility of collusion among a large, diverse, trustworthy group. Understanding this proof is essential for establishing the binding authority of the Quran and Sunnah as certain sources of Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
The passage contrasts certain knowledge (al-‘ilm al-yaqini) from mutawatir with probable knowledge from heedlessness. Note the author's claim that mutawatir knowledge is 'akin to direct observation' (bi-manzilat al-‘iyan).
This sets up the opponent's challenge and the Hanafi response.
2
Analyze the two-part Hanafi proof
First, linguistic convention (al-wad‘): we know our fathers through reports as certainly as we know our children by sight. Second, verification (al-tahqiq): when a large group with diverse natures and locations agree on a report, fabrication is impossible, so truth is confirmed.
The verification argument is the core rational proof.
3
Examine the opponent's claim and the Hanafi refutation
The opponent argues that tranquility (tuma'nina) from mutawatir arises from heedlessness (ghafla), like instantly recognizing a funeral gathering. The author counters that this applies only to probable matters; for mutawatir, the outward form confirms the inner meaning, and contemplation only strengthens certainty.
The funeral example shows the difference between psychological comfort and rational proof.
4
Apply the proof to the Sahaba and the Quran
The Companions were many, trustworthy, and widely dispersed; their agreement on the Quran precludes fabrication. The Quran’s inimitability (i‘jaz) further confirms its truth. This makes the Quran’s transmission certain (qat‘i).
This illustrates the practical thamarah al-khilaf: the Quran and Sunnah are certain sources of law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زرادشت اللعين، وإخبار اليهود صلب عيسى عليه السلام. وهذا قول باطل، نعوذ بالله من الزيغ بعد الهدى، بل المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين ضرورةً بمنزلة العيان، بالبصر والسمع بالأذن، وضعاً وتحقيقاً. أما الوضع فإنا نجد المعرفة بآبائنا بالخبر مثل المعرفة بأولادنا عياناً، ونجد المعرفة بأنا مولودون نشأنا عن صغر مثل معرفتنا به في أولادنا، ونجد المعرفة بجهة الكعبة خبراً مثل معرفتنا بجهة منازلنا سواء. وأما التحقيق: فلأن الخلق خلقوا على همم متفاوتة، وطبائع متباينة، لا تكاد تقع أمورهم إلا مختلفةً، فلما وقع الاتفاق كان ذلك لداع إليه، وهو سماع، أو اختراع وبطل الاختراع؛ لأن تباين الأماكن، وخروجهم عن الإحصاء مع العدالة يقطع الاختراع، فتعين الوجه الآخر. والطمأنينة على ما فسره المخالف إنما تقع بغفلة من المتأمل، لو تأمل حق تأمله لوضح له فساد باطنه، فلما اطمأن بظاهره كان أمراً محتملاً، فأما أمر يؤكد باطنه ظاهره، ولا يزيده التأمل إلا تحقيقاً فلا، كالداخل على قوم جلسوا للمأتم يقع له العلم به عن غفلة عن التأمل، ولو تأمل حق تأمله لوضح له الحق من الباطل. وأما العلم بالمتواتر فإنما يجب عن دليل أوجب علماً بصدق المخبر به؛ لمعنى في الدليل، لا بغفلة من المتأمل. وصحابة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورضي الله عنهم كانوا قوماً عدولاً، أئمةً لا يُحصى عددهم ولا تتفق أماكنهم، طالت صحبتهم، واتفقت كلمتهم من بعد ما تفرقوا شرقاً وغرباً، وهذا يقطع الاختراع، ولما تصور الخفاء مع بعد الزمان. ولهذا صار القرآن معجزة؛ لأنهم عجزوا عن ذلك، واشتغلوا ببذل الأرواح، فكان خبرهم في نهاية البيان قاطعاً احتمال الوضع، يقيناً بلا شبهة، إذ لو كان فيه شبهة وضع لما خفي مع كثرة الأعداء، واختلاط أهل النفاق، قال الله تعالى: {وفيكم سمعون لهم} التوبة/٤٧. وذلك مثل سلامة كتاب الله تعالى عن المعارضة، وعجز البشر عن ذلك، إذ لو كان ذلك لما خفي مع كثرة المتعنتين، وهذا مثله. فأما أخبار زرادشت فتخييل كله.
Zoroaster the accursed, and the reports of the Jews about the crucifixion of Jesus (peace be upon him). And this is a false statement; we seek refuge with Allah from deviation after guidance. Rather, the mutawatir (mass-transmitted report) necessitates certain knowledge necessarily, akin to direct observation, through sight and hearing, both in terms of linguistic convention and verification. As for linguistic convention: we find that knowledge of our fathers through reports is like knowledge of our children through direct observation, and we find knowledge that we were born and grew up from childhood is like our knowledge of that regarding our children, and we find knowledge of the direction of the Kaaba through reports is like our knowledge of the direction of our homes, the same. As for verification: because people were created with varied aspirations and diverse natures; their affairs hardly occur except differing. So when agreement occurs, it must be due to a cause that calls for it, which is either hearing or fabrication. And fabrication is invalidated because the diversity of places and their being beyond enumeration, combined with trustworthiness, precludes fabrication; thus the other aspect is confirmed. And the tranquility (طمأنينة) according to the opponent's interpretation only occurs due to heedlessness on the part of the contemplator. If he contemplated properly, the corruption of its inner meaning would become clear to him. So when he is at ease with its outward meaning, it becomes a probable matter. As for a matter that confirms its inner meaning by its outward meaning, and contemplation only increases its certainty, then it is not so, like one who enters upon a group sitting for a funeral; he obtains knowledge of it through heedlessness of contemplation, and if he contemplated properly, the truth would become clear to him from falsehood. And as for knowledge through mutawatir, it is only necessitated by evidence that obligates knowledge of the truth of the informant, due to a meaning in the evidence, not through heedlessness of the contemplator. And the Companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and may Allah be pleased with them, were trustworthy people, leaders whose number cannot be counted and whose places do not all agree; their companionship was long, and their word was united after they had dispersed east and west. And this precludes fabrication, and concealment was impossible with the passage of time. And for this reason the Quran became a miracle; because they were incapable of that, and they occupied themselves with sacrificing their lives. So their report was at the extreme of clarity, cutting off the possibility of fabrication, certainty without doubt. For if there were any doubt of fabrication, it would not have been concealed despite the multitude of enemies and the intermixing of hypocrites. Allah Almighty said: {And among you are those who listen to them} (At-Tawbah 9:47). And that is like the safety of the Book of Allah from opposition, and the inability of humans to do that; for if it were otherwise, it would not have been hidden despite the multitude of obstinate people. And this is similar. As for the reports of Zoroaster, they are all delusion.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul argument on the epistemological certainty of mutawatir (mass-transmitted) reports. The author begins by dismissing false claims about Zoroaster and the crucifixion of Jesus, then asserts that mutawatir yields certain knowledge akin to direct observation. The proof is twofold: (1) by linguistic convention (al-wad‘), we compare our knowledge of ancestors through reports to our knowledge of our own children by sight, and similarly for direction of the Kaaba; (2) by verification (al-tahqiq), he argues that when a large group of people with diverse natures and locations agree on a report, it cannot be due to collusion (fabrication), so it must be truthful. He then refutes the opponent (al-mukhalif) who says that such knowledge comes from heedlessness (ghafla). The author gives the example of entering a funeral gathering: one immediately knows it from context without deep thought, but this is not the same as mutawatir knowledge, which is based on evidence (dalil). He then applies this to the Sahaba (Companions) — their large number, widespread locations, trustworthiness, and agreement after dispersion precludes fabrication, and the Quran’s inimitability confirms its truth. The verse from Surah al-Tawbah (9:47) is cited to show that despite hypocrites, the truth of the Prophet’s message was preserved. The passage concludes that reports of Zoroaster are mere fantasy.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawatir): A mass-transmitted report that yields certain knowledge by virtue of the impossibility of collusion on falsehood.
علم اليقين (al-‘ilm al-yaqini): Certain knowledge that is indubitable, akin to seeing with one's own eyes.
طمأنينة (tuma'nina): A sense of tranquility or assurance that the opponent claims comes from heedlessness, not evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the knowledge from mutawatir differ from the tranquility felt when seeing a funeral gathering?
A) Because mutawatir involves many narrators.
B) Because mutawatir's certainty is based on evidence and grows with contemplation.
C) Because funeral gatherings are not reported.
D) Because mutawatir requires trustworthiness.

Key Takeaway
Mutawatir reports produce certain knowledge through rational evidence that fabrication is impossible, not through heedlessness.

The Mashhur Report: Definition and Authority
Defining the mashhur report and its evidentiary value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the mashhur report, distinguish it from mutawatir, and state the Hanafi ruling on denying a mashhur report.

Core Idea
A mashhur report is a binding proof like mutawatir, but its denier is misguided, not a disbeliever.

In this passage, al-Bazdawi defines the second category of khabar in Hanafi usul: the mashhur (well-known) report. Unlike mutawatir, which begins with multiple chains, mashhur starts as a single-chain (ahad) but later gains widespread acceptance. The author also presents an intra-madhhab debate about the consequence of rejecting such a report, settling on the view that the denier is led astray (yudallal) but not rendered a disbeliever (la yukaffar).

Guided Path
1
Identify the defining features of mashhur
The passage states that mashhur originally begins as an ahad (single-chain) report. Subsequently, it becomes widely transmitted by trustworthy narrators from the second Islamic century onward, such that collusion on lying is impossible.
Note the contrast with mutawatir: mutawatir requires multiple chains from the very start.
2
Note its evidentiary value
Through the thiqat and a'imma transmitters, the report becomes like mutawatir in authority—it is a hujjah (proof) from among the proofs of Allah. However, its epistemological certainty is considered slightly lower than mutawatir.
This is why the consequence of denial differs.
3
Understand the intra-madhhab dispute
Al-Jassas considered mashhur as one of two divisions of mutawatir, which would imply that denying it is kufr. Isa ibn Aban held that the denier is only misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever. The text declares Isa ibn Aban's view as the correct (sahih) position.
The tarjih is based on the fact that mashhur does not reach the absolute certainty of mutawatir in transmission.
4
Apply the distinction to examples
The hadith of wiping over khuffs (mas-h) is given as a prime example of mashhur. The passage lists numerous chains from Sahaba and the Six Books to demonstrate its widespread transmission, yet it is not mutawatir because it originated as ahad.
Another example is the hadith of stoning (rajm).
5
Derive the practical consequence
The practical thamarah (fruit) of this usul distinction: a person who denies a mashhur report like mas-h is not declared a kafir but is considered misguided. This prevents the serious charge of takfir while maintaining the binding nature of the report.
In contrast, denying a mutawatir report would lead to kufr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المرتبة الثانية فهو المشهور، وهذا باب المشهور من الأخبار:
المشهور: ما كان من الآحاد في الأصل، ثم انتشر، فصار ينقله قوم لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب وهم القرن الثاني بعد الصحابة رضي الله عنهم ومن بعدهم، وأولئك هم قوم ثقات أئمةٌ لا يتهمون، فصار بشهادتهم وتصديقهم بمنزلة المتواتر، حجةً من حجج الله تعالى.
حتى قال الجصاص رحمه الله : إنه أحد قسمي المتواتر.
وقال عيسى بن أبان رحمه الله : إن المشهور من الأخبار يُضلَّلُ جاحده، ولا يُكفر. مثل حديث المسح على الخفين وحديث الرجم، وهو الصحيح.
أما المسح : فروي من حديث جرير والمغيرة بن شعبة وبريدة، أخرجها الستة، ومن حديث سعد بن أبي وقاص وعمرو بن أمية أخرجهما البخاري، ومن حديث حذيفة ،وبلال أخرجهما ،مسلم ومن حديث صفوان أخرجه الترمذي والنسائي وابن ماجه وحديث خزيمة عند أبي داود والترمذي وابن ماجه، وحديث ثوبان عند أبي داود وحديث أسامة عند النسائي وحديث عمر بن الخطاب عند ابن ماجه، وحديث أبي بن عمارة عند أبي داود وابن ماجه وحديث سهل بن سعد الساعدي وأنس بن مالك أخرجهما ابن ماجه وحديث عائشة أخرجه النسائي في «الكبرى»، وحديث أبي هريرة عند أحمد، وحديث أبي أيوب عند إسحاق بن راهويه. وحديث أبي بكرة والبراء بن عازب وأبي عوسجة وأبي طلحة وأبي أمامة وعبادة =
As for the second rank, it is the mashhur. This is the chapter on mashhur reports. The mashhur: it is that which was originally ahad (isolated), then became widespread, such that it came to be transmitted by a people about whom it is not imagined that they collude in lying. They are the second generation after the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and those after them. Those are trustworthy people, imams who are not accused. So through their testimony and confirmation, it becomes like the mutawatir, a proof from among the proofs of Allah Almighty. Until al-Jassas, may Allah have mercy on him, said: It is one of the two divisions of mutawatir. And Isa ibn Aban, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The denier of mashhur reports is led astray but not rendered a disbeliever. Examples include the hadith of wiping over the khuffs and the hadith of stoning (Rajm). This is the correct view. As for wiping: it is narrated from Jarir, al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba, and Buraydah; the six (canonical books) transmitted it. And from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and Amr ibn Umayyah; al-Bukhari transmitted both. And from Hudhayfah and Bilal; Muslim transmitted both. And from Safwan; al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah transmitted it. And the hadith of Khuzaymah is with Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah. And the hadith of Thawban is with Abu Dawud. And the hadith of Usamah is with al-Nasa'i. And the hadith of Umar ibn al-Khattab is with Ibn Majah. And the hadith of Ubayy ibn 'Imarah is with Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah. And the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi and Anas ibn Malik; both are transmitted by Ibn Majah. And the hadith of 'Aisha is transmitted by al-Nasa'i in al-Kubra. And the hadith of Abu Hurayrah is with Ahmad. And the hadith of Abu Ayyub is with Ishaq ibn Rahawayh. And the hadith of Abu Bakrah, al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, Abu 'Awsajah, Abu Talhah, Abu Umamah, and 'Ubadah =
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage defines the second category of khabar (report) in the Hanafi classification of hadith: the mashhur (well-known). The author first distinguishes it from the mutawatir by noting that mashhur begins as an ahad report (single-chain) but later becomes widely transmitted by trustworthy narrators from the second Islamic century onward. Such narrators are reliable imams, and their collective transmission elevates the report to a level of certainty similar to mutawatir, making it a binding proof (hujjah). However, the passage highlights an intra-madhhab disagreement: al-Jassas considered mashhur to be one of two divisions of mutawatir, implying that denying it would be kufr. In contrast, Isa ibn Aban held the view that the denier of a mashhur report is misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever (la yukaffar). The text declares this latter view to be the correct (sahih) position. Two examples of mashhur reports are given: the hadith on wiping over leather socks (khuffs) during ablution and the hadith on stoning for adultery (rajm). The author then lists extensive narrations for the wiping hadith to demonstrate its widespread transmission. This classification is practical: it determines the legal consequence for rejection.

Key Terms
مشهور (mashhur): A report that was originally ahad (single-chain) but later became widely transmitted by trustworthy narrators, giving it a status similar to mutawatir in authority.
تضليل (tadlil): To declare someone misguided (but not a disbeliever) for rejecting a mashhur report.
متواتر (mutawatir): A report transmitted by a large number of narrators at every level, making collusion on lying impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who denies a mashhur hadith (e.g., the hadith of wiping over khuffs)?
A) He becomes a disbeliever (kafir).
B) He is led astray (yudallal) but not a disbeliever.
C) He is considered a sinner but still a believer.
D) He is not held accountable because the hadith is ahad.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a mashhur report is a binding proof whose denier is declared misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever (la yukaffar).

Definition and Authority of Mashhur Hadith
Defining mashhur hadith and its legal authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mashhur hadith, distinguish it from mutawatir and ahad, and explain its legal authority in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Mashhur is a proof for action, like mutawatir, but does not yield certain knowledge.

In Hanafi usul, the classification of hadith into mutawatir, mashhur, and ahad is foundational. This lesson unpacks the definition of mashhur, its relation to mutawatir and ahad, and what legal effects it carries—especially its role in abrogating Quranic rulings and its epistemological weight. Understanding this tripartite division is key to grasping how Hanafi scholars weigh evidence.

Guided Path
1
Break down the definition of mashhur
Read the Arabic definition phrase by phrase: 'ما كان من الآحاد في الأصل، ثم انتشر، فصار ينقله قوم لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب' – note the three phases: originally solitary, then spread, then transmitted by a group whose collusion is inconceivable. Identify each element.
The definition is carefully constructed to distinguish mashhur from both ahad and mutawatir.
2
Compare mashhur with mutawatir and ahad
Contrast the three categories: ahad (solitary transmission), mashhur (originally ahad but later widespread), mutawatir (continuous multitude from the start). Use the text's mention of al-Jassas classifying mashhur as a division of mutawatir to explore the nuance.
Mashhur shares the later widespread transmission with mutawatir but differs in its origin.
3
State the legal authority of mashhur
The text says it becomes 'حجةً من حجج الله تعالى' – a proof among Allah's proofs. Explain that it is a proof for action (hujja li'l-‘amal) but not for certain knowledge (yaqin). Cite the phrase 'لما كان في الأصل من الآحاد: ثبت به شبهة، فسقط به علم اليقين'.
This epistemic limitation is crucial: mashhur yields speculative knowledge (zann) but is binding in practice.
4
Apply to the examples given
The text mentions three examples: wiping over socks, stoning for adultery, and consecutiveness in fasting for oath expiation. Show how each is a mashhur hadith that adds to or abrogates a Quranic ruling. Trace the reasoning: because mashhur is like mutawatir in practical proof, addition/abrogation is valid.
These examples illustrate the practical impact of the mashhur category in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Explain the ruling on the denier
The text states 'يُضلَّلُ جاحده، ولا يُكفر' – the denier is misguided but not a disbeliever. Explain why: mashhur does not reach the level of certain knowledge, so rejection does not entail kufr, but it is a grave error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المشهور من الأخبار
المشهور: ما كان من الآحاد في الأصل، ثم انتشر، فصار ينقله قوم لا يتوهم تواطؤهم على الكذب وهم القرن الثاني بعد الصحابة رضي الله عنهم ومن بعدهم، وأولئك هم قوم ثقات أئمةٌ لا يتهمون، فصار بشهادتهم وتصديقهم بمنزلة المتواتر، حجةً من حجج الله تعالى.
حتى قال الجصاص رحمه الله : إنه أحد قسمي المتواتر.
وقال عيسى بن أبان رحمه الله : إن المشهور من الأخبار يُضلَّلُ جاحده، ولا يُكفر. مثل حديث المسح على الخفين وحديث الرجم، وهو الصحيح عندنا؛ لأن المشهور بشهادة السلف صار حجةً للعمل به كالمتواتر فصحت الزيادة به على كتاب الله تعالى، وهو نسخ عندنا.
وذلك مثل حديث زيادة الرجم والمسح على الخفين، والتتابع في صيام كفارة اليمين لكنه لما كان في الأصل من الآحاد: ثبت به شبهة، فسقط به علم اليقين ولم يستقم اعتباره في العمل، فاعتبرناه في العمل؛ لأنا لا نجد وسعاً في رد المتواتر.
وإنما يَشك فيه صاحب الوسواس.
Chapter on the Well-Known (Mashhur) Reports. The mashhur is: what was originally ahad (isolated), then spread, so that it is transmitted by a group whose collusion upon lying is not conceivable, and they are the second generation after the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, and those after them. Those are trustworthy people, imams, not accused. Thus, by their testimony and affirmation, it becomes like the mutawatir, a proof from among the proofs of Allah Almighty. So much so that al-Jassas (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is one of the two divisions of mutawatir. And Isa ibn Aban (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The denier of mashhur reports is misguided, but not disbelieved, such as the hadith of wiping over the socks and the hadith of stoning. This is the correct view with us; because the mashhur, by the attestation of the predecessors, became a proof for action like the mutawatir, so addition (to the Quran) by it is valid, and it is abrogation with us. That is like the hadith of adding stoning and wiping over the socks, and the consecutiveness (tawabi') in fasting the expiation of an oath. But because it was originally from the ahad, a doubt (shubha) is established by it, so certainty of knowledge falls, and it is not valid to consider it in action; so we considered it in action; because we find no room to reject the mutawatir. Only the one afflicted by doubt (waswas) doubts it.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage introduces the concept of mashhur (well-known) hadith in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author defines mashhur as a report that was originally khabar al-wahid (a solitary report) but later became widespread to the extent that it is transmitted by a group whose collusion on falsehood is impossible, similar to mutawatir. However, mashhur differs from mutawatir in thubut (establishment) because it started as ahad. The text notes that al-Jassas considered mashhur a division of mutawatir, while Isa ibn Aban ruled that the denier of a mashhur hadith is misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever (yukaffar). This ruling is affirmed as the correct position in the Hanafi school. The legal effect of mashhur is that it acts as a proof (hujja) in practical matters, equivalent to mutawatir, but it does not yield certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin). Consequently, mashhur can be used to add a ruling to the Quran, effectively abrogating (naskh) the Quranic text in the view of the Hanafis, as seen in the examples of stoning for adultery (rajm) and wiping over socks (mas'h ala al-khuffayn). The text also mentions the hadith of consecutiveness in fasting for the expiation of an oath. The phrase 'due to doubt' indicates that mashhur cannot override certain knowledge from the Quran. The passage concludes that only a person with severe doubt (waswas) would reject a mashhur hadith.

Key Terms
المشهور (al-mashhur): A hadith that was originally ahad but later became widely transmitted by a group whose collusion on falsehood is not conceivable, thus achieving the status of a proof for action but not certain knowledge.
الآحاد (al-ahad): A report transmitted by one or two transmitters initially, not reaching the level of tawatur; it does not yield certain knowledge.
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A report transmitted by so many transmitters that collusion on falsehood is impossible, yielding certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal status of the denier of a mashhur hadith in the Hanafi school?
A) He becomes a disbeliever (kafir).
B) He is considered misguided (yudallal) but not a disbeliever.
C) He is considered a sinner but remains a believer.
D) He is punished with ta'zir.

Key Takeaway
Mashhur hadith is a proof for action, like mutawatir, but does not yield certain knowledge; its denier is misguided, not a disbeliever.

8 min
Authority of Mashhur Hadith in Hanafi Usul
Establishes mashhur as hujjah for 'amal, distinguishing its epistemic level.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the mashhur hadith from mutawatir and ahad in terms of epistemic authority, and apply the Hanafi rule that mashhur can abrogate the Quran.

Core Idea
The mashhur hadith has the authority of mutawatir for action but yields only knowledge of tranquility, not certainty.

In this passage, the Hanafi school establishes the intermediate category of mashhur hadith, which is neither fully certain like mutawatir nor merely speculative like ahad. The key is the testimony of the Salaf (early community) who accepted and acted upon it, giving it the weight to even abrogate a Qur'anic ruling. This distinction is crucial for understanding how Hanafis derive law from prophetic traditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the threefold classification
The passage divides hadith into three ranks: mutawatir (certain), mashhur (between), and khabar al-wahid (speculative). Understand each rank's definition and epistemic level as outlined in the text.
2
Locate the Hanafi claim about mashhur
The claim is that mashhur, by the testimony of the Salaf, becomes a proof for action (hujjah li al-'amal) like mutawatir, and can even add to or abrogate the Qur'an. Focus on the phrase 'fasaht al-ziyada bihi 'ala kitab Allah ta'ala'.
3
Examine the epistemic distinction
The passage explains that mashhur yields 'ilm al-tuma'nina (knowledge of tranquility), not 'ilm al-yaqin (certain knowledge), because its origins are from ahad, creating a doubt that prevents certainty.
4
Note the examples provided
The hadith of stoning (rajm), wiping over socks (mas'h), and consecutive fasting for expiation (tawatur in kaffarah) are cited as mashhur traditions that abrogate or add to Qur'anic rulings. Consider how these illustrate practical application of the rule.
5
Trace the proof structure
The author uses the practice of the Salaf (their acceptance and action) as the evidence for the authority of mashhur, drawing an analogy to mutawatir. Reflect on how this proof combines rational inference (jima' of Salaf) with transmitted examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عندنا؛ لأن المشهور بشهادة السلف صار حجةً للعمل به كالمتواتر فصحت الزيادة به على كتاب الله تعالى، وهو نسخ عندنا. وذلك مثل حديث زيادة الرجم والمسح على الخفين، والتتابع في صيام كفارة اليمين لكنه لما كان في في الأصل من الآحاد: ثبت به شبهة، فسقط به علم اليقين ولم يستقم اعتباره في العمل، فاعتبرناه في العمل؛ لأنا لا نجد وسعاً في رد المتواتر. وإنما يَشك فيه صاحب الوسواس. وعبد الرحمن بن بلال وعبد الله بن رواحة وعبد الرحمن بن حسنة وعمرو بن حزم الله بن عمر ويعلى بن مرة عند الطبراني وحديث أبي برزة وابن عباس وعوف وعبد الملك بن مالك وابن مسعود وجابر عند البزار وكذا حديث ابن مسعود وحديث مالك بن سعد ومالك بن ربيعة عند أبي نعيم في «الصحابة»، وحديث أوس الثقفي عند ابن أبي شيبة، وحديث يسار عند العقيلي في «الضعفاء». وأما الرجم: فعن عمر رجم رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، ورجمنا بعده متفق عليه، وسيأتي في النسخ ص ٤٩٨ بأتم من هذا. وروي من حديث عبادة عند مسلم وأبي داود والترمذي، ومن حديث وائل بن حجر عند أبي داود والترمذي، ومن حديث النعمان بن بشير عند أبي داود والترمذي والنسائي، ومن حديث بريدة عند مسلم وأبي داود ومن حديث جابر عند أبي داود، ومن حديث عمران بن حصين عند مسلم وأبي داود والترمذي والنسائي، ومن حديث أبي هريرة وزيد بن خالد الجهني متفق عليه، ولأبي هريرة حديث آخر عند أبي داود، ومن حديث ابن أبي أوفى متفق عليه ومن حديث علي عند البخاري، ومن حديث ابن عمر عند البخاري وأبي داود. ونَحْرج في رد المشهور؛ لأنه لا يمتاز عن المتواتر إلا بما يَشقُ دَركُه، لكن العلم بالمتواتر كان لصدق في نفسه، فصار يقيناً، والعلم بالمشهور؛ لغفلة عن ابتدائه، وسكون إلى حاله، فسمي علمَ طُمأنينة، والأول علم يقين، والله أعلم. وأما المرتبة الثالثة: فهو خبر الواحد، وهذا باب خبر الوحد
According to us: because the mashhur, by virtue of the testimony of the Salaf, became a proof for action like the mutawatir, so addition by it to the Book of Allah is valid, and it is abrogation according to us. That is like the hadith of adding stoning and wiping over leather socks, and consecutiveness in fasting the expiation of an oath. But since it was originally from ahad, a doubt was established by it, so the knowledge of certainty fell away, and its consideration was not sound in action? So we considered it in action? For we do not find room to reject the mutawatir. And only the one with waswas doubts it. And [the hadith of] Abd al-Rahman ibn Bilal, Abdullah ibn Rawaha, Abd al-Rahman ibn Hasana, Amr ibn Hazm, [the hadith of] Allah ibn Umar, Ya'la ibn Murra reported by al-Tabarani, and the hadith of Abu Barza, Ibn Abbas, Awf, Abd al-Malik ibn Malik, Ibn Mas'ud, Jabir reported by al-Bazzar, and likewise the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and the hadith of Malik ibn Sa'd, Malik ibn Rabi'a reported by Abu Nu'aym in 'al-Sahaba', and the hadith of Aws al-Thaqafi reported by Ibn Abi Shayba, and the hadith of Yasar reported by al-Uqayli in 'al-Du'afa'. As for stoning: from Umar: The Messenger of Allah stoned, and we stoned after him, agreed upon. And it will come in the section on abrogation p.498 more completely than this. And it is narrated from the hadith of Ubada by Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi; from the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi; from the hadith of al-Nu'man ibn Bashir by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i; from the hadith of Burayda by Muslim, Abu Dawud; from the hadith of Jabir by Abu Dawud; from the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn by Muslim, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i; from the hadith of Abu Hurayra and Zayd ibn Khalid al-Juhani, agreed upon; and Abu Hurayra has another hadith by Abu Dawud; from the hadith of Ibn Abi Awfa, agreed upon; from the hadith of Ali by al-Bukhari; from the hadith of Ibn Umar by al-Bukhari and Abu Dawud. And we are reluctant to reject the mashhur; because it is not distinguished from the mutawatir except by what is difficult to perceive. But knowledge of the mutawatir was due to its truth in itself, so it became certainty; and knowledge of the mashhur is due to ignorance of its beginning and tranquility with its state, so it is called knowledge of tranquility, and the first is knowledge of certainty. And Allah knows best. As for the third rank: it is khabar al-wahid, and this is the chapter of khabar al-wahid.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul discussion on the classification of hadith and the authority of mashhur. The author establishes that according to the Hanafi school, the mashhur hadith (one that was narrated by two or more but not reaching mutawatir in the first generation, then became widespread) is a proof for action, just like mutawatir. Therefore, such a hadith can add to the Quran and even abrogate a Quranic ruling. Examples given are the hadith of stoning for adultery, wiping over leather socks, and the requirement of consecutive fasting for expiation of an oath. The author notes that since these hadiths originated as ahad, they introduce a level of doubt, so they do not produce certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin). Yet, we accept them for practice because rejecting them would require rejecting mutawatir, which is not permissible. The author then lists numerous narrators for the stoning hadith to show its wide transmission. The passage also explains that the knowledge from mutawatir is certain (yaqin) because it is based on truth itself, while the knowledge from mashhur is called 'ilm al-tuma'nina (knowledge of tranquility) because its initial transmission may not have been known, but it has been accepted by the community. Finally, the author signals that the next topic is khabar al-wahid, the third rank of hadith.

Key Terms
المشهور (al-mashhur): A hadith that was narrated by three or more in the first generation but did not reach mutawatir, then became widely known and accepted by the community.
المتواتر (al-mutawatir): A hadith narrated by such a large number that it is impossible they all agreed on a lie; it yields certain knowledge.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or by a number that is insufficient to reach the degree of mashhur; it yields speculative knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Hanafi school accept the authority of mashhur hadith for action?
A) Because it is mutawātir.
B) Because of the testimony of the Salaf.
C) Because it is narrated by only one person.
D) Because it is from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The mashhur hadith, though epistemically lower than mutawatir, is legally authoritative for action (including abrogation) due to the consensus and practice of the early community.

Definition and Epistemic Status of Khabar al-Wahid
Defines Khabar al-Wahid and its legal probative value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khabar al-wahid according to the Hanafi school, distinguish its epistemic status from mutawatir and mashhur, and evaluate the opposing views on whether it necessitates action and/or knowledge.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid necessitates action but not certain knowledge — a cornerstone of Hanafi legal epistemology.

In this passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul, we encounter the Hanafi classification of reports (akhbar). After mutawatir and mashhur, the third rank is khabar al-wahid — a report that does not reach the level of mass transmission. The central question is: what legal and epistemic weight does such a report carry? The Hanafi school takes a nuanced position that balances practical obligation with epistemic humility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its definition
Locate the Arabic phrase that defines khabar al-wahid in the source text. Note the key elements: number of narrators, relationship to mashhur and mutawatir.
The definition hinges on being 'less than mashhur and mutawatir'.
2
Extract the Hanafi epistemic ruling
Find the sentence that states the Hanafi position on whether khabar al-wahid necessitates action and knowledge. Note the term 'عندنا' (according to us).
The ruling is: يوجب العمل ولا يوجب العلم اليقين.
3
Analyze the first opposing view
Identify the group that denies khabar al-wahid necessitates action, their proof (Quran 17:36), and their rational argument about the Lawgiver's power.
This group argues that action requires knowledge, and khabar al-wahid does not give knowledge.
4
Analyze the second opposing view
Identify the group (some hadith scholars) that claims khabar al-wahid necessitates certain knowledge, their evidence (action requires knowledge, and its use in afterlife matters).
They point to ahad hadith on punishment of the grave and seeing Allah.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi response and practical consequence
Consider why the Hanafi school holds the middle position: action is required based on predominant opinion (zann) in practical matters, while for afterlife matters tranquility (tuma'ninah) suffices.
The practical result: a single-narrator hadith is binding for fiqh rulings but does not produce certainty of knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المرتبة الثالثة : فهو خبر الواحد، وهذا باب خبر الوحد

باب خبر الواحد
وهو الفصل الثالث من القسم الأول.
وهو كل خبر يرويه الواحد، أو الاثنان فصاعداً، لا عبرة للعدد فيه
بعد أن يكون دون المشهور والمتواتر.
وهذا يوجب العمل، ولا يوجب العلم يقيناً عندنا.
و
وقال بعض الناس : لا يوجب العمل ؛ لأنه لا يوجب العلم، ولا عمل إلا عن علم، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا نَقْفُ مَا لَيْسَ لَكَ بِهِ عِلْمُ ﴾ الإسراء /٣٦. وهذا لأن صاحب الشرع موصوف بكمال القدرة، فلا ضرورة له في التجاوز عن دليل يوجب علم اليقين.
بخلاف المعاملات؛ لأنها من ضروراتنا.
وكذلك الرأي من ضروراتنا، فاستقام أن يثبت غير علم اليقين.
وقال بعض أهل الحديث : إنه يوجب علم اليقين؛ لما ذكرنا أنه أوجب العمل، ولا عمل من غير علم.
وقد ورد الآحاد في أحكام الآخرة، مثل عذاب القبر، ورؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار، ولا حظ لذلك إلا العلم.
As for the third rank: it is khabar al-wahid, and this is the chapter of khabar al-wahid.

Chapter of khabar al-wahid
It is the third section of the first division.
It is every report narrated by one person, or two or more, with no consideration of number after being less than mashhur and mutawatir.
This necessitates action, but does not necessitate certain knowledge in our view.
And some people said: it does not necessitate action because it does not necessitate knowledge, and there is no action except with knowledge, Allah the Exalted said: {And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge} (al-Isra 17:36). This is because the Lawgiver is described with complete power, so there is no need for Him to go beyond a proof that necessitates certain knowledge.
Contrary to transactions because they are among our necessities.
Likewise opinion (al-ra'y) is among our necessities, so it is appropriate that something other than certain knowledge is established.
And some hadith scholars said: it necessitates certain knowledge because it necessitates action, and there is no action without knowledge.
And indeed ahad hadith have been transmitted concerning rulings of the afterlife, such as the punishment of the grave and seeing Allah Most High with eyes, and there is no scope for that except knowledge.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage defines Khabar al-Wahid and its epistemic status according to the Hanafi school. The author introduces khabar al-wahid as the third rank of reports after mutawatir and mashhur. It is defined as any report narrated by one or more people that does not reach the level of mashhur or mutawatir in terms of number of narrators at every level. The key ruling: such a report necessitates action (yūjibu al-ʿamal) but does not produce certain knowledge (lā yūjibu al-ʿilm al-yaqīn). The Hanafi position distinguishes between practical obligation and epistemic certainty. The author then presents two opposing views. First, some people (likely referring to a group of theologians or jurists) argue that khabar al-wahid does not even necessitate action because it does not yield knowledge, citing the Quranic verse 'Do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' (17:36). Their reasoning: the Lawgiver is all-powerful and has no need to rely on uncertain proofs when certain proofs are available; unlike worldly transactions which require practical rulings based on majority opinion (al-ra'y) due to necessity, religious rulings should be based on certainty. Second, some hadith scholars (ahl al-ḥadīth) claim that khabar al-wahid does yield certain knowledge because it obligates action, and action cannot be based on mere conjecture. They point to the use of ahad hadith for matters of the unseen (like punishment in the grave and seeing Allah), which cannot be known except through certain knowledge. The Hanafi school maintains the middle position: action is required based on zann (predominant opinion) but absolute certainty is not attained. The mention of 'aḥadīth āḥād' for afterlife matters is presented as the hadith scholars' proof; Hanafis respond that such reports produce tranquility of the heart (ṭumaʾnīnah) rather than logical certainty, which suffices for belief and action in those matters.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A report narrated by one or more persons (up to less than mashhur) that does not reach the level of tawatur, and which necessitates action but not certain knowledge in the Hanafi view.
المتواتر (al-mutawātir): A report narrated by such a large number at every level that it is impossible for them to have conspired on a lie; it yields certain knowledge.
المشهور (al-mashhūr): A report initially narrated by one or two in the first generation but later becoming widely known; it yields tranquility (ṭumaʾnīnah) but not certainty.
العلم (al-ʿilm): Certain knowledge (yaqīn) that admits no doubt; the highest epistemic category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the epistemic and practical status of khabar al-wahid?
A) It necessitates both action and certain knowledge (ʿilm yaqīn).
B) It necessitates action but not certain knowledge; it produces zann.
C) It does not necessitate action because it does not produce knowledge.
D) It necessitates knowledge but not action.

Key Takeaway
Khabar al-wahid is binding for action in practical legal matters but does not produce certain knowledge — a key distinction in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Acting upon Ahad Hadith: The Practice of the Sahaba
Evidence of Sahaba acceptance of ahad hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain how the Sahaba's acceptance of isolated hadith (al-ahad) provides a precedent for the Hanafi position on the authority of ahad hadith in non-creedal legal matters.

Core Idea
The Sahaba routinely accepted single-narrator reports in legal rulings, establishing the precedent for ahad hadith as binding proof.

This lesson presents a general overview of the evidence from the practice of the Companions (Sahaba) demonstrating that they acted upon isolated hadith (akhbar al-ahad) in numerous legal rulings. The examples include inheritance, jizya, and waiting periods. The Hanafi school uses this historical precedent to justify the acceptance of ahad hadith as binding proof in non-creedal matters. The passages from the source text provide multiple narrations that serve as dalil (evidence) for this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching claim
The author asserts that the Sahaba acted upon isolated hadith and argued with them, and that this practice is too abundant and famous to require exhaustive enumeration.
The claim is a foundational premise in Hanafi usul.
2
Survey the examples provided
The text lists several historical incidents: the grandmother's inheritance under Abu Bakr and 'Umar, the jizya from Magians, the plague of Syria, and the waiting period of Furay'a bint Malik. Skim through each to see the common pattern.
Pay attention to the number of witnesses in each case.
3
Analyze the common pattern
In each case, a single narrator (e.g., Mughira ibn Shu'ba, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf) reports a ruling from the Prophet, and the Caliph acts upon it, sometimes after requesting a second witness but ultimately accepting the solitary report when corroborated or when no contradiction exists.
The request for a second witness is for extra caution (ihtiyat), not because a single report is insufficient.
4
Extract the usul principle
The consistent practice of the Sahaba indicates that ahad hadith are valid and binding in legal matters, provided the narrator is reliable. This supports the Hanafi doctrine that ahad hadith (with proper conditions) constitute hujja (proof) for fiqh rulings.
This principle contrasts with the Shafi'i requirement for multiple chains in some contexts, but the Hanafi rely on the Sahaba precedent.

Commentary
This passage provides extensive historical evidence that the Companions (Sahaba) of the Prophet ﷺ acted upon isolated hadith (akhbar al-ahad). The author first notes that such examples are too numerous and too famous to require exhaustive enumeration. The core argument is: if the Sahaba themselves accepted single-person reports in matters of law (such as inheritance, jizya, and waiting period), then later scholars are justified in doing so. The examples cited include: (1) Abu Bakr accepting the testimony of Mughira ibn Shu'ba and Muhammad ibn Maslama regarding the grandmother's sixth share, initially requiring two witnesses but ultimately acting upon a single report combined with another; (2) 'Umar accepting the testimony of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf alone regarding the Magians' jizya; (3) 'Umar accepting 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf's solitary report about the plague and the prohibition of entering an afflicted land. Additionally, the story of Furay'a bint Malik illustrates the Prophet's own ruling based on a single narration. All these examples demonstrate that the Sahaba did not require multiple witnesses or chains for every report; rather, they acted upon ahad hadith when they deemed them reliable. The footnote from Kitab al-Istihsan further elaborates that 'Umar's request for additional witnesses was for precaution (ihtiyat), not because a single witness was insufficient. Thus, the Hanafi position that ahad hadith are valid and binding is firmly rooted in the practice of the early community.

Key Terms
الآحاد (al-ahad): isolated or single-narrator hadith, as opposed to mutawatir
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): a method of legal reasoning preferring a ruling due to equity or necessity, often based on a hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because he did not accept solitary testimony at all.
B) Because he wanted to be extra cautious (ihtiyat), not because the solitary report was invalid.
C) Because he wanted to test the memory of the first witness.
D) Because the grandmother was a woman.

Key Takeaway
The Sahaba's consistent acceptance of solitary reports provides a strong precedent for the Hanafi position that ahad hadith are binding proof in legal matters.
