فإن روى عنه السلفُ، وشهدوا له بصحة الحديث: صار حديثه مثل حديث المعروف بشهادة أهل المعرفة. وإن سكتوا عن الطعن فيه بعد النقل فكذلك؛ لأن السكوت. وأما سلمة بن المُحبَّق، واسم المحبَّق صخر، فأخرج له الطبراني عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في رجل وقع على جارية امرأته : إن كان استكرهها : فهي حرة، وعليه لسيدتها مثلها، وإن كانت طاوعته فهي له ولها عليه مثلها». رواه النسائي وأبو داود. وأخرج عنه أيضاً أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان في سفر، فأتى على قربة معلقة، فاستقى، فقيل : ميتةً، فقال : ذكاة الأديم دباغه»، وأخرجه النسائي وأبو داود. وأخرج عنه أيضاً أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعث ببدنتين مع رجل، فقال: أشعرهما من منحرهما». الحديث، ورواه أحمد. وأخرج أيضاً قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَن كانت له حمولة، ويأوي إلى شبَع ورِيّ : فليصم رمضان حيث أدركه»، ورواه أبو داود. وعنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مرَّ يوم خيبر بقدورٍ فيها لحم حُمُر الناس، فأمر بها، فأكفئت». رواه أحمد، وعنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «البكر بالبكر جلد مائة، ونفي سنة». رواه أحمد. وحديث : أرأيت لو وجدت مع امرأتك رجلاً». رواه ابن ماجه. وهذا خلاف ما يُذكر عنهما، والله ولي الإعانة. وأما معقل بن سنان فروى النسائي عنه أنه قال : مرَّ علي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأنا أحتجم في اثنتي عشرة ليلة خلت من رمضان، فقال: أفطر الحاجم والمحجوم». وعنه : أنه قال لعبد الله بن مسعود: قضى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بروع بنت واشق امرأة منا مثل ما قضيت». رواه الخمسة، وصححه الترمذي. موضع الحاجة إلى البيان: بيان ، ولا يُتّهم السلف بالتقصير. ٤ - وإن اختلف فيه مع نقل الثقات عنه : فكذلك عندنا، مثل حديث معقل بن سنان أبي محمد الأشجعي في حديث بروع بنت واشق الأشجعية أنه مات عنها زوجها هلالُ بن أبي مُرَّة، ولم يكن فَرَضَ لها مهراً، ولا دخل بها، فقضى لها رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بمهر مثل نسائها. فعَمِل بحديثه(۱) عبد الله بن مسعود رضي الله عنه، ورده علي رضي الله عنه لما خالف رأيه، وقال: «ما نصنعُ بقول أعرابي بوال على عقبيه (۲) ولم يعمل الشافعي رحمه الله بهذا القسم ؛ لأنه خالف القياس عنده. (۱) قوله : عَمِل به ابن مسعود : يفسره ما تقدم، وقد أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة، وفيه: فما رأيت ابن مسعود فرح بشيء ما فرح يومئذ به. (۲) قوله : وردَّه علي لما خالف رأيه، وقال ما نصنع بقول أعرابي بوال على عقبيه : لم أقف عليه بهذا اللفظ، وإنما أخرج عبد الرزاق عن الحكم بن عتيبة: «أن علياً كان يجعل لها الميراث، وعليها العدة، ولا يجعل لها صداقاً». قال الحكم وأخبر بقول ابن مسعود، فقال: لا نُصدَّقُ الأعراب على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأخرجه ابن أبي شيبة ثنا ابن عيينة عن عمرو وعطاء بن السائب عن عبد خيرٍ يرى أنه عن علي قال لها الميراث، ولا صداق لها. ثنا أبو معاوية عن الشيباني عن عمرو بن مرة عمن أخبره عن علي قال لها الميراث، ولا صداق لها.
If the Salaf (early Muslims) transmitted from him and attested to the authenticity of his hadith, his hadith becomes like the hadith of one known through the testimony of knowledgeable people. And if they remained silent about criticizing him after transmission, it is the same; because silence... And as for Salamah ibn al-Muhabbaq, his name is Sakhr, al-Tabarani narrated from him that the Prophet ﷺ said concerning a man who had intercourse with his wife's slave-girl: if he coerced her, she is free and he owes her mistress her like, and if she consented, she is his and he owes her mistress her like. Narrated by al-Nasa'i and Abu Dawud. Also from him that the Prophet ﷺ was on a journey and came upon a water skin hanging, so he drank, and it was said: it is dead, so he said: the purification of skin is tanning. Narrated by al-Nasa'i and Abu Dawud. Also from him that the Prophet ﷺ sent two sacrificial animals with a man and said: mark them at their humps. Narrated by Ahmad. Also from him: whoever has a mount and can find satiety and drink, let him fast Ramadan wherever he reaches it. Narrated by Abu Dawud. Also from him that the Prophet ﷺ passed by pots containing donkey meat on the day of Khaybar and ordered them to be overturned. Narrated by Ahmad. Also from him that the Prophet ﷺ said: the virgin with the virgin receives 100 lashes and exile for a year. Narrated by Ahmad. And the hadith: 'Do you see if you found a man with your wife?' Narrated by Ibn Majah. This contradicts what is mentioned about them, and Allah is the Helper. And as for Ma'qil ibn Sinan, al-Nasa'i narrated from him that he said: the Prophet ﷺ passed by me while I was cupping on the twelfth night of Ramadan and said: the cupper and the cupped break fast. And from him that he said to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet ﷺ judged in the case of Barwa' bint Washiq, a woman from us, as you judged. Narrated by the five, authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. The place of need for clarification is clarification, and the Salaf are not accused of falling short. And if there is disagreement about him while trustworthy narrators transmit from him, it is the same with us, like the hadith of Ma'qil ibn Sinan Abu Muhammad al-Ashja'i concerning Barwa' bint Washiq al-Ashja'iyya that her husband Hilal ibn Abi Murra died without having set a dowry for her or consummated, and the Prophet ﷺ judged for her the like dowry of her peers. So Abdullah ibn Mas'ud acted on his hadith, and Ali rejected it when it opposed his opinion, saying: 'What do we do with the statement of a Bedouin who urinates on his heels?' And al-Shafi'i did not act on this category because it contradicts analogy in his view. (1) Note: He acted on it - Ibn Mas'ud - is explained previously, and it was narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba, in it: I never saw Ibn Mas'ud so happy with anything as he was that day. (2) Note: Ali rejected it when it opposed his opinion, saying 'What do we do with the statement of a Bedouin who urinates on his heels?' I did not find it in this wording, rather Abd al-Razzaq narrated from al-Hakam ibn Utayba that Ali gave her inheritance and made her observe iddah but did not give her a dowry. Al-Hakam said: Then he was informed of Ibn Mas'ud's statement, and he said: We do not trust Bedouins regarding the Messenger of Allah. And Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Ibn Uyayna from Amr and Ata ibn al-Sa'ib from Abd Khayr who thinks it is from Ali: She has inheritance and no dowry. Also from Abu Muawiya from al-Shaybani from Amr ibn Murra from one who informed him that Ali said: She has inheritance and no dowry.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul discusses two related rules for accepting hadith from narrators whose reliability is not explicitly known. The first rule: if the Salaf (the early generation, especially the Companions and Successors) narrated from a narrator and explicitly attested to the authenticity of his hadith, then his hadith is treated like that of a well-known trustworthy narrator. Even if they remain silent about him after transmitting his hadith, their silence is considered approval because the Salaf would not remain silent about a weak narrator if they knew of his weakness — they were meticulous. This is a Hanafi principle: the Salaf's tacit acceptance is sufficient. The passage then lists several hadith narrated by Salamah ibn al-Muhabbaq as examples (though these are illustrative for biographical purposes, the main legal point is the principle). The second rule (point 4): if there is disagreement among scholars about a narrator (some accepting him, some rejecting) but trustworthy narrators have transmitted from him, then his hadith is also accepted according to the Hanafis. As evidence, the author cites the case of Ma'qil ibn Sinan's hadith about Barwa' bint Washiq, where Ibn Mas'ud acted upon it while Ali rejected it, saying: 'We do not take a Bedouin's statement against the Prophet.' The Hanafis side with Ibn Mas'ud because the hadith was transmitted by trustworthy narrators, and the mere opposition of qiyas (analogical reasoning) does not disqualify it. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, rejects this category because it contradicts qiyas in his view. The footnotes provide additional textual verification for the reports. The core lesson is that Hanafi usul prioritizes the transmission of the Salaf and their implicit endorsement over personal reasoning when the narrator is not positively challenged.

Key Terms
السلف (al-salaf): The early generation of Muslims, primarily the Companions and Successors, whose practice and testimony are authoritative
نقل الثقات (naql al-thiqāt): Transmission by trustworthy narrators whose reliability is established
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning used to derive legal rulings from established sources

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if the Salaf transmit from a narrator but remain silent about him?
A) His hadith is rejected because silence indicates weakness.
B) His hadith is accepted like that of a known narrator because their silence implies approval.
C) His hadith is accepted only if at least two Salaf attest to his authenticity.
D) His hadith requires additional scrutiny from later scholars.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, transmission by trustworthy narrators (explicit or implicit Salaf approval) makes a hadith acceptable even if the narrator is disputed and even if it contradicts qiyas.

Authority of Khabar al-Wahid and Its Categories
Defining authority of khabar al-wahid and its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify khabar al-wahid into mustankar and mustatir based on the reaction of the early generations and apply the rule that it is hujja only when it conforms to qiyas.

Core Idea
A khabar al-wahid is hujja only if it conforms to qiyas and was not rejected by the salaf.

In this passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh, we explore the Hanafi classification of single-narrator hadith (khabar al-wahid). The key to its authority is not just authenticity, but conformity to established principles (qiyas) and the stance of the early generations (salaf). Understanding this distinction is essential for proper istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and scope of khabar al-wahid
A report that does not reach the level of tawatur or shuhra; its authority is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
This is the default category for most hadith.
2
State the Hanafi rule for its authority
Khabar al-wahid is hujja (proof) if it conforms to qiyas; if it contradicts qiyas, it is rejected.
The text emphasizes 'عندنا هو حجة؛ لأنه وافق القياس'.
3
Distinguish between mustankar and mustatir
Mustankar: the hadith became known but the salaf explicitly rejected it, so it is not acted upon when it contradicts qiyas. Mustatir: the hadith did not become known and was neither accepted nor rejected; acting upon it is permissible but not obligatory.
The key is the salaf's reception, not just the chain.
4
Recognize the epistemological value
Mutawatir gives certainty (ilm al-yaqin), mashhur gives tranquility (ilm al-tuma'nina), khabar al-wahid gives predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), and mustankar gives mere conjecture (zann) which is insufficient.
This hierarchy is important for weighing evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندنا هو حجة؛ لأنه وافق القياس عندنا، وإنما يُترك إذا خالف القياس. وقد روى عنه الثقات، مثل عبد الله بن مسعود، وعلقمة، ومسروق، ونافع بن جبير والحسن البصري رضي الله عنهم، فثبتت بروايتهم عدالته، أنه مع من قرن العدول، فلذلك صار حجةً، وساعده عليه أناس من أشجع منهم أبو الجراح، وغيره.

(قوله : وقد روى عنه الثقات مثل عبد الله بن مسعود وعلقمة ومسروق ونافع بن جبير والحسن، أما رواية ابن مسعود : فلم أقف عليها التحديث عنه ، بصريح وإنما قَبِل منه، وصدقه، وفرح بما أخبره به ، وأما رواية علقمة عنه: فعند الأربعة، ورواية مسروق عنه : عند أبي داود والنسائي وابن ماجه ورواية نافع بن جبير عنه : عند أحمد في المسند، ورواية الحسن البصري عنه : عند النسائي، وكذا الأسود بن يزيد، والله أعلم.)

(قوله : وساعده عليه ناس من أشجع منهم أبو الجراح، وغيره: أما رواية أبي الجراح فأخرجها أبو داود فقال الجراح، ولفظه: «فقام ناس من أشجع فيهم الجراح وأبو سنان فقالوا: يابن مسعود نحن نشهد أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضاها فينا في بروع بنت واشق وإن زوجها هلال بن مرة الأشجعي كما قضيت». الحديث.)

وقال أبو موسى في معرفة الصحابة: أبو الجراح. وعند النسائي: «أُتي عبد الله بن مسعود في امرأة توفي عنها زوجها قبل أن يُفرض لها الحديث، وفيه : فقام سلمة وفلان وفلان فشهدوا أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى في بروع بنت واشق. الحديث.

وعنده في رواية : فقام رجل من أشجع - قال منصور: أراه سلمة بن يزيد فقال : مثل هذا قضى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في بروع». الحديث.

وعند أحمد: «فقام رجل من أشجع فقال أشهد على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قضى بذلك، قال: هلم من يشهد لك بذلك، فشهد أبو الجراح بذلك». وفي رواية: «فقال: هلم شاهداك، فشهد أبو سنان والجراح ورجلان من أشجع، وفي رواية : فقام رهط من أشجع ، منهم الجراح وأبو سنان».

فأما إذا كان ظَهَرَ حديثه، ولم يظهر من السلف إلا الردُّ: لم يُقبل حديثه، وصار مستنكراً، لا يُعمل به على خلاف القياس، وصار هذا غير حجة، يحتمل أن يكون حجةً على عكس المشهور أنه حجة يحتمل شبهةً عند التأمل.

وأما إذا لم يظهر حديثه في السلف، فلم يقابل برد ولا قبول : لم يُترك به القياس، ولم يجب العمل به في زماننا، لكن العمل به جائز؛ لأن العدالة أصل في ذلك الزمان.

ولذلك جَوَّز أبو حنيفة رحمه الله القضاء بظاهر العدالة من غير تعديل، حتى إن رواية مثل هذا المجهول في زماننا لا يَحلّ العمل به؛ لظهور الفسق.

فصار المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين والمشهور: علم طمأنينة ، وخبر الواحد : علم غالب الرأي والمستنكَرُ منه يُفيدُ الظَّنَّ، وإن الظَّنَّ لا يغني من الحق شيئاً.

والمستتر منه : في حيّز الجواز للعمل دون الوجوب، والله أعلم.

ومثال المستنكر مثل حديث فاطمة بنت قيس أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يجعل لها نفقةً، ولا سكنى.

(حديث فاطمة بنت قيس: عن الشعبي عن فاطمة بنت قيس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه لم يجعل لها نفقة ولا سكنى.)
And according to us, it (khabar al-wahid) is a proof (hujja) because it conforms to analogy (qiyas) in our view, and it is only abandoned if it contradicts analogy. And indeed trustworthy people narrated from him, such as Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Alqama, Masruq, Nafi' ibn Jubayr, and al-Hasan al-Basri, may Allah be pleased with them. So his integrity was established through their narration, that he is with those who are united with the just ones. Therefore it became a proof, and some people from Ashja' supported him, including Abu al-Jarrah and others. ... (footnotes) ... As for when his hadith became apparent, and only rejection appeared from the early generations: his hadith is not accepted, and it becomes mustankar (rejected), not to be acted upon if it contradicts analogy, and this becomes not a proof. It could be a proof contrary to the well-known that it is a proof, but it likely involves ambiguity upon reflection. And as for when his hadith did not become apparent among the early generations, so it was not met with rejection or acceptance: qiyas is not abandoned for it, and acting upon it is not obligatory in our time, but acting upon it is permissible because integrity (adala) was the norm in that time. For that reason, Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) permitted ruling based on apparent integrity without explicit verification, to the extent that the narration of such an unknown person in our time is not permissible to act upon due to the prevalence of immorality. Thus mutawatir produces knowledge of certainty, mashhur produces knowledge of tranquility, khabar al-wahid produces knowledge based on predominant opinion, and the mustankar from it produces conjecture, and conjecture cannot substitute for the truth at all. And the mustatir (hidden) from it is in the realm of permissibility for action, not obligation. And Allah knows best. An example of mustankar is the hadith of Fatima bint Qais that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not grant her maintenance and shelter.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's usul text discusses the authority of khabar al-wahid (a single-narrator hadith) within the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the Hanafi position that khabar al-wahid is a valid proof (hujja) as long as it conforms to qiyas (analogy); if it contradicts qiyas, it is rejected. The text then provides evidence from narrations of trustworthy companions like Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and others, whose reports were accepted. It notes that the integrity of the narrator is confirmed by the fact that other reliable narrators transmitted from him, placing him among the just. The passage then distinguishes between three categories of hadith based on the reaction of the early generations (salaf): (1) if the hadith became known and was explicitly rejected, it is considered mustankar (rejected) and not to be acted upon when it contradicts qiyas; (2) if the hadith did not become known and was neither accepted nor rejected, acting upon it is permissible but not obligatory, because in the early times integrity was assumed; (3) the hadith that is not widely known but not rejected (mustatir) is in the category of permissible action, not obligatory. Abu Hanifa allowed ruling based on apparent integrity without explicit verification. The text then ranks the epistemological value: mutawatir gives certainty, mashhur gives tranquility, khabar al-wahid gives predominant opinion, and mustankar gives conjecture, which is insufficient. An example of a mustankar hadith is the one about Fatima bint Qais regarding no maintenance and shelter for the divorced woman, which is rejected because it contradicts the general principles derived from the Qur'an. The commentary emphasizes that the Hanafi school prioritises qiyas and the practice of the salaf in evaluating hadith.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of mutawatir or mashhur.
مستنكر (mustanqar): A khabar al-wahid that became known but was explicitly rejected by the early generations (salaf), thus not to be acted upon if it contradicts qiyas.
مستتر (mustatir): A khabar al-wahid that did not become widely known nor was explicitly rejected; acting upon it is permissible but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as discussed in this passage, what is the status of a khabar al-wahid that contradicts qiyas and was rejected by the early generations (salaf)?
A) It is accepted as a proof (hujja) because hadith overrides analogy.
B) It is considered mustanqar (rejected) and not to be acted upon.
C) It is considered mutawatir and must be followed.
D) It is considered mustatir and action is permissible but not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The authority of khabar al-wahid in the Hanafi school depends on its conformity to qiyas and the reception by the salaf, not solely on chain authenticity.

Mustankar and Mustatir: Hanafi Classification of Hadith
Classifying hadith transmissions and explaining the ruling on mustankar and mustatir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a hadith as mustankar or mustatir and state the Hanafi ruling regarding acting upon each.

Core Idea
A hadith rejected by the Salaf is mustankar and cannot override qiyas; a hadith unknown to them is mustatir and permissible but not obligatory.

In this passage, Bazdawi explains how the reception of a hadith by the Salaf (early generations) determines its legal authority. A hadith that became known among them but was rejected becomes mustankar, while one that remained unknown and was neither accepted nor rejected becomes mustatir. The Hanafi school has distinct rulings for each category, which we will explore through the example of Fatima bint Qays.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the Arabic and translation to find the definitions of mustankar and mustatir. Note the key condition: mustankar requires the hadith to have become known to the Salaf and met with rejection; mustatir means it was not known and thus not subject to acceptance or rejection.
The textual clue: 'فأما إذا كان ظَهَرَ حديثه' vs 'وأما إذا لم يظهر حديثه'.
2
Understand the epistemic weight
The passage assigns epistemic values: mutawatir yields certainty, mashhur yields reassurance, khabar al-wahid yields predominant opinion, mustankar yields mere conjecture (zann), and mustatir permits action but does not oblige.
Conjecture does not avail against truth (الظن لا يغني من الحق شيئاً).
3
Analyze the time factor
Note that in early times, uprightness was assumed, so acting on a mustatir hadith was permissible. In later times, due to prevalent sin, a narrator of unknown character (like a mustatir) cannot be acted upon.
This explains Abu Hanifa's ruling on judging by apparent uprightness.
4
Apply to the example
The hadith of Fatima bint Qays is given as mustankar: it became known and was rejected by 'Umar and other Companions. Understand why 'Umar's rejection overrides its apparent authenticity.
Why did 'Umar reject it? He said: 'We will not abandon the Book and Sunnah for the statement of a woman.' 'Isa ibn Aban interpreted 'Book and Sunnah' as qiyas.

فأما إذا كان ظَهَرَ حديثه، ولم يظهر من السلف إلا الردُّ: لم يُقبل حديثه، وصار مستنكراً، لا يُعمل به على خلاف القياس، وصار هذا غير حجة، يحتمل أن يكون حجةً على عكس المشهور أنه حجة يحتمل شبهةً عند التأمل. وأما إذا لم يظهر حديثه في السلف، فلم يقابل برد ولا قبول : لم يُترك به القياس، ولم يجب العمل به في زماننا، لكن العمل به جائز؛ لأن العدالة أصل في ذلك الزمان. ولذلك جَوَّز أبو حنيفة رحمه الله القضاء بظاهر العدالة من غير تعديل، حتى إن رواية مثل هذا المجهول في زماننا لا يَحلّ العمل به؛ لظهور الفسق. فصار المتواتر يوجب علم اليقين والمشهور: علم طمأنينة ، وخبر الواحد : علم غالب الرأي والمستنكَرُ منه يُفيدُ الظَّنَّ، وإن الظَّنَّ لا يغني من الحق شيئاً. والمستتر منه : في حيّز الجواز للعمل دون الوجوب، والله أعلم. ومثال المستنكر مثل حديث فاطمة بنت قيس أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لم يجعل لها نفقةً، ولا سكنى» (۱). (۱) حديث فاطمة بنت قيس: عن الشعبي عن فاطمة بنت قيس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في المطلقة ثلاثاً قال : ليس لها سكنى، ولا نفقة». رواه أحمد ومسلم. وفي رواية عنها قالت: طلقني زوجي ثلاثاً، فلم يجعل لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سكنى ولا نفقة. رواه الجماعة إلا البخاري. فقد ردَّه عمر (۱) رضي الله عنه ، فقال : لا ندع كتاب ربَّنا ، ولا سُنَّةَ نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم بقول امرأة لا ندري أصدقت أم كذبت؟ أحفظت أم نسیت؟ قال عيسى بن أبان رحمه الله : فيه : أنه أراد بالكتاب والسنة القياس. وقد رده غيره من الصحابة أيضاً (۲) . (۱) قوله : وقد ردَّه عمر: عن الشعبي أنه حدث بحديث فاطمة بنت قيس: «أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يجعل لها سكنى ولا نفقة»، فأخذ الأسود بن يزيد من حَصَى فَحَصَبَه ،به وقال : ويلك ! تحدث بمثل هذا قال عمر: لا نترك كتاب وسنة نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم لقول امرأة لا ندري لعلها حفظت أو نسيت». رواه مسلم والترمذي، وزاد وكان عمر يجعل لها السكنى والنفقة. وأخرجه الطحاوي، وفيه: «فأخبرتُ بذلك إبراهيم النخعي، فقال: قال عمر وأخبر بذلك : لا ندع كتاب ربنا وسُنَّةَ نبينا». وفي رواية: لسنا بتاركي كتاب ربنا وسنة نبينا بقول امرأة لعلها كذبت. وفي رواية : لسنا بتاركي آية من كتاب الله، وقول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لقول امرأة لعلها وَهَمَتْ، سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: لها النفقة والسكنى. (۲) قوله : وقد ردَّه غيره من الصحابة أيضاً عن عروة بن الزبير أنه قال لعائشة : ألم ترَيْ فلانة بنت الحكم طلقها زوجها ألبتة، فخرجت، فقالت : قال : ألم تسمعي إلى قول فاطمة ؟ فقالت: أما إنه لا خير لها في ذكر ذلك». متفق عليه.
As for when his hadith became known, and nothing appeared from the Salaf except rejection: his hadith is not accepted, and it becomes 'mustankar' (rejected), not to be acted upon contrary to qiyas, and this is not a proof; it could be that it is a proof contrary to the well-known view that it is a proof that suggests a doubt upon reflection. And as for when his hadith did not become known among the Salaf, and it was not met with rejection or acceptance: qiyas is not abandoned for it, and acting upon it is not obligatory in our time, but acting upon it is permissible, because uprightness was the norm in that time. For that reason, Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) permitted judgment based on apparent uprightness without explicit attestation, even to the extent that narrating from such an unknown narrator in our time is not permissible to act upon due to the prevalence of sin. Thus, mutawatir produces certain knowledge; mashhur produces reassurance; khabar al-wahid produces a predominance of opinion; and the mustankar from it yields conjecture, and conjecture does not avail anything against the truth. The mustatir (hidden) type is in the realm of permissibility for action, not obligation, and Allah knows best. An example of the mustankar is the hadith of Fatima bint Qays that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not assign her maintenance nor housing. (1) (1) Hadith of Fatima bint Qays: from al-Sha'bi from Fatima bint Qays from the Prophet (peace be upon him) concerning a thrice-divorced woman: he said, 'She has no housing nor maintenance.' Narrated by Ahmad and Muslim. In another narration from her: she said, 'My husband divorced me three times, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not assign me housing nor maintenance.' Narrated by all except al-Bukhari. So 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) rejected it, saying: 'We will not abandon the Book of our Lord nor the Sunnah of our Prophet (peace be upon him) for the statement of a woman, we do not know whether she spoke truthfully or lied, whether she remembered or forgot?' 'Isa ibn Aban (may Allah have mercy on him) said: therein he meant by 'the Book and the Sunnah' qiyas. And others among the Companions also rejected it (2). (1) His saying: 'Umar rejected it: from al-Sha'bi that he narrated the hadith of Fatima bint Qays: 'The Messenger of Allah did not assign her housing nor maintenance' — so al-Aswad ibn Yazid took some pebbles and threw them at him, saying: 'Woe to you! You narrate such a thing?' He said: 'Umar said: We will not abandon the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet (peace be upon him) for the statement of a woman, we do not know, perhaps she remembered or forgot?' Narrated by Muslim and al-Tirmidhi, and he added: 'And 'Umar used to assign her housing and maintenance.' Al-Tahawi also narrated it, with: 'So I informed Ibrahim al-Nakha'i of that, and he said: 'Umar said: We will not abandon the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet.' In another narration: 'We are not going to abandon the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the statement of a woman, perhaps she lied.' In another narration: 'We are not going to abandon a verse from the Book of Allah and the statement of the Messenger of Allah for the statement of a woman, perhaps she made a mistake (wahimat); I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: She has maintenance and housing.' (2) His saying: 'And others among the Companions also rejected it' from 'Urwa ibn al-Zubayr that he said to 'A'isha: 'Did you not see so-and-so daughter of al-Hakam, her husband divorced her absolutely, and she went out?' She said: 'What did she do?' He said: 'Did you not hear the statement of Fatima?' She said: 'There is no good for her in mentioning that.' Agreed upon.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage from Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh discusses the classification of transmitted hadith based on their acceptance or rejection among the Salaf (the early generations of Muslims). The text first explains the ruling regarding a narrator whose hadith became known to the Salaf but was met only with rejection. Such a hadith is called 'mustankar' (rejected). It is not accepted as a proof and should not be acted upon if it contradicts qiyas (analogical reasoning). It suggests doubt upon reflection. On the other hand, if the hadith did not become known among the Salaf and was neither accepted nor rejected, it is called 'mustatir' (hidden). In that case, qiyas is not abandoned for it, and acting upon it is not obligatory but permissible. This permissibility is because uprightness (adala) was the norm among the early narrators. Abu Hanifa even allowed judging based on apparent uprightness without formal attestation. However, in later times, due to the increase of sin, such unknown narrators are not to be acted upon. The text then categorizes transmissions by epistemic value: mutawatir yields certain knowledge (ilm al-yaqin), mashhur yields reassurance (tuma'nina), khabar al-wahid yields predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), and mustankar yields only conjecture (zann). Conjecture does not suffice against the truth. Mustatir falls in the realm of permissible action but not obligation. The example of mustankar is the hadith of Fatima bint Qays reporting that the Prophet did not assign housing or maintenance to a thrice-divorced woman. This hadith was rejected by 'Umar and other Companions. 'Umar said he would not abandon the Book and Sunnah for the statement of a woman. 'Isa ibn Aban interpreted 'Umar's reference to 'Book and Sunnah' as meaning qiyas, i.e., the general principle derived from those sources. This illustrates that when a hadith contradicts established principles known from the Quran, Sunnah, or qiyas, and was rejected by the Salaf, it is mustankar and not accepted as a proof.

Key Terms
مستنكر (mustankar): A hadith that became known among the Salaf but was rejected by them; it is not accepted as a proof and only yields conjecture.
مستتر (mustatir): A hadith that did not become known among the Salaf and was neither accepted nor rejected; acting upon it is permissible but not obligatory.
متواتر (mutawatir): A hadith narrated by such a large number that collusion on a lie is impossible; it yields certain knowledge.
مشهور (mashhur): A hadith that became widely known among the scholars, though not reaching the level of tawatur; it yields reassurance.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary hadith narrated by one or a few narrators; it yields predominant opinion, not certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the category of the hadith of Fatima bint Qays regarding maintenance for a thrice-divorced woman?
A) Mutawatir
B) Mashhur
C) Mustankar
D) Mustatir

Key Takeaway
A hadith that became known to the Salaf and was rejected by them is mustankar and cannot be used as a proof; a hadith unknown to them is mustatir and its use is permissible but not obligatory.

Evaluating the Hadith of Busrah: Khabar al-Adl and Narrator Conditions
Disputed hadith and introduction to narrator conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for khabar al-adl to evaluate a disputed hadith and explain why the Hanafi school does not require wudu after touching the private part.

Core Idea
A khabar is not automatically accepted; it requires a just narrator who does not contradict stronger evidence.

In this passage, al-Bazdawi uses the hadith of Busrah as an example of a disputed khabar. He then states the foundational usul rule: khabar al-adl is authoritative only with conditions in the narrator. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi criteria for accepting a report and how they apply to the hadith of Busrah, showing the interplay between usul and fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and opposing narrations
Locate the hadith of Busrah that commands wudu after touching the private part, and note the many Companion statements (Ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, Ali, etc.) that contradict it.
This sets up the conflict for the usul analysis.
2
Recognize the usul rule stated
Al-Bazdawi asserts that khabar al-adl is only hujja (authoritative) with conditions in the narrator. Identify this as the core usul principle governing acceptance of reports.
The conditions will be explored in the next chapter.
3
Apply the rule to the hadith of Busrah
Consider which conditions might be lacking. The hadith is technically authentic (sahih) but contradicts the known practice (amal) and stronger evidence from multiple Companions. The Hanafi school considers that a khabar al-wahid that contradicts what is more firmly established is not accepted.
This is the Hanafi tarjih: the stronger evidence outweighs the isolated report.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The hadith of Busrah is a khabar al-wahid that opposes the statements of many Companions and the general principle that touching a part of one's own body does not invalidate wudu. Thus, it is not taken as proof.
The practical outcome: no wudu required.
5
Conclude the practical result
The resulting fiqh ruling is that touching the private part does not break wudu. This illustrates how usul principles directly shape fiqh rulings.
Contrast with the Shafi'i school, which accepts the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك حديث بسرة بنت صفوان في مَس الذكر من هذا القسم.
وإنما جعل خبرُ العدل حجةً بشرائط في الراوي، وهذا: باب بيان شرائط الراوي التي هي من صفات الراوي.
(1) قوله : وكذلك حديث بسرة : عن بُسرة بنت صفوان : أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن مسَّ ذَكَرَه فلا يصلي حتى يتوضأ». رواه الخمسة، وصححه الترمذي. عن أرقم بن شرحبيل أنه سأل عبد الله بن مسعود فقال : إني أحتك فأُفضي بيدي إلى فرجي، فقال ابن مسعود : إن علمت أن منك بضعة نجسةً فاقطعها. وعن قيس قال: قال عبد الله : ما أُبالي مسستُ ذَكَري أو أُذُني أو إبهامي أو أنفي. وعن حذيفة أنه قال: ما أبالي مسستُ ذكري أو أُذُني. وعن سعيد بن جبير عن ابن عباس مثله. وعن عمار بن ياسر أنه سئل عن مس الذكر في الصلاة، فقال: ما هو إلا بضعةٌ منك. وعن قيس قال: سأل رجل سعداً عن مس الذكر ، فقال : إن علمت أن منك بضعةً نجسة فاقطعها. وعن الحسن أن عمران بن حصين :قال ما أُبالي إياه مسستُ أو بطن فخذي، يعني : ذَكَرَه. وعن قابوس عن أبيه قال: سئل علي رضي الله عنه عن الرجل يمس ذَكَرَه قال : لا بأس. أخرجها ابن أبي شيبة.
And likewise the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan about touching the private part is of this section. And indeed the report of a just narrator is made a proof only with conditions in the narrator, and this is the chapter explaining the conditions of the narrator, which are among the qualities of the narrator. (1) His saying: and likewise the hadith of Busrah: from Busrah bint Safwan: that the Prophet said: 'Whoever touches his private part should not pray until he performs wudu.' Reported by the five, and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. From Arqam ibn Shurahbil: he asked Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: I scratch myself and my hand reaches my genitals. Ibn Mas'ud said: If you know that there is a dirty piece from you then cut it off. And from Qays: Abdullah said: I do not care whether I touch my private part or my ear or my thumb or my nose. And from Hudhayfah: he said: I do not care whether I touch my private part or my ear. And from Sa'id ibn Jubayr from Ibn Abbas the like. And from Ammar ibn Yasir: he was asked about touching the private part during prayer, he said: It is only a piece of you. And from Qays: a man asked Sa'd about touching the private part, he said: If you know that there is a dirty piece from you then cut it off. And from al-Hasan: Imran ibn Husayn said: I do not care whether I touch it or my thigh, meaning his private part. And from Qabus from his father: Ali was asked about a man touching his private part, he said: No harm. Ibn Abi Shaybah collected them.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of disputed khabar. The hadith of Busrah, which commands wudu after touching the private part, is countered by many Companions (Ibn Mas'ud, Hudhayfah, Ali, etc.) who did not require wudu. The author then states the usul rule: khabar al-adl is only authoritative with specific conditions in the narrator. This introduces the next chapter on narrator conditions (shurut al-rawi). The Hanafi position on touching the private part is that it does not break wudu, based on the stronger evidence from the Companions' statements. This illustrates that not every technically authentic hadith is accepted; the narrator's reliability and consistency with other evidence matter.

Key Terms
خبر العدل (khabar al-adl): A report from a just, reliable narrator; it is authoritative only with conditions.
مس الذكر (mas al-dhakar): Touching the male private part; the ruling on whether it necessitates wudu is disputed.
شرائط الراوي (shurut al-rawi): Conditions of the narrator for accepting his report as proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The narrator must be just.
B) The narrator must have good memory.
C) The report must not contradict stronger evidence.
D) The report must be mutawatir.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a khabar al-adl only when the narrator meets conditions and the report does not contradict stronger evidence, as illustrated by the hadith of Busrah.

Conditions of the Narrator in Hadith Transmission
Defining the four conditions required in a hadith narrator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the four conditions of a hadith narrator (intellect, precision, Islam, integrity) and justify each condition using Hanafi usul reasoning.

Core Idea
A narrator's 'adala (integrity) is not automatic; it is inferred rationally because the narrator is not infallible.

Hadith transmission forms a primary source of Islamic law. For a report to be authoritative, the narrator must meet certain conditions. This passage outlines four such conditions—intellect, precision, Islam, and integrity—and explains the rational basis for each. Understanding these conditions helps us evaluate the reliability of hadith and their use as legal proof.

Guided Path
1
List the four conditions
Identify the four conditions as stated in the passage: intellect, precision, Islam, and integrity.
The passage explains only three; Islam is listed but not elaborated here.
2
Analyze the condition of intellect
Understand why intellect is necessary: meaningful speech requires both form and meaning; meaning depends on intellect.
The author argues that without intellect, speech is mere sound without communicative value.
3
Analyze the condition of precision
Precision (dabt) ensures that the narrator accurately preserves and conveys the report, making truthfulness more likely.
Truth is the basis of proof; precision is the means to achieve truth.
4
Analyze the condition of integrity
Integrity ('adala) is required because the narrator is not infallible; his truthfulness must be inferred from his moral conduct.
The text defines 'adala as refraining from religious prohibitions, which increases the preponderance of truth.
5
Synthesize the implications
Recognize that these conditions are rationally derived from the nature of communication and legal proof.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of istidlal (rational inference) in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب
بيان شرائط الراوي التي هي من صفات الراوي
وهي أربعة: العقل، والضبط، والإسلام، والعدالة.
١ - أما العقل: فهو شرط؛ لأن المراد بالكلام: ما يُسمى كلاماً صورةً ومعنى، ومعنى الكلام لا يوجد إلا بالتمييز والعقل؛ لأنه وضع للبيان، ولا يقعُ البيانُ بمجرد الصوت والحروف بلا معنى، ولا يوجد معناه إلا بالعقل.
وكل موجود من الحوادث فبصورته ومعناه يكون، فلذلك كان العقل شرطاً؛ ليصير الكلام موجوداً.
٢ - وأما الضبط فإنما يشترط؛ لأن الكلام إذا صح خبراً: فإنه يحتمل الصدق والكذب، والحجةُ هو الصدق، فأما الكذب: فباطل، والكلام في خبر هو حجة، فصار الصدق والاستقامة شرطاً للخبر؛ ليثبت حجة، بمنزلة المعرفة والتمييز لأصل الكلام، والصدق: بالضبط يحصل.
وأما العدالة: فإنما شرطت؛ لأن كلامنا وقع في خبرِ مُخبِرٍ غيرِ معصوم عن الكذب، فلا يثبت صدقه ضرورة، بل بالاستدلال والاحتمال، وذلك بالعدالة، وهي: الانزجار عن محظورات دينه؛ ليثبت به رجحان الصدق في خبره.
Chapter: Explanation of the conditions of the narrator that are from his attributes. And they are four: intellect, precision, Islam, and integrity. 1. As for intellect: it is a condition because the intended meaning of speech is what is called speech in form and meaning, and the meaning of speech does not exist except through discernment and intellect; because it is placed for communication, and communication does not occur by mere sound and letters without meaning, and its meaning does not exist except through intellect. And every existing thing among events exists by its form and meaning, therefore intellect is a condition for speech to come into existence. 2. As for precision: it is required because when speech is sound as a report, it admits of truth and falsehood, and the proof is truth. As for falsehood, it is invalid. Speech in a report is a proof, so truth and uprightness become a condition for the report to establish a proof, akin to knowledge and discernment for the origin of speech, and truth is attained through precision. As for integrity: it is only required because our discourse is about the report of a reporter not infallible from lying, so his truthfulness is not established necessarily, but through inference and probability, and that is through integrity, which is refraining from the prohibitions of his religion, so that the preponderance of truthfulness in his report is established.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a definitional text from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. It opens by stating the chapter's topic: the conditions of the narrator (rawi) that relate to his personal attributes. The author lists four conditions: intellect ('aql), precision (dabt), Islam, and integrity ('adala). However, only three are explained in the available excerpt; Islam is listed but not elaborated, possibly due to a missing portion. The explanation for intellect focuses on the nature of meaningful speech: language conveys meaning only through the speaker's intellect, and the listener must also have intellect to comprehend. The condition of precision is tied to ensuring truthfulness in transmission, as a report can be true or false, and only truth is authoritative. Precision (dabt) ensures that the narrator accurately preserves and conveys the report. The condition of integrity ('adala) is required because the narrator is not infallible; his truthfulness is not automatic but inferred based on his moral uprightness—specifically, his avoidance of religious prohibitions. This increases the likelihood that his report is true. The reasoning follows Hanafi usul principles, emphasizing the need for rational inference (istidlal) in establishing the authority of a single-narrator report (khabar al-wahid).

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): Intellect or reason, necessary for meaningful speech and communication.
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision in memorizing and transmitting a report, ensuring truthfulness.
العدالة (al-'adala): Integrity, the quality of refraining from religious prohibitions, which makes one's truthfulness preponderant.
الإسلام (al-islam): Being Muslim; listed as a condition but not explained in the excerpt.

D) To ensure the narrator refrains from prohibitions

Key Takeaway
The four conditions—intellect, precision, Islam, and integrity—are rationally necessary for accepting a hadith as legal proof, each addressing a distinct aspect of reliable transmission.

The Four Conditions of the Narrator: Intellect, Accuracy, Integrity, and Islam in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the four necessary qualities for a narrator's testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four conditions of the narrator (al-rawi) according to Hanafi usul and explain the legal rationale ('illah) for each condition using the author's talil.

Core Idea
The narrator's truthfulness is established by accuracy and integrity, not by Islam alone—disbelief creates suspicion, not falsehood.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul outlines the essential qualities a narrator must possess for his testimony to be accepted in religious matters. The author distinguishes conditions that affect truthfulness from those that affect acceptance due to suspicion. Understanding this distinction is foundational to evaluating narrators and their reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four conditions
Locate the four qualities listed: intellect ('aql), accuracy (dabt), integrity ('adalah), and Islam. Note that each has a specific role.
2
Classify each condition's function
For each condition, determine whether it is required for the existence of meaningful speech, for establishing truth, for preponderance of truth, or for removing suspicion. Intellect is for meaning; accuracy for truth; integrity for preponderance; Islam for acceptance not truth.
3
Analyze the author's talil
Read the reasoning (ta'lil) for each condition. Intellect: speech requires meaning, meaning requires intellect. Accuracy: reports admit truth/falsehood, truth requires precision. Integrity: narrator not infallible, so need preponderance via refraining from sin. Islam: not for truth but for suspicion of bias against religion.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ليس بشرط لثبوت الصدق' for Islam.
4
Understand the special status of Islam
Islam is not a condition for truthfulness; a disbeliever can be truthful. However, it is required for acceptance because the context is religion, and a disbeliever is suspected of trying to undermine it.
Analogous to a father's testimony for his son due to suspected bias.
5
Apply the analogy
The author compares the disbeliever's testimony to a father testifying for his child: both have a legally recognized bias (tuhma) that prevents acceptance, even though truth is possible.
This analogy is a form of qiyas illustrating the reason for rejection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب بيان شرائط الراوي التي هي من صفات الراوي وهي أربعة: العقل، والضبط، والإسلام، والعدالة. ١ - أما العقل : فهو شرط ؛ لأن المراد بالكلام : ما يُسمى كلاماً صورةً ومعنى، ومعنى الكلام لا يوجد إلا بالتمييز والعقل؛ لأنه وضع للبيان، ولا يقعُ البيانُ بمجرد الصوت والحروف بلا معنى، ولا يوجد معناه إلا بالعقل. وكل موجود من الحوادث فبصورته ومعناه يكون، فلذلك كان العقل شرطاً؛ ليصير الكلام موجوداً. ٢ - وأما الضبط فإنما يشترط ؛ لأن الكلام إذا صح خبراً: فإنه يحتمل الصدق والكذب، والحجةُ هو الصدق، فأما الكذب: فباطل، والكلام في خبر هو حجة، فصار الصدق والاستقامة شرطاً للخبر؛ ليثبت حجة، بمنزلة المعرفة والتمييز لأصل الكلام ، والصدق: بالضبط يحصل. وأما العدالة : فإنما شرطت ؛ لأن كلامنا وقع في خبرِ مُخبِرٍ غيرِ معصوم عن الكذب، فلا يثبت صدقه ضرورة، بل بالاستدلال والاحتمال، وذلك بالعدالة، وهي: الانزجار عن محظورات دينه؛ ليثبت به رجحان الصدق في خبره. ٣ وأما الإسلام فليس بشرط لثبوت الصدق؛ لأن الكفر لا ينافي الصدق، ولكن الكفر في هذا الباب يوجب شبهةً يجب بها ردُّ الخبر ؛ لأن الباب بابُ الدِّين، والكافِرُ ساع لِمَا يَهدِم الدينَ الحقِّ، فيصير متّهَماً باب الدين، فثبتت بالكفر تهمة زائدة لا نقصان حال، بمنزلة الأب فيما يشهد لولده، ولهذا لم تُقبل شهادة الكافر على المسلم؛ لما قلنا من العداوة، ولانقطاع الولاية، والله أعلم.
Chapter explaining the conditions of the narrator which are from the attributes of the narrator. They are four: intellect, accuracy, Islam, and integrity. 1. As for intellect: it is a condition because what is meant by speech is what is called speech in form and meaning, and the meaning of speech is only found through discrimination and intellect; because it is placed for elucidation, and elucidation does not occur merely by sound and letters without meaning, and its meaning is only found through intellect. And every existent among events is by its form and meaning, therefore intellect was a condition so that speech becomes existent. 2. As for accuracy: it is only stipulated because when speech is valid as a report, it admits of truth and falsehood, and the proof is truth; as for falsehood, it is invalid. And speech in a report is a proof, so truth and uprightness become a condition for the report to establish a proof, like knowledge and discrimination for the origin of speech. And truth is obtained by accuracy. As for integrity: it is only stipulated because our speech concerns a report of an informant who is not infallible from falsehood, so his truth is not established necessarily, but through inference and probability, and that is through integrity, which is: refraining from prohibited things of his religion, to establish thereby the preponderance of truth in his report. 3. As for Islam: it is not a condition for establishing truth because disbelief does not contradict truth, but disbelief in this chapter creates a suspicion that requires rejection of the report; because the chapter is the chapter of religion, and the disbeliever strives for what destroys the true religion, so he becomes accused concerning the religion. Thus suspicion is established by disbelief as an added factor, not a deficiency in condition, like a father testifying for his son; for this reason the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not accepted, due to what we said of enmity and due to severance of guardianship. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions required in a narrator (rawī) for acceptance of hadith or testimony. The author enumerates four qualities: intellect, accuracy, Islam, and integrity, but with nuanced reasoning. Intellect is essential because meaningful speech requires rational understanding; a report without meaning is not truly speech. Accuracy (ḍabṭ) is needed because a report can be true or false; truth is established by the narrator's precision in memorization and transmission. Integrity ('adālah) ensures the narrator refrains from major sins, giving preponderance to truthfulness. Islam, remarkably, is not a condition for the truth of the report itself, as a disbeliever can be truthful. However, it is required for acceptance because the context is religion; a disbeliever is suspected of attempting to undermine Islam, analogous to a father's bias in testimony for his child. Hence, the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is rejected due to enmity and lack of guardianship. This analysis follows the Hanafi usul, stressing that integrity and Islam are necessary not for truth per se but for reliable inference.

Key Terms
العقل (al-'aql): Intellect or rationality; the capacity to understand meaning, necessary for speech to convey meaning.
الضبط (al-ḍabṭ): Accuracy and retention; the ability to correctly memorize and transmit reports, ensuring truthfulness.
العدالة (al-'adālah): Integrity; refraining from prohibited acts of religion, which makes the narrator's truthfulness preponderant.
الإسلام (al-islām): Being a Muslim; not a condition for truth but for acceptance due to suspicion of bias against religion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is Islam a condition for accepting a narrator's report?
A) Because a disbeliever cannot be truthful.
B) Because disbelief creates a suspicion of bias against religion.
C) Because Islam is a condition for intellect.
D) Because all conditions require Islam.

Key Takeaway
A narrator's report is accepted based on intellect, accuracy, and integrity for truth, while Islam is required only to remove suspicion of religious bias; truthful non-Muslims can be rejected due to contextual suspicion.

Intellect and Precision as Conditions for Narration
Definition of two conditions and their classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of intellect and precision as conditions for accepting a narrator's report, and apply them to determine whether a minor's or heedless person's report is accepted in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A narrator must have perfect intellect and precision; otherwise, the report is not a proof.

In this passage, the author of Kanz al-Wusul defines two key conditions for accepting a narrator's report: intellect and precision. These are not mere theoretical qualities but have practical consequences: a minor's report is rejected, and a heedless person's report is not accepted. The passage also addresses a potential objection regarding the transmission of the Quran. Understanding these definitions will sharpen your ability to evaluate narrators and their reports in Hanafi hadith criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the first two headings. The conditions are intellect and precision. Note that the passage defines each and then gives rulings.
These conditions are for the acceptance of a single narrator's report (khabar al-wahid).
2
Analyze the definition of intellect
Intellect is defined as a light by which the heart perceives beyond the senses. It is divided into deficient (child's intellect) and complete (adult intellect). The Shari'a attaches rulings to the lowest degree of complete intellect, using puberty as its indicator.
Perfect intellect (kamil al-'aql) is required for the report to be a proof.
3
Analyze the definition of precision
Precision (dabt) involves hearing correctly, understanding the intended meaning, memorizing with effort, and preserving until delivery. It has two types: textual precision and juristic precision (adding fiqh understanding). The complete type is required.
Extreme heedlessness by nature, carelessness, or recklessness prevents precision.
4
Apply the conditions to cases
The passage states that a minor's report is not a proof because the law did not make him a guardian in worldly affairs, so even more so in religious matters. Similarly, the report of a habitually heedless person is not a proof.
In tarjih, preference is given to a narrator known for fiqh.
5
Examine the Quran objection and Hanafi response
The author preempts an objection: the Quran is transmitted by people who may not have perfect dabt (e.g., children), yet it is accepted. The response is that the Quran's transmission is mutawatir by a reliable group, and its miraculous wording is integral. For the Sunnah, meaning is primary, so perfect dabt is required for individual narrators.
This demonstrates the school's consistency: the condition applies to khabar al-wahid, not mutawatir.

أما العقل : فنورٌ يُضيء به طريقٌ يُبتدأ به من حيث ينتهي إليه دَرك الحواس، فيتبدى المطلوب للقلب، فيُدركه القلب بتأمله بتوفيق الله تعالى، وإنه لا يُعرَف في البشر إلا بدلالة اختياره فيما يأتيه ويَذَرُه ما يصلح له في عاقبته.

قاصر لما يقارنه ما يدل على نقصانه في ابتداء وجوده، وهو عقل الصبي؛ لأن العقل يوجد زائداً.
ثم هو بحكم الله تعالى وقسمته متفاوت لا يُدرك تفاوته، فعلقت أحكام الشرع بأدنى درجات كماله واعتداله، وأُقيمَ البلوغ الذي هو دليل عليه مقامه تيسيراً.

وكذلك المعتوه.
وأما الضبط: فإن تفسيره: سماع الكلام كما يَحقُّ سماعه، ثم فَهُمُه بمعناه الذي أريد به، ثم حفظه ببذل المجهود له، ثم الثبات عليه بمحافظة حدوده، ومراقبته بمذاكرته على إساءة الظن بنفسه إلى حين أدائه.

والمطلق من الضبط: يتناول الكامل.
ولهذا لم يكن خبرُ مَن اشتدَّت غفلته خلقةً، أو مسامحةً أو مجازفةً حجةً؛ لعدم القسم الأول من الضبط، ولهذا قصرت روايةُ مَن لم يُعرف بالفقه عند معارضة مَن عُرف بالفقه في باب الترجيح، وهذا مذهبنا في الترجيح.

ولأن نقل القرآن ممن لا يضبط الصيغة بمعناها إنما يصح إذا بَذَلَ مجهوده واستفرغ وُسعَه، ولو فعل ذلك في السنة لصار ذلك حجةً، إلا أنه لما عُدم ذلك عادةً شَرَطنا كمال الضبط ليصير حجةً.

Chapter: Explanation of these conditions and their divisions. As for intellect: it is a light by which a path is illuminated, beginning from where the perception of the senses ends, so the sought thing appears to the heart, and the heart perceives it by reflection with the help of God Almighty. It is not known in humans except by the indication of his choice in what he does and leaves that is beneficial for him in the end. It is of two types: Deficient (for what accompanies it indicating its deficiency at the beginning of its existence) – and that is the intellect of a minor; because intellect exists as additional. Then it, by God's decree and division, varies in a way that its variation cannot be perceived. The rulings of the law were attached to the lowest degrees of its perfection and balance, and puberty, which is evidence of it, was established in its place for ease. The absolute of everything applies to its perfection. So we stipulated for the obligation of a ruling and the establishment of proof: perfection of intellect. Thus we said: The report of a minor is not a proof because the law did not make him a guardian in his worldly affairs – then in religious matters it is more fitting. Likewise the insane. As for precision (dabt): its explanation is hearing the speech as it ought to be heard, then understanding it in the meaning intended, then memorizing it by exerting effort, then adhering to it by preserving its boundaries and guarding it by reviewing it with a suspicion of oneself until the time of its delivery. It is of two types: Precision of the text in its wording and its linguistic meaning. The second: that to this combined is precision of its meaning in jurisprudence and law – and this is the more complete. The absolute of precision includes the complete. For this reason, the report of one whose heedlessness is severe by nature, or by carelessness or recklessness, is not a proof due to the absence of the first type of precision. For this reason, the narration of one not known for jurisprudence is outweighed when opposed to one known for jurisprudence in the chapter of preference (tarjih). This is our school in tarjih. And it does not necessitate that the transmission of the Qur'an from one without precision be made a proof – because its transmission originally is established by a people who are the imams of guidance and the best of mankind, and because the wording of the Qur'an is miraculous and rulings are attached to it specifically, such as the permissibility of prayer and the prohibition of recitation for the menstruating and the junub. So its wording was considered in its transmission, and its meaning was built upon it. As for the Sunnah: meaning is its foundation, and wording is not binding in it. And because the transmission of the Qur'an from one who does not preserve the wording with its meaning is valid only if he exerts his effort and exhausts his capacity. And if he did that in the Sunnah, it would become a proof, except that when that is customarily absent, we stipulated perfect precision so that it becomes a proof. And the meaning of our statement "he hears it as it ought to be heard": that a man may reach
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of two key conditions for accepting a narrator's report: intellect (aqal) and precision (dabt). The author first defines aql as a light that allows the heart to perceive what is beyond the senses; it is known through one's choices. He divides it into deficient (the intellect of a minor, which is naturally incomplete) and complete. The Shari'a attaches rulings to the lowest degree of complete intellect, using puberty as its indicator for practicality. Since the absolute term 'intellect' refers to perfection, the condition for proof is perfect intellect; hence a minor's or insane person's report is not hujjah. Next, he defines dabt as hearing correctly, understanding the intended meaning, memorizing with effort, and maintaining it until delivery. Dabt is of two kinds: textual precision (wording and linguistic meaning) and combined juristic precision (also understanding the fiqh implications). The latter is more complete. Only complete dabt suffices; thus a habitually heedless, careless, or reckless person's report is not proof. In cases of conflict, a narrator known for fiqh is given preference over one who is not—this is the Hanafi position in tarjih. The author then addresses a potential objection: the Quran is transmitted from people without perfect dabt (like children) yet accepted. He responds that the Quran's transmission is by a group (mutawatir) of reliable imams, and its wording is miraculous and integral; for Sunnah, meaning is primary. Moreover, if someone exerted maximum effort in transmitting a hadith wording, it would be accepted, but since that is rare, we require perfect dabt as a condition for proof. The final sentence explains 'hearing properly'—a person may reach a point where he cannot hear the full hadith correctly; this justifies the requirement.

Key Terms
العقل (al-‘aql): A light by which the heart perceives what is beyond the senses; it is known through one's choices. Divided into deficient (child's intellect) and complete (adult intellect).
الضبط (al-dabt): Precision in hearing, understanding, memorizing, and retaining a hadith. Two types: textual (dabt al-matn) and juristic (dabt al-fiqh). The complete includes both.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because a minor cannot hear properly
B) Because a minor lacks the perfect intellect required for trustworthiness in religious matters
C) Because a minor cannot memorize the text
D) Because the Shari'a does not consider minors as narrators at all

Key Takeaway
A narrator's report is accepted only if the narrator possesses perfect intellect and complete precision; otherwise, it is not a valid proof.

Dabt and Adalah: The Two Pillars of Narrator Reliability in Hanafi Usul
Defining the two types of dabt and adalah and their implications for hadith acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of dabt and the two types of adalah, and explain why the Hanafi school requires complete dabt (including fiqh understanding) for narrator reliability, and how this relates to the exceptional status of the Quran.

Core Idea
A narrator must have complete dabt (wording + fiqh meaning) and complete adalah (predominance of religion over desire) for his report to be authoritative.

In this lesson, we examine two fundamental conditions for accepting a narrator's report in Hanafi usul: dabt (accuracy) and adalah (uprightness). Al-Bazdawi defines these conditions in detail, distinguishing between deficient and complete levels, and explains how they apply to the transmission of the Sunnah versus the Quran. Understanding these conditions is essential for evaluating hadith and for resolving conflicts between narrators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of dabt
The passage distinguishes between preserving the text's wording and linguistic meaning (first type) and additionally preserving its fiqh and sharia meaning (second, more complete type). The absolute term 'dabt' refers to the complete type.
The first type is minimal; the second is required for authoritative transmission.
2
Understand the role of dabt in tarjih
Hanafi tarjih gives preference to a narrator known for fiqh over one not, because complete dabt includes fiqh understanding. A narrator lacking the second type yields a weaker narration when opposed.
This is a distinctive Hanafi principle.
3
Analyze the exception for the Quran
The Quran's transmission does not require complete dabt from each individual because it is transmitted by tawatur and its wording is essential for its miraculous nature. For the Sunnah, meaning is primary, so complete dabt is stipulated.
This prevents a reductio ad absurdum against the Hanafi position.
4
Examine the two types of adalah
Deficient adalah is based on apparent Islam and intellect; complete adalah requires predominance of religion and intellect over desire. Committing a major sin or persisting in minor sins destroys adalah, but occasional minor sins without persistence do not.
The distinction affects the acceptance of a narrator's reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بمعناه الذي أريد به، ثم حفظه ببذل المجهود له، ثم الثبات عليه بمحافظة حدوده، ومراقبته بمذاكرته على إساءة الظن بنفسه إلى حين أدائه.
وهو نوعان:
ضبط المتن بصيغته ومعناه لغةً.
والثاني: أن يُضَمَّ إلى هذه الجملة ضبط معناه فقهاً وشريعة، وهذا أكملها.
والمطلق من الضبط : يتناول الكامل.
ولهذا لم يكن خبرُ مَن اشتدَّت غفلته خلقةً، أو مسامحة أو مجازفةً حجةٌ ؛ لعدم القسم الأول من الضبط، ولهذا قصرت روايةٌ مَن لم يُعرف بالفقه عند معارضة مَن عُرف بالفقه في باب الترجيح، وهذا مذهبنا في الترجيح.
ولا يلزم عليه أن نَقل القرآن ممن لا ضبط له جعل حجةً ؛ لأن نقله في الأصل إنما ثبت بقوم هم القرآن معجز تتعلق به أحكام على الخصوص، مثل جواز الصلاة، وحرمة التلاوة على الحائض والجنب ، فاعتُبر في نقله نَظْمُه، وبني عليه معناه. فأما السنة: فإن المعنى: أصلها، والنظم غير لازم فيها .
أئمة الهدى، وخير الورى، ولأن نظم القرآن ممن لا يضبط الصيغة بمعناها إنما يصح إذا بَذَلَ مجهوده، واستفرغ وُسعَه ، ولو فَعَلَ ذلك في السنة: لصار ذلك حجةً، إلا أنه لما عُدم ذلك عادةً شَرَطنا كمال الضبط ؛ ليصير حجة.
ومعنى قولنا أن يسمعه حق سماعه : أن الرجل قد ينتهي إلى المجلس وقد مضى صدرٌ من الكلام، فربما يخفى على المتكلم هجومه ليُعيد عليه ما سبق من كلامه، فعلى السامع الاحتياط في مثله.
ثم قد يزدري السامع بنفسه، فلا يراها أهلاً لتبليغ الشريعة، فيُقصر في بعض ما أُلقي إليه، ثم يُفضي به فضلُ الله تعالى إلى أن يتصدى لإقامة الشريعة وقد قصَّر في بعض ما لزمه، فلذلك شَرَطنا مراقبته.
وأما العدالة: فإن تفسيرها الاستقامة يقال للجادة : طريق عَدْلٌ، وجائر للبنيات وهي نوعان أيضاً : قاصر، وكامل.
أما القاصر: فما ثبت منه بظاهر الإسلام واعتدال العقل؛ لأن الأصل: حالة الاستقامة، لكن هذا الأصل لا يفارقه هوى يُضلّه، ويَصدُّه عن الاستقامة.
وليس لكمال الاستقامة حدٌ يُدرك مداه ؛ لأنها بتقدير الله تعالى ومشيئته تتفاوت، فاعتبر في ذلك ما لا يؤدي إلى الحرج والمشقة، وتضييع حدود الشريعة، وهو رجحان جهة الدين والعقل على طريق الهوى والشهوة.
فقيل : مَن ارتكب كبيرةً : سقطت عدالته ، وصار متهماً بالكذب. وإذا أصر على ما دون الكبيرة : كان مثلها في وقوع التهمة، وجرح العدالة. فأما من ابتلي بشيء من غير الكبائر من غير إصرار: فعَدلُ كامل العدالة، وخبره حجة في إقامة الشريعة.
By its meaning that was intended, then preserving it by exerting effort for it, then steadfastness upon it by guarding its limits, and monitoring oneself by reviewing it while thinking ill of oneself until the time of its delivery. And it is of two types: First: preserving the text in its wording and its meaning linguistically. Second: that to this is added preserving its meaning in fiqh and sharia, and this is the more complete. The absolute [term] 'dabt' includes the complete. For this reason, the report of one whose heedlessness is intense by nature, or through carelessness or recklessness, is not authoritative; due to the absence of the first type of dabt. And for this reason, the narration of one not known for fiqh is considered weaker when opposed to one known for fiqh in the chapter of tarjih, and this is our madhhab in tarjih. And it does not follow from this that the transmission of the Qur'an from one lacking dabt is made authoritative; because its transmission originally was only established by a people [such that] the Qur'an is a miracle with particular rulings attached, like the permissibility of prayer and the prohibition of recitation for the menstruating woman and the junub. So its wording was considered in its transmission, and its meaning was built upon it. As for the Sunnah, the meaning is its foundation, and wording is not necessary in it. [Because] the Imams of guidance, the best of creation, and because the transmission of the Qur'an from one who does not preserve the wording with its meaning is only valid if he exerts his effort and exhausts his capacity. And if he did that for the Sunnah, it would become authoritative, except that since that is normally absent, we stipulated complete dabt so it becomes authoritative. And the meaning of our saying 'he hears it properly' is that a man may come to the gathering after part of the speech has passed, and perhaps the speaker's sudden arrival is hidden from him, so that he may repeat what has passed of his speech. So the listener must be cautious in such a case. Then the listener may think lowly of himself, not considering himself worthy of conveying the sharia, so he falls short in some of what was entrusted to him. Then Allah's favor leads him to undertake establishing the sharia while he has fallen short in some of what was incumbent upon him. Therefore we stipulated his self-monitoring. As for 'adalah' (uprightness): its interpretation is 'straightness'. It is said: 'a straight road' and 'deviating for side paths'. And it is also of two types: deficient and complete. As for the deficient: what is established by apparent Islam and sound intellect, because the original state is uprightness, but this original state is not free from a desire that misguides him and turns him away from uprightness. And there is no limit for complete uprightness that can be grasped, because it varies by Allah's decree and will. So what is considered in that is what does not lead to hardship and difficulty and neglect of the limits of sharia, which is the preponderance of the side of religion and intellect over the path of desire and lust. So it is said: whoever commits a major sin, his adalah falls and he becomes accused of lying. And if he persists in a minor sin, it is like a major sin in causing accusation and damaging adalah. As for one who is afflicted with something from minor sins without persistence, he is of complete adalah, and his report is authoritative in establishing the sharia.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul defines two essential conditions for a narrator's report to be authoritative: dabt (accuracy/precision) and adalah (uprightness/justice). The author first discusses dabt, which is of two types: 1) preserving the text's wording and linguistic meaning, and 2) additionally preserving its meaning in fiqh and sharia, the latter being more complete. A narrator lacking the first type due to innate heedlessness or carelessness is not accepted. Hanafi tarjih (preference) considers a narrator known for fiqh over one not. The author addresses a potential objection: why is Quranic transmission accepted from those without dabt? Because the Quran's wording is essential due to its miraculous nature and specific rulings; its transmission requires precise wording. For Sunnah, meaning is primary, wording not necessarily preserved. However, if someone exerted effort to preserve both wording and meaning for Sunnah, it would be authoritative, but since that rarely happens, complete dabt is stipulated. The author then explains 'hearing properly' requires the listener to be cautious about missing parts. The condition of 'self-monitoring' (muraqabah) ensures the narrator does not underestimate his duty. Then discussion of adalah (uprightness), also two types: qasir (deficient) and kamil (complete). Deficient adalah is established by apparent Islam and sound intellect, but may be corrupted by desires. Complete adalah has no fixed limit but requires predominance of religion and intellect over desire. A major sin destroys adalah; persistence in minor sins does similarly. But occasional minor sins without persistence still leave the narrator with complete adalah, making his report authoritative.

Key Terms
الضبط (al-dabt): حفظ الحديث بلفظه ومعناه، نوعان: ضبط المتن بصيغته ومعناه لغة، وضبط معناه فقهاً وشريعة
العدالة (al-'adalah): الاستقامة في الدين، نوعان: قاصر (بظاهر الإسلام واعتدال العقل) وكامل (رجحان جهة الدين والعقل على الهوى)
الترجيح (al-tarjih): تفضيل رواية من عرف بالفقه على من لم يعرف به عند التعارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to a narrator who persists in a minor sin?
A) His adalah remains complete because minor sins do not affect it.
B) His adalah falls immediately like committing a major sin.
C) His adalah becomes deficient and his report is not authoritative.
D) His adalah is only questioned if he commits a major sin.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a narrator must have both complete dabt (preserving wording and fiqh meaning) and complete adalah (predominance of religion and intellect) for his report to be authoritative; the Quran is an exception because its transmission relies on tawatur.

The Condition of 'Adala (Uprightness) in Narrators
Defining 'adala, its degrees, and conditions for accepting reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two degrees of 'adala (qasir and kamil) and apply the Hanafi rule for accepting reports from narrators based on their uprightness.

Core Idea
‘Adala has two degrees; only the complete degree (kamil) makes a narrator’s report a proof in the Shari‘ah.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi defines the essential quality of 'adala (uprightness) required in narrators for accepting their reports. It explains that 'adala has two levels—deficient and complete—and clarifies what constitutes each. The text also addresses the status of narrators who commit minor sins, persist in them, or are unknown, including a key inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi‘i on accepting reports from the first generation.

Guided Path
1
Define 'adala linguistically and terminologically
Identify that 'adala linguistically means straightness, like a straight road. Terminologically, it is a quality of uprightness that makes a narrator trustworthy in religious transmission.
The term derives from 'adl ( straightness) and contrasts with ja'ir (deviation).
2
Distinguish between the two degrees: qasir and kamil
Recognize that qasir 'adala is based on apparent Islam and sound intellect but is vulnerable to desire; kamil 'adala is the complete form where religion and intellect preponderate over desire.
Kamil 'adala has no fixed limit; it varies by divine decree.
3
Identify the causes that destroy 'adala
Major sins (kabira) completely destroy 'adala. Persistence (israr) on minor sins also destroys it; a single minor sin without persistence does not.
The text equates persistence on minor sins with major sins in terms of accusation of lying.
4
Apply the ruling to fasiq and mastur
The report of a fasiq (open sinner) or mastur (person of unknown standing) is not accepted because they lack proven complete 'adala.
The absolute term 'adala in the Shari'ah refers to the complete type (kamil).
5
Analyze the Shafi'i dispute and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues by analogy that if a mastur is rejected, a majhul (unknown) is even more deserving of rejection. The Hanafi response is that majhul narrators from the first generation are accepted due to the Prophet's collective testimony to their uprightness.
This shows that the condition of 'adala is not absolute for that generation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما العدالة: فإن تفسيرها الاستقامة يقال للجادة : طريق عَدْلٌ، وجائر للبنيات وهي نوعان أيضاً : قاصر، وكامل. أما القاصر: فما ثبت منه بظاهر الإسلام واعتدال العقل؛ لأن الأصل: حالة الاستقامة، لكن هذا الأصل لا يفارقه هوى يُضلّه، ويَصدُّه عن الاستقامة. وليس لكمال الاستقامة حدٌ يُدرك مداه ؛ لأنها بتقدير الله تعالى ومشيئته تتفاوت، فاعتبر في ذلك ما لا يؤدي إلى الحرج والمشقة، وتضييع حدود الشريعة، وهو رجحان جهة الدين والعقل على طريق الهوى والشهوة. فقيل : مَن ارتكب كبيرةً : سقطت عدالته ، وصار متهماً بالكذب. وإذا أصر على ما دون الكبيرة : كان مثلها في وقوع التهمة، وجرح العدالة. فأما من ابتلي بشيء من غير الكبائر من غير إصرار: فعَدلُ كامل العدالة، وخبره حجة في إقامة الشريعة. والمطلق من العدالة : ينصرف إلى أكمل الوجهين، ولهذا لم يُجعل خبر الفاسق والمستور حجة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لما لم يكن خبر المستور حجة: فخبر المجهول أولى. والجواب أن خبر المجهول من الصدر الأول مقبول عندنا على الشرط الذي قلناه بشهادة النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لذلك القَرْن بالعدالة.
And as for uprightness (adala): its interpretation is straightness. It is said for the main road: a straight ('adl) path, and a deviating (ja'ir) path for side roads. And it is also of two types: deficient (qasir) and complete (kamil). As for the deficient: what is established from it by apparent Islam and soundness of intellect; because the origin is the state of uprightness, but this origin is not separated from a desire that leads him astray and prevents him from uprightness. And for complete uprightness, there is no limit that can be perceived; because it varies by the decree of Allah and His will. So what is considered in that is what does not lead to hardship and difficulty and neglect of the limits of the Shari'ah, which is the preponderance of the side of religion and intellect over the way of desire and lust. So it is said: Whoever commits a major sin (kabira): his uprightness falls, and he becomes accused of lying. And if he persists (israr) in what is less than a major sin, it is like it in begetting accusation and injuring uprightness. As for one who is afflicted with something from other than major sins without persistence: he is completely upright, and his report is a proof in establishing the Shari'ah. And the absolute from uprightness refers to the more complete of the two aspects, and for this reason the report of the fasiq (sinner) and the mastur (concealed) is not made a proof. And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Since the report of the mastur is not a proof, then the report of the majhul (unknown) is even more so. The answer: that the report of the majhul from the first generation is accepted with us on the condition we have mentioned, by the testimony of the Prophet, peace be upon him, for that generation to uprightness.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the condition of 'adala (uprightness) for accepting reports (khabar wahid). The author first defines 'adala as straightness, analogous to a straight road. He then divides 'adala into two types: qasir (deficient) and kamil (complete). Deficient 'adala is established by apparent Islam and sound intellect, but it is susceptible to being overcome by desire. Complete 'adala has no fixed limit; it varies by divine decree, and is measured by the preponderance of religion and intellect over desire. The author then states that committing a major sin (kabira) destroys 'adala entirely, as does persistence (israr) on minor sins. A single minor sin without persistence does not destroy complete 'adala, and such a narrator's report is a hujja. The absolute term 'adala refers to the complete type, so the reports of a fasiq (open sinner) or mastur (person of unknown character) are not accepted. The text then presents a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i: he argues by analogy that if a mastur is not accepted, then a majhul (unknown) is even less acceptable. The Hanafi response is that a majhul from the first generation (الصدر الأول) is accepted due to the Prophet's testimony that generation was characterized by uprightness. This shows that the condition of 'adala is not absolute but can be waived for a group collectively known for integrity.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-'adala): Uprightness; a quality that makes a person trustworthy in religious matters, especially in transmitting reports.
الفاسق (al-fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins; his report is not accepted.
المستور (al-mastur): A person whose reputation is not openly known; his report is not accepted according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on the report of a narrator who persists in minor sins (israr)?
A) It is accepted because minor sins do not affect 'adala.
B) It is rejected, as persistence on minor sins is like a major sin.
C) It is accepted only if the narrator repents.
D) It is accepted only for matters related to worship.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires complete 'adala (kamil) for accepting a narrator's report, but the first generation is an exception due to prophetic testimony.
