Acceptance of Reports from Unknown Narrators of the First Generation
Dispute about whether absolute justice implies complete reliability of narrators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on accepting reports from majhul narrators of the first generation and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Prophet's testimony for the first generation makes even unknown narrators from them trustworthy.

This passage addresses a key usul dispute: can a hadith narrated by a completely unknown (majhul) narrator be accepted? The Hanafi school distinguishes between later narrators and those from the first generation, relying on the Prophet's collective praise. The Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response illustrate how different usul principles lead to different rulings on the same source material.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi premise on absolute 'adala
The term 'adala in its absolute sense means the most complete form. Therefore, reports of a fasiq or mastur are not accepted. This sets the baseline for what is normally required.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues by a fortiori: if the mastur (whose state is unknown but not corrupt) is rejected, then the majhul (completely unknown) should be even more rejected.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response creates an exception: the majhul from the first generation (al-sadr al-awwal) is accepted because the Prophet himself testified to the 'adala of that entire generation via mutawatir reports.
The condition is the prophetic testimony.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence
A hadith from an unknown Companion is accepted in the Hanafi school, but rejected in the Shafi'i school unless his 'adala is individually established. This difference affects many early hadiths.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the dispute).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمطلق من العدالة : ينصرف إلى أكمل الوجهين، ولهذا لم يُجعل خبر الفاسق والمستور حجة. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لما لم يكن خبر المستور حجة: فخبر المجهول أولى. والجواب أن خبر المجهول من الصدر الأول مقبول عندنا على الشرط الذي قلناه بشهادة النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام لذلك القَرْن بالعدالة.
The absolute from justice: refers to the most complete of the two aspects, and for this reason the report of the corrupt and the concealed is not made authoritative. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Since the report of the concealed is not authoritative, then the report of the unknown is more deserving of rejection. The answer is that the report of the unknown from the first generation is acceptable according to us on the condition we stated, due to the Prophet's, peace be upon him, testimony for that century with justice.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the acceptance of reports from narrators whose 'adala (justice/trustworthiness) is not explicitly known. The text begins by stating that when the term 'adala is used in an absolute sense (mutlaq), it is taken to mean the most complete form of justice. Therefore, the report of a fasiq (open sinner) or a mastur (hidden state, i.e., a narrator whose 'adala is not known but no corruption is known) is not accepted as proof. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since the report of the mastur is not authoritative, then the report of the majhul (completely unknown) is even more deserving of rejection. The Hanafi response is that the report of a majhul narrator from the first generation (al-sadr al-awwal, the Companions and early Followers) is acceptable, provided the condition that the Prophet, peace be upon him, testified to the 'adala of that entire generation. Thus, the absolute 'adala of the early Muslims is presumed, and their reports are accepted without further scrutiny of individual trustworthiness. This is based on the famous hadith: 'The best of you is my generation…' which establishes that generation's justice.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-ʿadālah): Absolute justice/trustworthiness; in this context, the most complete form of moral integrity required for acceptance of testimony and narration.
المستور (al-mastūr): A narrator whose external state is hidden (neither known for corruption nor known for ʿadālah).
المجهول (al-majhūl): A narrator completely unknown in terms of ʿadālah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the report of a majhul (unknown) narrator from the first generation acceptable?
A) Because all individuals in that generation are equally known for piety.
B) Because the Prophet testified to the ʿadālah of that entire generation.
C) Because the Hanafi school does not require ʿadālah in narrators.
D) Because mastur narrators are also accepted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the collective 'adala of the first generation, established by prophetic testimony, overrides individual unknown status, making reports from unknown Companions acceptable.
